"modified": "2015-09-19T02:14:29", "date_gmt": "2014-02-14T02:13:02", "_links": {"wp:term": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/categories?post=206", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "category"}, {"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/tags?post=206", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "post_tag"}], "curies": [{"href": "https://api.w.org/{rel}", "name": "wp", "templated": true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/206"}], "version-history": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/206/revisions"}], "collection": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts"}], "wp:featuredmedia": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media/207", "embeddable": true}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=206", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/users/1", "embeddable": true}], "wp:attachment": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media?parent=206"}], "about": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/types/post"}]}, "excerpt": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>Not much to put forth for an introduction here. \u00a0This is an article examining the connection between black Americans and Afro-Latinos. \u00a0A good read, especially for Black History Month. Interesting point raised in the article: Brazil has the highest black population in the world today outside of Africa, with the United States coming in third. [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [71, 66, 73, 22], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=206"}, "id": 206, "title": {"rendered": "Repost: Black Americans and Afro-Latinos A Common History"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-19T02:14:29", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "repost-black-americans-and-afro-latinos-a-common-history", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 203, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/black-history-month-2014-american-slavery-the-early-days/", "date": "2014-02-04T02:09:02", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<figure style=\"width: 400px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-GI4JuUWcu6Q/UvCdfg6KWRI/AAAAAAAAAmM/3-pe9BWfvvg/s1600/sugarplantation.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"400\" height=\"228\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Illustration of plantation slavery in the Canary Islands</figcaption></figure>\n<div class=\"\">\n<p>We&#8217;ve <a href=\"http://rationalwhimsy.com/black-history-month-2014-the-anatomy-of-a-slave-ship/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">looked at the slave ships</a> that brought Africans to the New World, but what were they brought here for? In order to begin to answer this question, I put on my &#8220;I Can Learn Anything with Google&#8221; hat and look briefly at what necessitated American slavery. The focus here is slavery in the U.S. and the colonies that would be come the U.S., <a href=\"http://www.slavevoyages.org/tast/assessment/estimates.faces\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">where an estimated 253,000 slaves were shipped</a>. \u00a0Seeing as how American slavery (1619 &#8211; 1865) existed for longer than our nation has actually been a nation (246 years vs. 238 years), I&#8217;m going to do this in parts. \u00a0Let&#8217;s skip back to the early 1600s to examine Slavery &#8211; The Early Days. \u00a0Spoiler Alert: native Americans get hit first, and the life of an African was very, very cheap.</p>\n</div>\n<p class=\"separator\"><i>Note: My apologies to anyone that I may offend with my smart assery and occasional silliness. \u00a0This whole topic is a pot full of painful stuff and humor is how I cope. If you&#8217;re still reading, bear with me.</i><!--more--></p>\n<p class=\"separator\">The first permanent colony of what would become the United States was Jamestown, VA (British-owned), whose chief export was tobacco. \u00a0The great climate and demand for growing tobacco necessitated cheap labor, and options were limited: indentured British servants, native American slaves, and African slaves.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">Indentured servants were introduced by the Virginia Company to colonial America in 1619. \u00a0They were a combination of willing migrants, the religiously persecuted, criminals, and other undesirables. \u00a0In exchange for food, clothing, lodging, and a trip to the colonies, they worked for a fixed term (4-10 years) for no wages. \u00a0At the end, they&#8217;d be free to look for new jobs and a life in the colonies. They would also receive &#8220;freedom dues&#8221;, with some contracts including at least 25 acres of land, a year&#8217;s worth of corn, arms (&#8216;Murica), a cow, and new clothes (<a href=\"http://www.pbs.org/opb/historydetectives/feature/indentured-servants-in-the-us/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">source</a>). There were even some blacks treated as indentured servants and given the same opportunities for freedom dues as whites. \u00a0This, however, didn&#8217;t work out in the long term (clearly). Why pay all that money for someone only\u00a0to\u00a0lose them in the end? Cut costs! Get workers that have no opportunity for freedom. You pay for them once, and never again. \u00a0Get slaves.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 300px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-GQ5OoJKeNBw/UvCo-AC4tEI/AAAAAAAAAmw/7fNDdDarFG8/s1600/300px-Native_American_slaves.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"211\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Native Americans enslaved by Spaniards, 1596</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Different versions of slavery were present in the Americas before Europeans took it over (hell, it was present in Africa before Europe caught on, but we&#8217;re focusing on the U.S. of A). \u00a0Natives would enslave captives of war who they would use for small scale labor and ritual sacrifice. \u00a0The rights and privileges of these slaves varied widely between tribes. \u00a0Some were even able to marry widows. This all changed when the British began to colonize. \u00a0Being high on product and short on labor, British colonies were more than willing to buy the slaves from the local tribes. \u00a0Then they began instigate conflicts between tribes for more war slaves, and eventually stole from the tribes directly. \u00a0As an example, it&#8217;s estimated that between 30,000 to 50,000 natives were shipped out of Charleston, SC alone to the Caribbean between 1670 and 1715. I&#8217;d provide more numbers in this bit, but the records are spotty at best.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">The enslavement of natives didn&#8217;t work out so well for the fledgeling colonies. \u00a0Don&#8217;t get me wrong here, it still happened. \u00a0Huge swaths of native American communities were devastated by the capture and sale of their people throughout the history of American slavery. \u00a0Many were traded to work in West Indian sugarcane plantations when the sugar market boomed. \u00a0However, the enslavement of natives proved costly in money and lives. Although several tribes were complicit in the enslavement of rival tribes, toward the mid 1700&#8217;s they began to band together to resist their enslavement. \u00a0Also, as time went on from the 1600s to the 1700s, African slaves became more readily available.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><img src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-xe4yg1UVURo/UvCn7FtWY0I/AAAAAAAAAmk/utjUrpQjmXA/s1600/slaveauction2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"194\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">A sample slave auction; Richmond, VA</figcaption></figure>\n<p>While the first sets of Africans were brought to Virginia in 1619, the first sets of African <b><i>slaves</i></b> were brought into present-day New York City (NYC represent!) in 1625 by the Dutch West India Company. Although enslaved, Africans had a few basic rights and families were preserved. Their children could be baptized, they could testify in court, sign legal documents, and even *gasp* bring civil actions against whites. \u00a0Some were permitted to work after hours, earning wages equal to those paid to white workers.</p>\n<div class=\"\">\n<p>In 1662, Virginia decreed that children born in VA &#8220;shall be bond or free according to the condition of the mother&#8221;, thereby allowing plantation owners the right to enslave their illegitimate mixed-race children, removing their responsibility to acknowledge, support, or emancipate these children. \u00a0Along with that, &#8220;free&#8221; white women would be penalized for sex with slaves by serving that slave&#8217;s master for life, preserving the property rights of slaveowners. By 1664, the colonies all passed laws mandating lifelong servitude for all black slaves. \u00a0During the late 1600s, British indentured servitude declined, and planters became increasingly concerned about creating a large class of restless, landless, poor white men (former indentured servants). Wealthy VA and MD planters bought slaves in preference to indentured servants, and eventually poorer planters followed suit. \u00a0By the end of the 1600s, a planter could buy an African slave for life for the same price that he could purchase a white indentured servant for 10 years.</p>\n<p>Consider the economic choice between a white indentured servant with a term of 4 years and a slave. Figures here will be an irresponsible combo of <a href=\"http://www.virtualjamestown.org/documents1.html\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">these indentured servant contracts</a>. \u00a0Let&#8217;s take young William Buckland&#8217;s 1755 salary of \u00a320 sterling per year for 4 years (80 pounds total) and <a href=\"http://www.measuringworth.com/ppoweruk/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">scale that back to the 1627 economy</a>. \u00a0That&#8217;s an average \u00a313.7 per year in 1627, totaling \u00a354.8. \u00a0For reference, \u00a354.8 pounds in the 1627 economy scales up to \u00a3135,000 in 2012, or about $220,000 American. \u00a0At roughly $55,000 per year, PLUS food, housing, clothes, and job prospects at the end if their terms, they&#8217;re looking like a mighty better deal than an astronomy grad student. \u00a0But I digress. \u00a0Atop the \u00a354.8 salary, housing, food, and clothes for 4 years, there&#8217;s the cost of the voyage (\u00a35, about $20,000 today), and the freedom dues of 25 acres of land, a year&#8217;s worth of corn, arms (&#8216;Murica), and a cow. If we devalue all the freedom dues, a 4 year servant still cost roughly $250,000 in today&#8217;s dollars.</p>\n<p>Contrast that with the average slave cost of \u00a320 in the 1600s (very rough estimate based on <a href=\"http://discoveringbristol.org.uk/slavery/routes/from-africa-to-america/tradeing-africa/value-of-trade/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">this</a>). Let&#8217;s assume that slaves came in at about&#8230;24 years of age, and lived to the average life colonial life expectancy of 44 \u2013 that&#8217;s 20 years of service. \u00a0So, for the total cost of an indentured servant, you could buy roughly 3 slaves that would work <i>FOR LIFE</i>. \u00a0In addition, you are guaranteed ownership of their offspring. \u00a0If each slave had only one kid, you then had 3 new slaves for 40 years. \u00a0Considering only two generations in this model, the price of one indentured servant (\u00a360) got you 6 slaves and a combined 180 years of service. Your costs reduce from \u00a315 per year to ~\u00a30.3 per year; a 98% reduction of cost. Slavery: the ultimate capitalist model.</p>\n</div>\n<p class=\"separator\">In 1676 Bacon&#8217;s Rebellion hit Virginia like a molotov cocktail, in that the capital was bathed in fire and literally burned to the ground. Discontented frontiersmen and frequent attacks from natives caused the white underclass to ally with Africans against bond-servitude and revolt, demanding the colonial government seize native American land for distribution, amongst other things. They held the rebellion for 8 months before the British royal army suppressed it. This unity amongst the underclass alarmed the ruling class, and in response racial lines drawn by slavery were brought to the fore and solidified into law and common rhetoric.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">From here it turns darker for a while. \u00a0But there&#8217;s sunshine on the horizon. \u00a0Have to first remember the struggle before we celebrate the triumphs. \u00a0Cheers.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">References:</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/202"}], "version-history": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/202/revisions"}], "collection": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts"}], "wp:featuredmedia": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media/203", "embeddable": true}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=202", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/users/1", "embeddable": true}], "wp:attachment": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media?parent=202"}], "about": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/types/post"}]}, "excerpt": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>We&#8217;ve looked at the slave ships that brought Africans to the New World, but what were they brought here for? In order to begin to answer this question, I put on my &#8220;I Can Learn Anything with Google&#8221; hat and look briefly at what necessitated American slavery. The focus here is slavery in the U.S. [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [71, 66, 72], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=202"}, "id": 202, "title": {"rendered": "Black History Month 2014: American Slavery &#8211; The Early Days"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-19T02:12:41", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "black-history-month-2014-american-slavery-the-early-days", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 200, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/black-history-month-2014-the-anatomy-of-a-slave-ship/", "date": "2014-02-03T02:04:17", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<figure style=\"width: 400px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-EDdkFZVZm2M/UvARBnZo87I/AAAAAAAAAlM/qtzHORM3Ebc/s1600/slaveship1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"400\" height=\"123\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Horizontal cross section of a slave ship. \u00a0Slaves stacked up against one another like boxes \u00a0or cattle. \u00a0The notion of the slave as property starts here and reverberates throughout the history of the American negro.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Slavery was a horrid and sad era in American history. \u00a0Even though it&#8217;s an ugly and depressing thing to dwell on, appreciation for what our people have become today starts with the recognition of what got us here. \u00a0So, we start with what literally got us here: the Slave Ship.<!--more--></p>\n<p>The typical slave ship was a cargo vessel outfitted to carry slaves from the Eastern Hemisphere over to the New World. \u00a0An example of this is the frigate Duc du Maine, which brought the first African slaves from Senegambia (confederation of Senegal and Gambia) to Louisiana in 1797. \u00a0At 101.7 feet long and 29.9 feet wide (at its widest point), it could carry 500-600 slaves per voyage. \u00a0Its destinations were typically around the Gulf Coast and the Caribbean.</p>\n<div></div>\n<div>\n<p>Let&#8217;s do some math here to get a sense of the types of conditions we&#8217;re talking about. Remember as you read what follows that this is an approximation, where our slave ship is a paper-thin box. \u00a0Consider the average adult to be 5.7 feet tall and 1.6 feet wide, and stack them as tightly as you can in a paper-thin box that&#8217;s 101.7 feet long and 29.9 feet wide. That&#8217;s fitting 63 people (since you can&#8217;t have fractions of a person) along its length laying shoulder-to-shoulder in 5 rows (feet flush against heads) from end to end. \u00a0That&#8217;s <b>315 people per deck</b>. \u00a0Average frigate-class ships from this era had two full decks. \u00a0Two levels of slaves would <b>total roughly 630 men, women, and children</b>, each with mere centimeters of &#8220;wiggle room&#8221;. \u00a0Keep in mind, this is envisioning a slave ship as a paper-thin box of those exact measurements. \u00a0Adding in the thickness of the wood between the slaves and the water, the front of the ship tapering into a point (see first image), and space for things like stairs make this all the more horrifying.</p>\n<div></div>\n<div>\n<p>Slaves were gathered from the coasts of western Africa, and packed in like boxes of wine. \u00a0Conditions aboard the slave ships were, to put it lightly, inhumane. \u00a0Men, women, and children were crammed into every available nook, denied adequate room, food, or breathing space. \u00a0There was little regard for the need for food, water, or sanitation. One account of a captured vessel&#8217;s &#8220;cargo&#8221; counts 562 slaves, 55 of which had been thrown overboard. \u00a0Another has slaves numbering in the 800&#8217;s for a vessel regulated for 350.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><img src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-oN4S2w8n4Fk/UvAV7iq6fvI/AAAAAAAAAlc/f1C3jonigpU/s1600/slaveship2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"122\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Vertical cross-section of typical slave ships</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Voyages along the middle passage could last from one to three months, during which time many of the enslaved would die from disease, suicide (jumping overboard or other means), malnourishment, and just plain violence.</p>\n<p>Over 35,000 voyages were made to transport slaves to the Americas. \u00a0If you consider an arbitrary figure of 400 slaves taken per voyage, that results in at about 14 million slaves legally transported to the Americas between 1527 and 1808 (when the abolition of the international slave trade took effect in the United States; legal domestic slavery lasted until 1865 with the 13th amendment). \u00a0It&#8217;s actually estimated that the number is closer to 20 million slaves. \u00a0Bringing our average up to roughly 570 slaves per voyage. \u00a0The mortality rate for the voyage alone was about 15%, making the trip to the western hemisphere responsible for a genocide of Africans closing in on numbers put up by the Holocaust.</p>\n<p>Cheers, everyone.</p>\n<p>References:</p>\n<p><a href=\"http://www.eyewitnesstohistory.com/slaveship.htm\">http://www.eyewitnesstohistory.com/slaveship.htm<br />\n</a><a href=\"http://www.inmotionaame.org/migrations/topic.cfm?migration=1&amp;topic=5\">http://www.inmotionaame.org/migrations/topic.cfm?migration=1&amp;topic=5<br />\n</a><a href=\"http://theslaveship.clevelandhistory.org/the-ship-2/\">http://theslaveship.clevelandhistory.org/the-ship-2/<br />\n</a><a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slave_ship\">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slave_ship<br />\n</a><a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duc_du_Maine_(slave_ship)\">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duc_du_Maine_(slave_ship)<br />\n</a><a />\n</a><a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Passage\">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Passage</a></p>\n</div>\n</div>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-19T02:08:07", "date_gmt": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/long-term-investing-how-much-growth-is-there-really/", "date": "2014-02-01T02:01:08", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-uBJtmvdyfm0/Uu0Wgq2j_sI/AAAAAAAAAko/NOiARXPIIZE/s1600/invest-2.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-uBJtmvdyfm0/Uu0Wgq2j_sI/AAAAAAAAAko/NOiARXPIIZE/s1600/invest-2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"213\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>This is going to be one of my shorter posts&#8230;</p>\n<p>I&#8217;ve been really interested in money lately. \u00a0Namely, how to keep it from flowing forth from my pockets, and even how to make it grow on its own. \u00a0This, along with discussions of money amongst other grad students in my department, led me to create a PowerPoint presentation (available after next month) giving a basic overview of things like budgeting, debt, and investing.<!--more--></p>\n<p>Now, when talking about investing with those that have invested, I&#8217;ve tended to have the feeling of it being this mystical world where money goes in and dice are rolled. If they land face-up on your number, then you&#8217;re lucky and you get something back. Otherwise, your funds are in the abyss. I didn&#8217;t quite see how it all translated to growth over time. However, I was vaguely aware that some math was involved, and I happen to do math every single day. So, I wrote a quick Python script to calculate how money can grow over time. \u00a0It resulted in the plot you see below.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 568px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-wU5gZeGPOqE/Uu0X5I2sN6I/AAAAAAAAAkw/3BiywEcpERI/s1600/ira_interest.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"568\" height=\"640\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">This is essentially what I do every day, just for Astronomy</figcaption></figure>\n<p>With $0 principal investment and a contribution of $100 per month over 40 years, you can do fairly well (depending on your rate of growth). \u00a0Even though over those 40 years you only contribute $48K, your money more than doubles! That&#8217;s insane!</p>\n<p>Now, it&#8217;s not good enough to just hard code in some values and produce a plot. At least, not if you want people to want to use what you create. So, with that in mind, and wanting some practice using the iPython Notebook, I wrote an adjustable script so that you can see how your investment can grow with any (consistent) monthly contribution, any principal contribution, any interest rate, and any length of time. And anyone (that&#8217;s familiar with Python) can use it! Unfortunately, I don&#8217;t know Java (yet), so this is what you get. \u00a0Still, it&#8217;s something.</p>\n<p>If you want to just see what the iPython Notebook looks like, <a href=\"http://nbviewer.ipython.org/github/nhuntwalker/mystuff/blob/master/blog/interestPost/interestCalc.ipynb?create=1\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">go here</a>.</p>\n<p>If you want to actually use the Notebook I wrote, get your own copy <a href=\"https://github.com/nhuntwalker/mystuff/blob/master/blog/interestPost/interestCalc.ipynb\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">from here</a>.</p>\n<p>Comments are always welcome. \u00a0Cheers!</p>\n<p><i>Note: I use the compound interest formula, and the default is a monthly compounding.</i></p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-19T02:03:59", "date_gmt": "2014-02-01T02:01:08", "_links": {"wp:term": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/categories?post=194", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "category"}, {"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/tags?post=194", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "post_tag"}], "curies": [{"href": "https://api.w.org/{rel}", "name": "wp", "templated": true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/194"}], "version-history": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/194/revisions"}], "collection": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts"}], "wp:featuredmedia": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media/195", "embeddable": true}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=194", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/users/1", "embeddable": true}], "wp:attachment": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media?parent=194"}], "about": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/types/post"}]}, "excerpt": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>This is going to be one of my shorter posts&#8230; I&#8217;ve been really interested in money lately. \u00a0Namely, how to keep it from flowing forth from my pockets, and even how to make it grow on its own. \u00a0This, along with discussions of money amongst other grad students in my department, led me to create [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [8, 35, 69, 10, 70], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=194"}, "id": 194, "title": {"rendered": "Long-Term Investing: How Much Growth is There, Really?"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-19T02:03:59", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "long-term-investing-how-much-growth-is-there-really", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 192, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/defining-black-pride-for-self/", "date": "2013-09-06T01:57:36", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p><a href=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/blackpride.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-192\" src=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/blackpride.jpg?resize=213%2C320\" alt=\"blackpride\" srcset=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/blackpride.jpg?w=213 213w, http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/blackpride.jpg?resize=200%2C300 200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 213px) 100vw, 213px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p>I began thinking about this in earnest yesterday, after several discussions (see: Facebook) on race and race politics in America. \u00a0The seed for this was planted in my mind after reading <a href=\"http://alineinthesand.com/i-hate-myself-what-are-respectability-politics-and-why-do-black-people-subscribe-to-them/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">this spectacular article</a> written by my friend Mo the Educator regarding race politics and &#8220;proper blackness&#8221;. \u00a0After reading this article and leaving my comments on it, I began thinking: What does it mean to me to be a Black American and to have Black Pride? I ask these questions and, in what follows, hope that I have found the beginnings of an answer. \u00a0As always, please chime in on the comments (or contact me by other means) if you have an opinion. \u00a0Twenty-seven years of life as a Black American doesn&#8217;t qualify me as some supreme expert on the subject, and I welcome all feedback; anything that makes me think is worth considering.</p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<div>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-nhYpMJU1wDY/UioQS13g1eI/AAAAAAAAAgA/5-Dj3P8manY/s1600/whoami.jpg\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-nhYpMJU1wDY/UioQS13g1eI/AAAAAAAAAgA/5-Dj3P8manY/s320/whoami.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"320\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>Starting broadly, I think that being a Black American means that your ancestry is traceable back to any one of the millions of slaves that inhabited this country. Whether you can actually trace it back yourself is irrelevant. Whether your skin color shows your heritage or not is also irrelevant, though it does make it harder for you to assert your &#8220;blackness&#8221; where applicable. \u00a0If you share blood with one of those that was enslaved here in the United States, you&#8217;re a Black American. \u00a0That means, to me, that Black Canadians, Caribbeans, Central Americans, and South Americans that come to the United States are not Black Americans. They&#8217;re still Black, as they share that same slave descent, but they&#8217;re not Black Americans. That also means that, again to me, Africans (immigrant and otherwise) are not Black\u2014 they&#8217;re African (and since Africa is <b>not </b>a country, they&#8217;re Nigerian, Ethiopian, Egyptian, Moroccan, Senegalese, etc). \u00a0 This is not to say that being a Black American is any better (or worse) than being Black Dominican, Black Brazilian, or Congolese; it&#8217;s simply just not the same category.</p>\n</div>\n<div></div>\n<div>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-lz1tmqMjtpE/UioOOly_LuI/AAAAAAAAAfg/rEIiuqrOS_U/s1600/Slave_Auction_Ad.jpg\"><img class=\"alignright\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-lz1tmqMjtpE/UioOOly_LuI/AAAAAAAAAfg/rEIiuqrOS_U/s320/Slave_Auction_Ad.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"218\" height=\"320\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>That said, I think that the essence of &#8220;Blackness&#8221;, whether you&#8217;re in America or not, lies in that shared history of pain coming from slavery. \u00a0That&#8217;s the common thread that binds all of us lost children in the Western Hemisphere. \u00a0We&#8217;re lost because much of our history has been scrambled and/or lost by the slave trade, so much so that we might as well have sprouted randomly from American soil. \u00a0Our ancestors lost their music, their gods, their dances, their food, their names\u2014their identities were lost in the beatings, the killings, and the suicides that characterized those difficult times. \u00a0In this oppressive alien land, Blacks as a people have had to reboot their culture from the ground up. \u00a0Thus, when I think on Black Pride and try to define it in my own mind, this is where I start. \u00a0I hesitate to use &#8220;African American&#8221;, for these very reasons. \u00a0Yes, we&#8217;re of African descent and we never can nor should we ever deny that. \u00a0However, we&#8217;re so disconnected from that root that to call ourselves African-Americans similar to the way in which others refer to themselves as Chinese-Americans, Indian-Americans, and Norwegian-Americans is disingenuous, as it pertains to our actual connection to anything in Africa. \u00a0There is no &#8220;old country&#8221; for us. \u00a0Our pre-slavery history is black as our skin (ooh wee, that was clever! Wasn&#8217;t that clever? \u00a0I thought that was clever.).</p>\n</div>\n<div></div>\n<div>\n<p>Black Pride means first acknowledging and owning that slave ancestry, and very simply being proud that you managed to come out of that. It means remembering their struggle and honoring the values that they fought for. It means keeping in mind that, above all else, our forebears bled, suffered, and died for <b>the opportunity to choose who we wanted to be</b>, and be acknowledged as human. It means honoring our skin color, our typical common tracer (though not always obvious, as my own grandmother could&#8217;ve passed for a tanned white lady), and the rainbow of shades in which we can appear.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-iMjrhWEbas8/UioO_xhvBtI/AAAAAAAAAf0/W_4pu7eEMok/s1600/hairstyles.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-iMjrhWEbas8/UioO_xhvBtI/AAAAAAAAAf0/W_4pu7eEMok/s400/hairstyles.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"400\" height=\"282\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>It means being proud of our hair in its natural state, in the bouquet of different curls in which it can come. It also means knowing and acknowledging with honesty the historical roots of hairstyles like relaxed hair, weaves, and extensions. The reason for a style is as important as, if not more than, the style itself. If you relax or otherwise disguise/alter the nature of your hair, know that women and men use to do it because our hair was thought of as disgusting and deplorable in its natural state. Know that women and men burned themselves with lye and hot combs in order to get hair that looked &#8220;white&#8221;. Know that &#8220;goodness&#8221; of one&#8217;s hair is still a raw wound amongst people of color. \u00a0And if you&#8217;re on the flip side of that and are judging those with hair appearing different than yours, cut that nonsense and know that everyone has different preferences and may not be the &#8220;lost child&#8221; that you think they are. \u00a0Check yourself accordingly, then move on with your life knowing that the style you choose is the style YOU choose that makes you happy, and not the product of any residual self hate or a misguided need to rebel.</p>\n</div>\n<div></div>\n<div>\n<p><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1xJWSRei59s/UioRDZa1BeI/AAAAAAAAAgM/2WGQ9zHv6zQ/s1600/dance.jpg\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-1xJWSRei59s/UioRDZa1BeI/AAAAAAAAAgM/2WGQ9zHv6zQ/s320/dance.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"209\" border=\"0\" /></a>It means honoring others like us that share our history and working to bring them up in ways that respect their individual struggles, as they&#8217;re the descendants of our own ancestors&#8217; partners in struggle. It means honoring the music our people make, the steps that our people take when they dance, and calling out either one when they dishonor us. It also means honoring the fact that we are of African origin, and paying homage to the cultures that have sprouted up and lived there over time, though I caution against generic African reverence because it carries a similar ignorance of the individual peoples of Africa that is shared by those that have oppressed those people.</p>\n<p>Black pride means honoring our food and cooking styles, while taking strides to find healthier alternatives to classic &#8220;soul food&#8221; which will annihilate your body over time. \u00a0It means honoring our bodies and all of the different ways in which they can appear. \u00a0Because of centuries of selective breeding, convolved with basic characteristics of our African ancestry and some mixture of native American and European (from both legitimate and illegitimate relationships), our body types follow certain trends. \u00a0Honor your musculature, your curves, and your other physical characteristics, but also honor your health. \u00a0Don&#8217;t write off poor (or nonexistent) eating and exercise habits. \u00a0There&#8217;s a big difference between a genetic big butt and a McDonald&#8217;s big butt. \u00a0Own it.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 150px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/--gbCZEMDqbM/UioSBEMNi3I/AAAAAAAAAgU/WVuN6iAKy3E/s200/Black_Jesus_2990.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"150\" height=\"200\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Bet you didn&#8217;t know Black Jesus had dreads! Haha!</figcaption></figure>\n<p>It means honoring Black religious practices, whether you believe or don&#8217;t (like myself). That in particular means not only revering your Muhammad or Black Jesus, but respecting practitioners of Vodou, Candombl\u00e9, Santeria, and other religions that have sprouted from Black mouths and minds, as well as respecting those who have chosen not to subscribe to a religion. You don&#8217;t have to believe the way that someone else does to pay respect.</p>\n<p>It also means honoring the style with which we speak, and not denigrating the slang that comes out of our neighborhoods just because it&#8217;s different from the &#8220;proper English&#8221; that we&#8217;ve all learned. It&#8217;s its own English dialect and should be viewed as such, and not looked down upon simply because it has grown out of the ghettos. It should also be allowed to be analyzed and critiqued like any other dialect, especially when parts of it put prison, pimp, and drug culture on a pedestal. The same goes for our fashion.</p>\n<p>To me, Black Pride means all of these things and more, much of which I&#8217;m still fleshing out for myself. At the last, Black Pride means honoring yourself because you are who you are, and not dishonoring other cultures because they&#8217;re different, or because individuals in those cultures resemble (and let&#8217;s face it, sometimes actively emulate) those that once beat, raped, swindled, and lynched our ancestors. Acknowledge the pain, the anger, and the resentment, but don&#8217;t transfer it to those who exist today. Unless they deserve it.</p>\n</div>\n<div></div>\n<div>\n<div data-blogger-escaped-style=\"-webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; color: black; font-family: Times; font-size: medium; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; line-height: normal; orphans: auto; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: auto; word-spacing: 0px;\"></div>\n<div data-blogger-escaped-style=\"-webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; color: black; font-family: Times; font-size: medium; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; line-height: normal; margin: 0px; orphans: auto; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: auto; word-spacing: 0px;\">\n<p><i>I apologize in advance if I rambled a little. I just like to define my terms for clarity before starting a discussion of this type. Blame my desire to write in my speaking voice and my speech training as an astronomer.\u00a0</i></p>\n</div>\n</div>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-19T02:00:48", "date_gmt": "2013-09-06T01:57:36", "_links": {"wp:term": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/categories?post=191", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "category"}, {"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/tags?post=191", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "post_tag"}], "curies": [{"href": "https://api.w.org/{rel}", "name": "wp", "templated": true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/191"}], "version-history": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/191/revisions"}], "collection": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts"}], "wp:featuredmedia": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media/192", "embeddable": true}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=191", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/users/1", "embeddable": true}], "wp:attachment": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media?parent=191"}], "about": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/types/post"}]}, "excerpt": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>I began thinking about this in earnest yesterday, after several discussions (see: Facebook) on race and race politics in America. \u00a0The seed for this was planted in my mind after reading this spectacular article written by my friend Mo the Educator regarding race politics and &#8220;proper blackness&#8221;. \u00a0After reading this article and leaving my comments [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [66, 46, 67, 32, 68, 57], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=191"}, "id": 191, "title": {"rendered": "Defining Black Pride for Self"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-19T02:00:48", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "defining-black-pride-for-self", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 189, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/orishas-oxum/", "date": "2013-08-28T01:49:17", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Rfsv1UoOCX8/UhoOGwJvz2I/AAAAAAAAAbo/lS5z0T2hmiI/s1600/oxumart1.jpg\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Rfsv1UoOCX8/UhoOGwJvz2I/AAAAAAAAAbo/lS5z0T2hmiI/s400/oxumart1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"263\" height=\"400\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>This is my second post about the orix\u00e1s of Candombl\u00e9. \u00a0This time, we&#8217;ll chat about the Orix\u00e1 of freshwater, love, beauty, wealth, and other such things: Oxum (Oshun, Ochun; pronounced &#8220;oh-SHOON&#8221; regardless of spelling). \u00a0A bit of disclaimer before we begin (and this will be at the end as well): I am by no means an expert on Orix\u00e1s of any religion, be it Candombl\u00e9, Umbanda, Yoruba, Santeria, Vodou, or anything else. \u00a0I&#8217;m just a dude with a lot of curiosity and the power of the internet. \u00a0As such, if you see something here that seems kinda fishy, take it with a huge grain of salt. \u00a0And if you know more about the subject matter here, please please PLEASE speak up and point me in the right direction. \u00a0I also didn&#8217;t do references like I did last time, as this was much more of a synthesis of ideas instead of a line-by-line pasting (except where mentioned).</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><!--more--></p>\n<div>\n<div></div>\n<div></div>\n<div>\n<figure style=\"width: 173px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-TDgDjkIEWHQ/UhobkekPYUI/AAAAAAAAAcU/CUms3KJYrgI/s200/oxumart4.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"173\" height=\"200\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Oxum underneath a waterfall, on the shores of a river</figcaption></figure>\n<p>As with the other orix\u00e1 in Candombl\u00e9, Oxum doesn&#8217;t simply have one association. \u00a0To begin with, there&#8217;s always the association with nature\u2014Oxum rules over fresh water (<i>as \u00e1guas doces</i>). \u00a0This includes rivers, lakes, waterfalls, and streams; all water that springs from the earth and has yet to reach\u00a0the ocean, the realm of <a href=\"http://rationalwhimsy.com/orishas-yemanja/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Yemanj\u00e1</a>.</p>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p class=\"separator\">\nAs the rivers do for the people that use them, Oxum nurtures and purifies. \u00a0She provides food by way of the fish that swim with her, clean drinkable water for the thirsty, the source for growth via the irrigation of nearby plants, and waters within which you can cleanse yourself. \u00a0As such, she&#8217;s also associated with maternity, fertility, femininity, vitality, and purification/healing.<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Yyo-_zVcnHs/UhoUFJis4xI/AAAAAAAAAb4/gJfICncniRc/s1600/oxumart2.jpg\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Yyo-_zVcnHs/UhoUFJis4xI/AAAAAAAAAb4/gJfICncniRc/s320/oxumart2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"256\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>Expanding more into the feminine qualities, she, like <a href=\"http://rationalwhimsy.com/orishas-yemanja/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Yemanj\u00e1</a> and other female orix\u00e1s, represents not the entirety of the feminine psyche, but specific parts. \u00a0Her demeanor is loving, caring, nurturing, and seldom ever angry. \u00a0She is the sweetness in sweet women; the very personification of the &#8220;sweet princess&#8221; concept. \u00a0At times, she is even somewhat coquettish, and there are many stories about her seduction of several of the male orix\u00e1s. However, while sweet, she is not eternally docile. \u00a0Like the rivers in a violent storm, when she loses her temper, she can be widely and indiscriminately destructive. \u00a0By no means is she na\u00efve; her wisdom and counsel often being sought by men and women.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-lKAo1Wj83NE/UhoZWXNjvFI/AAAAAAAAAcM/YAegK7f6D3U/s1600/oxumart3.jpg\"><img class=\"alignright\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-lKAo1Wj83NE/UhoZWXNjvFI/AAAAAAAAAcM/YAegK7f6D3U/s320/oxumart3.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"226\" height=\"320\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>She is also, in a word, beautiful. \u00a0Now, typically the female orix\u00e1s are all described as beautiful, so to simply describe her as such does her no justice. \u00a0She is not just beautiful; she is beauty. \u00a0Because beauty is her quality, she&#8217;s often depicted holding a mirror (the symbolic item of beauty), and in provocative clothing (if there&#8217;s any clothing at all). \u00a0In the same way that she is beauty personified, she embodies female sexuality. \u00a0As such, children of Oxum (women AND men that Oxum chooses to share her spirit with; &#8220;possess&#8221; only describes half of the process) are to be stunningly beautiful and are always the subject of attraction. \u00a0Though beautiful, they are by no means dumb; I cannot stress this enough. \u00a0They appreciate luxury and sex, they are vain, elegant, sensuous, and like changes, at times resulting in infidelity. \u00a0But, they are calm, tranquil, emotional, and cry easily. \u00a0They are smart, managing to get everything they want through imagination and plot. \u00a0Though complacent and prodigal, they can be self-seeking, lazy, and hesitant. \u00a0They are very suspicious, and have a great intuition which is often put to work for artfulness (plagiarized mostly from <a href=\"http://tranceform.org/index.php?option=com_content&amp;view=article&amp;id=40%3Acandomble-a-psychological-types&amp;catid=20%3Amember-article&amp;Itemid=89&amp;lang=en\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">here</a>). \u00a0Oxum&#8217;s children also favor bright colors, music, dance, and excitement.</p>\n<p>Her dominion over fertility should not go without mention. \u00a0As the orix\u00e1 of fertility, she protects all pregnancies. \u00a0Interestingly enough, while she herself loves to become pregnant, she is not inclined to raise her children, having a tendency to pawn them off to her siblings (terrible!). \u00a0But yeah, as much as women in Brazil may pray to Oxum to find their luck in love, they will also look to her for protection in their pregnancy.</p>\n<p>Oxum is one of the children of Oxal\u00e1 (the male orix\u00e1 of purity, light, and creation) and, as one might expect, Yemanj\u00e1 (the &#8220;All-Mother&#8221; if you will, and orix\u00e1 of the oceans), and the most loved of those children. \u00a0She was at a time one of the wives of Xango (warrior orix\u00e1 of fire, thunder, justice, and male power/sexuality), taking him from his original wife Ians\u00e1 (orix\u00e1 of winds, hurricanes, change, and gates of the underworld), but as is her nature, she floated in and out of that relationship, has been a lover of Ogun (<span style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">warrior orix\u00e1 of iron, war, labour, sacrifice</span>), Orunmil\u00e1 (orix\u00e1 of wisdom, knowledge, and divination), and seducer of Exu (orix\u00e1 of many things, not least of which are trickery and messages between orix\u00e1 and man). \u00a0<a href=\"http://www.juntosnocandomble.com.br/2008/11/oxum.html\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">One myth I&#8217;ve found</a> (and likely poorly translated and interpreted) goes as follows: Oxum was always extremely curious and passionate for an orix\u00e1. \u00a0She had wanted her father&#8217;s best friend, the orix\u00e1 Orunmil\u00e1, to teach her how to see the future. \u00a0This secret was the domain of the Olu\u00f4/Awo (essentially Orunmil\u00e1&#8217;s priest), a position that could not be held by a woman. \u00a0Determined to learn divination, she tried to seduce the information from him, but Orunmil\u00e1, already old and beyond her seductive abilities, refused to teach her.</p>\n<p>Not to be deterred by this minor setback, Oxum set about trying to find other ways to learn this secret. \u00a0She turned to seduce Exu, who couldn&#8217;t resist being enchanted by her beauty. \u00a0She ordered him to steal Orunmil\u00e1&#8217;s ikin. \u00a0For reference, the ikin (consecrated palm nuts)\u00a0are generally used for divine protection, and special four-eyed ikin are used for divination. \u00a0Having managed to steal Orunmil\u00e1&#8217;s ikin, Exu gave them to Oxum. \u00a0As such Orunmil\u00e1 was forced to share with Oxum the secrets of fortune-telling and handed her the sixteen cowrie shells that she has used for divination ever since. \u00a0Wow, that was confusing. \u00a0Long story short: \u00a0She wanted Orunmil\u00e1 to teach her to see the future, but he refused. \u00a0She seduced Exu and made him steal the Orunmil\u00e1&#8217;s fortune-telling ikin, and once she had them, Orunmil\u00e1 was like &#8220;screw it, here&#8217;s the secrets.&#8221; \u00a0This shows Oxum willing to get what she wants by any means necessary.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-utEvgXKIvT0/UhpkMPIE8GI/AAAAAAAAAck/1l4Gsl_nYug/s1600/oxumart5.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-utEvgXKIvT0/UhpkMPIE8GI/AAAAAAAAAck/1l4Gsl_nYug/s320/oxumart5.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"213\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>Like the other orix\u00e1s, there is a ceremonial dance associated with the celebration of Oxum (what follows about the dancing was mostly plagiarized from <a href=\"http://juicyr.blogspot.com/2009/05/oxum-orisha-of-love.html\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">here</a>). \u00a0Oxum usually starts her dance slowly with hand motions. \u00a0She is usually dancing in the middle of the floor, her feet positioned closely together as it was said that she lived in the river like a mermaid. \u00a0Thus, she has no real foot choreography. \u00a0She makes small dance steps and she usually slides across the floor, rather than steps. \u00a0Her lack of dance steps makes us focus more on her arm movements, as well as her chest, neck, and stomach. \u00a0Her dance is very complicated because the sternum must be in command, since Oxum lives in the waters. \u00a0The hands should always be at the side of the body with palms up. \u00a0The body is required that the shoulders do slight contradictions up as the elbows move away from the body and down as they close in. \u00a0She dances with grace and she constantly drops to the floor to collect water. \u00a0Oxum&#8217;s arms go up and she slides her tail. \u00a0She uses her mirror, as well as her lipstick, rouge, and her comb.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-psr7gbzd7Ao/UhpvdiEtBwI/AAAAAAAAAc0/AqkCtPa-PmI/s1600/oxumart6.jpg\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-psr7gbzd7Ao/UhpvdiEtBwI/AAAAAAAAAc0/AqkCtPa-PmI/s200/oxumart6.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"150\" height=\"200\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>If you&#8217;ve been reading this far and have been paying attention the entire time, you&#8217;ll notice something of a constant with representations of Oxum. \u00a0She&#8217;s always depicted wearing yellow and gold, or when her clothes are few, possessing items of yellow/gold. \u00a0Yellow is her color, and gold is her metal. \u00a0As she represents beauty in its purest form, she keeps beauty about her in the form of gold and precious items. \u00a0Looking across cultures, she&#8217;s worshipped in many essentially parallel religions, and they each have small differences in how they worship. \u00a0It&#8217;s thus difficult to pin down her Feast Day. \u00a0However, regardless of location, it appears to occur sometime around the second week of September (though there is a mention of a date in December). \u00a0It is then, as well as whenever else she is worshipped, that followers will offer such things as honey, pumpkin, white wine, rum, cakes, jewelry, and hens.</p>\n<p>I think that this is probably about enough to get a decent picture of this orix\u00e1. \u00a0Let&#8217;s end as we did before, with some more artwork pertaining to Oxum. \u00a0I wanted to put up some videos of songs pertaining to Oxum, but they&#8217;re not showing up here so, bleh. Ora i\u00e9i\u00e9 Oxum!</p>\n<p>======= Learning stops here. \u00a0Now it&#8217;s just artwork =======</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a "tags": [55, 56, 32, 57], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=188"}, "id": 188, "title": {"rendered": "Orishas: Oxum"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-19T01:56:45", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "orishas-oxum", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 186, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/science-sunday-the-black-after-the-fire/", "date": "2013-06-22T01:47:26", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Lx7T5IW7WQw/UbSt6fYBqbI/AAAAAAAAAXQ/oaKlcez-evo/s1600/Burned_House_III.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Lx7T5IW7WQw/UbSt6fYBqbI/AAAAAAAAAXQ/oaKlcez-evo/s320/Burned_House_III.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"240\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>This should be a relatively short one. \u00a0The other day, this question popped into my mind: Why is it that when things burn, they turn black? \u00a0Physically, what exactly happens when something is being burned that causes that blackness to be left behind, and what is that blackness? \u00a0The answer that made the most sense to me at first thought was that the blackness that was left behind was probably some form of carbon. \u00a0Firstly, materials of pure carbon tend to appear blackish (e.g. graphite), except when their atomic bonds are arranged in the tetrahedra that create diamonds.</p>\n<p><!--more--><br />\nSecondly, organic matter (the type of stuff that tends to burn anyway, and which comprises much of what is on the surface of the Earth aside from air and water) is choc full of carbon, which tends to be bound to a bunch of other elements (your hydrogens, nitrogens, oxygens, etc.). When whatever compound that carbon is a part of heats up, what probably happens is that energy input into that compound goes into breaking the bonds between carbon and other elements, and the other elements vaporize while carbon creates new bonds with itself (and other oxygen atoms creating CO and CO2; carbon is really quite good at bonding with other elements). \u00a0The hydrogen that&#8217;s bound to the carbon links up with the oxygen that&#8217;s being liberated and creates water, etc. \u00a0I only took introductory chemistry, so my knowledge of such things is limited.</p>\n<p>Thus was my initial speculation. \u00a0Following what I&#8217;d always grown up being told to do, I looked it up. \u00a0Luckily, such questions are easily answered by Google.</p>\n<p>What we think of as &#8220;burning&#8221; is really the rapid oxidation of organic molecules. \u00a0When organic molecules are oxidized, they combine with oxygen in the air and produce carbon dioxide, water, and energy (in the form of heat, light, and sound).</p>\n<table class=\"tr-caption-container\" cellspacing=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" align=\"center\">\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-z48WdvhLBbQ/UcXljQN_VHI/AAAAAAAAAYw/2va4XEBtsRU/s1600/combustionrxn.gif\"><img src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-z48WdvhLBbQ/UcXljQN_VHI/AAAAAAAAAYw/2va4XEBtsRU/s320/combustionrxn.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"152\" border=\"0\" /></a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td class=\"tr-caption\"><i>Propane combustion, as an example.</i></td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<p>For things like wood, you have this combustion reaction. \u00a0The energy that&#8217;s released comes out in the form of fire and what&#8217;s left behind is more or less a carbon skeleton (alongside other inorganic compounds and whatever material wasn&#8217;t oxidized). \u00a0Bing bam boom, simple answer for a simple question.</p>\n<p>Looking at this, another question comes to mind: Oxygen comprises 20.95% of dry air by volume. \u00a0Even at this small fraction, we&#8217;re effectively large, fleshy bags of organic matter, walking through veritable fields of oxygen all the time. \u00a0If oxidation happens when objects combine with oxygen, and oxidation is highly exothermic (heat producing), why is it that organic compounds like trees, houses, and hell, PEOPLE, aren&#8217;t just on fire all the time?</p>\n<table class=\"tr-caption-container\" cellspacing=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" align=\"center\">\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-kxfa7nLqwKI/UcXogw8DnEI/AAAAAAAAAZA/7DGww-yiIr0/s1600/burningearth.jpg\"><img src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-kxfa7nLqwKI/UcXogw8DnEI/AAAAAAAAAZA/7DGww-yiIr0/s320/burningearth.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"200\" border=\"0\" /></a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td class=\"tr-caption\"><i>OH MY GOD WHY?!?</i></td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<p>Turns out that organic combustion is temperature-dependent. \u00a0There&#8217;s some lower threshold beneath which something will not burn (at standard atmospheric temperature and pressure) called the activation energy. \u00a0Once a substance reaches this temperature, if it is in the presence of a sufficient amount of oxygen, it will then have the energy necessary to sprout flames without an external heat source. \u00a0Thus, your skin is just fine and safe. \u00a0Try not to walk through any fires, though. \u00a0I can&#8217;t guarantee your safety there.</p>\n<p>And that&#8217;s it! \u00a0Fire!</p>\n<p><b><i>FIRE!!!</i></b></p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-E67iVR2IepI/UcXsyPwVxRI/AAAAAAAAAZQ/0bhtvCV4KYw/s1600/fire_meaney.gif\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-E67iVR2IepI/UcXsyPwVxRI/AAAAAAAAAZQ/0bhtvCV4KYw/s320/fire_meaney.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"269\" height=\"320\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-19T01:49:04", "date_gmt": "2013-06-22T01:47:26", "_links": {"wp:term": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/categories?post=185", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "category"}, {"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/tags?post=185", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "post_tag"}], "curies": [{"href": "https://api.w.org/{rel}", "name": "wp", "templated": true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/185"}], "version-history": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/185/revisions"}], "collection": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts"}], "wp:featuredmedia": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media/186", "embeddable": true}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=185", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/users/1", "embeddable": true}], "wp:attachment": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media?parent=185"}], "about": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/types/post"}]}, "excerpt": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>This should be a relatively short one. \u00a0The other day, this question popped into my mind: Why is it that when things burn, they turn black? \u00a0Physically, what exactly happens when something is being burned that causes that blackness to be left behind, and what is that blackness? \u00a0The answer that made the most sense [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [65, 2, 16, 23], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=185"}, "id": 185, "title": {"rendered": "Science Sunday: The Black After the Fire"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-19T01:49:04", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "science-sunday-the-black-after-the-fire", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 179, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/science-sunday-the-sound-and-fury-of-lightning/", "date": "2013-03-20T01:35:26", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p><a href=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/lightningstorm.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-179\" src=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/lightningstorm.jpg?resize=400%2C300\" alt=\"lightningstorm\" srcset=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/lightningstorm.jpg?w=400 400w, http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/lightningstorm.jpg?resize=300%2C225 300w, http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/lightningstorm.jpg?resize=135%2C100 135w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 400px) 100vw, 400px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p>It&#8217;s been a long while. \u00a0I shouldn&#8217;t have left you (left you), without a dope post to step to. \u00a0Step to, step to, step to&#8230; \u00a0I&#8217;m <b><i>so</i></b> totally not addressing the 3 month absence. \u00a0Onward!</p>\n<p>Lightning! \u00a0One of nature&#8217;s many spectacular light shows! I learned a little bit about electric discharges in college-level Electricity and Magnetism, with a brief mention as to how lightning works. \u00a0However, since I never took any atmospheric science, I never got an in-depth look at it. \u00a0Let&#8217;s get into it RIGHT NOW! \u00a0Note, there is going to be a bit of physics jargon in this post, but I promise to keep it light. \u00a0Cross my heart, hope to die, stick a needle in my eye.</p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<p>Lighting in its essence is the large-scale version of a small spark emitted from a faulty wire: an electrostatic discharge. \u00a0Why does this discharge occur? \u00a0Well, to understand that, we have to take another look at electric charges (first one was <a href=\"http://rationalwhimsy.com/science-sunday-light-you-magnificent-bastard/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">here</a>). \u00a0Charged particles, such as electrons, generally tend to move away from areas with very high concentrations of like-charges (highly negative) to areas of either low concentrations of like-charges, or really any concentration of opposing charges.</p>\n<p><a href=\"http://i2.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/electroninplate.gif\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-180\" src=\"http://i2.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/electroninplate.gif?resize=300%2C180\" alt=\"electroninplate\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p>Their motivator is the electrostatic force, their paths for motion are dictated by electric fields, and in most familiar cases, their conduits are through metal wires. \u00a0Metal allows for electrons to move more or less freely (I&#8217;ll get into how that works another time), and so when an electric field is set up within a metal wire, charges feel an electrostatic force and move. \u00a0That motion of charge is what we know as current. \u00a0Ok, that&#8217;s set.</p>\n<p>What happens when, instead of having empty space (note, not <i>air</i>, but<i> empty space</i>)\u00a0between two oppositely charged objects like above, you have a massive obstacle in between them? \u00a0An object that is resistive to the flow of charges, like say an insulator? \u00a0Well, we have what&#8217;s called a <b>dielectric</b>. \u00a0Dielectrics are basically big insulators that sit between two oppositely charged objects for the purpose of disrupting the flow of charge, and requiring more charge to build before the flow of charge can resume. \u00a0The easy way that I can think about it is like a dam in a river. \u00a0Normally a river would flow just fine when unobstructed, and you only need a minimal amount of water to resume that flow. \u00a0However, when a dam is built in that river, water must build up behind the dam before it can continue its flow. \u00a0If the river&#8217;s current is increased such that it can now go over the dam, you&#8217;ll have a waterfall over the dam (relating back to electricity, overcoming the dielectric strength of the insulator), and the flow will resume. \u00a0If that dam is destroyed by the increase in current, then the river will flow with a greater force than it did before the dam was built. \u00a0So it goes with dielectrics. \u00a0Note, the thinner the dielectric, the weaker the barrier, and the easier it is for current to flow. \u00a0This comes into play later.</p>\n<p>You can also use an already-charged object to induce a charge on a neutral, conducting object. \u00a0As you might imagine, this is called <b>induction</b>. \u00a0That&#8217;s the gist of it, now here&#8217;s the physics of it. \u00a0Consider the following system of a mysteriously-floating negatively-charged stick, an electrically neutral metal ball\u00a0\u00a0(good conductor) insulated from the ground, and some idiot standing nearby. \u00a0Cue the self-made artwork!</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-NaxAlJHgSKc/UUpgVPClCcI/AAAAAAAAAUo/JWkh7kJn94c/s1600/induction1.png\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-NaxAlJHgSKc/UUpgVPClCcI/AAAAAAAAAUo/JWkh7kJn94c/s320/induction1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"160\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>Now, we know that opposite charges attract, and like charges repel. \u00a0So, if we bring the charged stick toward the neutral conducting ball (though not touching), we would expect that the positive and negative charges will separate based on their affinity for the negativity.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-NWNT92d6xWE/UUphf7jX7YI/AAAAAAAAAUw/GvrGBK7uLvw/s1600/induction2.png\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-NWNT92d6xWE/UUphf7jX7YI/AAAAAAAAAUw/GvrGBK7uLvw/s200/induction2.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"200\" height=\"107\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>The electrons naturally want to get as FAR away from the negatively-charged stick as is possible. \u00a0Unfortunately for them, without a conduit to some lower concentration of undesirable charges, they&#8217;re still confined to the structure of the metal ball. \u00a0But consider now the idiot connected to the ground. \u00a0The ground is special because it represents what is essentially an infinite reservoir of neutrality.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-M9J5oZUO_1M/UUpkK5_E-YI/AAAAAAAAAU4/ye8MI6d7h5Q/s1600/induction3.png\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-M9J5oZUO_1M/UUpkK5_E-YI/AAAAAAAAAU4/ye8MI6d7h5Q/s200/induction3.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"200\" height=\"119\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>All charges that are in unfavorable environments prefer to rush toward that neutrality by any available means. \u00a0When the idiot touches the now-unbalanced sphere, all of the electrons looking for a place to go rush toward his arm, through his body, and into the ground. \u00a0Since I don&#8217;t like this guy, let&#8217;s say that the current running through his body was enough to stop his heart and kill him. \u00a0He&#8217;s dead now. \u00a0Soon after his body hits the floor, the mysterious charged stick floats away, onto other mischief.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-KOMJZ2QhQH8/UUpn4_wMZXI/AAAAAAAAAVQ/0JWcDyExlKE/s1600/induction4.png\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-KOMJZ2QhQH8/UUpn4_wMZXI/AAAAAAAAAVQ/0JWcDyExlKE/s200/induction4.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"200\" height=\"97\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>With no reason to all be bunched up in one spot anymore, the positive charges redistribute due to their mutual repulsion. \u00a0What&#8217;s left is a dead body, and a positively charged sphere. \u00a0Ta da! Induction!</p>\n<p>So what have we learned thus far, aside from the danger of touching charged objects? \u00a0A) Charges, when given a conduit, tend to flow toward their electrical opposite. \u00a0B) If you stick an insulator in the path of the flow of charges, it&#8217;ll interrupt that flow until enough charge builds up behind the insulator to overwhelm it. \u00a0C) Charged objects, when brought near neutral objects, can induce a charge onto that neutral object. \u00a0D) A neutral object with an induced charge can become a charged object when its electrons have somewhere to go. \u00a0That&#8217;s all well and good, but how does any of this apply to lightning?</p>\n<p>Before I continue, please know that the theory of lightning creation still isn&#8217;t even fully fleshed out by the people that actually study the stuff. \u00a0So, what follows is what makes&#8230;enough sense to me.</p>\n<p>Now, consider the thundercloud.</p>\n<p><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-u7bSRvPpYlw/UUptkB-wKTI/AAAAAAAAAVY/zTiQm9M2BCU/s1600/angrycloud.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-u7bSRvPpYlw/UUptkB-wKTI/AAAAAAAAAVY/zTiQm9M2BCU/s200/angrycloud.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"191\" height=\"200\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>Your typical thundercloud is a cumulonimbus-type cloud (<a href=\"http://rationalwhimsy.com/science-sunday-the-basics-of-clouds/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">here for more on clouds</a>). \u00a0It&#8217;s big and bulky, full of liquid water at its bottom and small ice particles at its top, and has a large amount of turbulent air to help puff it up. \u00a0The turbulent air contains strong updrafts and downdrafts, occurring with regularity near one another. \u00a0The updrafts carry warm water droplets up from the base of the cloud, while the downdrafts transport ice crystals frozen at the top downward toward the base. \u00a0When the upward-moving water encounters the downward-moving ice, they meet like two great armies on the field of battle. \u00a0My own mind conjures up images of Aragorn and his army of the dead fighting at Minas Tirith. Yes, I&#8217;m a nerd of many facets, so hush. \u00a0The downward moving ice is the army of the dead colliding into the water droplets of Sauron, shearing electrons off and collecting them as they move across the battlefield, downward toward the base of the cloud. \u00a0It&#8217;s rarely a good idea to mix analogies. \u00a0Anyway, what we get here is a massive separation of charge, with all the negative charge building up at the base of the cloud over the neutral ground.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 200px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><img src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-E2G8Ruka1gU/UUpxWJJbx9I/AAAAAAAAAVg/_H8uV5NAQc4/s200/how_lightning_works560.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"200\" height=\"150\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">How ominous&#8230;</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The negative base of the cloud induces a similarly-strong positive charge on the ground. \u00a0Awww snap, it looks like some current&#8217;s about to flow. \u00a0BUT WAIT! \u00a0There isn&#8217;t empty space between the cloud base and the ground! \u00a0There&#8217;s air, and air don&#8217;t like no free electrons moving through it. \u00a0No, friends. \u00a0Air is a dielectric. \u00a0Air don&#8217;t like none of that in its house.</p>\n<p>Thus the charge at the base of the cloud, with nowhere else to go (<i>I&#8217;m lying)</i>, just builds. \u00a0And it builds. \u00a0And it continues to build until a seriously tremendous amount of charge is present at the cloud base. \u00a0Worse yet, if the cloud happens to be caught up in a strong wind, it&#8217;ll be moving, building up massive amounts of positive charge on the ground as it goes. \u00a0At this point, it&#8217;s roaming and just LOOKING for something to piss it off so it can discharge some holy lightning. \u00a0Once it comes across an object tall enough for there to be significantly less air between the cloud base and the object, and to allow all that positive charge to flow through that object toward its top, you&#8217;ll get a massive electrical discharge. \u00a0The positive charges of the ground rush to meet the negative charges in the cloud base, ionizing the air between them, creating a bright, hot plasma. \u00a0LIGHTNING!!!</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-QpNTtIN41sA/UUpz1xyyCHI/AAAAAAAAAVw/r-2dq5LujzE/s320/17950_sky_lightning_lightning_storm.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"203\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Wow. Just wow.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Before I continue, you may notice that I said that I was lying a bit up top there. \u00a0Yeah, I was. \u00a0The charge does have somewhere to go, and typically it&#8217;s within the cloud. \u00a0As such, most lightning occurs within the cloud. \u00a0But no one cares about that. \u00a0We want the good stuff!</p>\n<p>So at this point you may be wondering when the &#8220;sound&#8221; part of the &#8220;Sound and Fury&#8221; comes in. \u00a0Well, the average temperature inside of a lightning channel is ~20,000 Kelvin, or ~36,000\u00b0 F. \u00a0The average temperature of air is around 70\u00b0F. \u00a0If we remember our basic chemistry and model the air as an ideal gas (always wrong, but close enough for this), the air inside of the lightning channel expands and expands RAPIDLY. \u00a0This expanding pressure wave compresses that cooler air, creating a shockwave into that cool air outside of the lightning channel, which produces that loud booming sound that you hear whenever lightning strikes. \u00a0WOO! \u00a0The closer you are to the lightning strike, the louder the boom (the energy in the shockwave, while moving at the speed of sound, disperses as the shockwave expands, diminishing loudness of the sound with distance).</p>\n<p>And that&#8217;s it! \u00a0Now for one last stunning picture of lightning, because it&#8217;s just so goddamn awesome.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 400px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-knoOSm04MGo/UUp3SS7S5CI/AAAAAAAAAWA/wL5UQPRqnAk/s400/Lightning+Storm+Over+City+Lights.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"400\" height=\"300\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">BOOM hahahahaha!! \u00a0I am become death! Destroyer of worlds!</figcaption></figure>\n<p><i>Disclaimer: As I stated above, I know very little about atmospheric science, and only retain a smattering of the thermodynamics that applies to it. \u00a0I do, however, know a bit of physics. \u00a0As such, some of my conclusions and musings may be questionable (though will always at least make physical sense to me). \u00a0This is MOST CERTAINLY NOT to be taken as a definitive source of information. \u00a0I reference wikipedia and other, shadier corners of the web for information, and I&#8217;m too busy (read: lazy) to do any REAL research about this stuff. If anything, maybe this can serve as just a primer. \u00a0But seriously though, learn this for yourself. \u00a0Don&#8217;t rely on me. Feel free to ask questions to me, as well as your local weather folk. \u00a0You may not believe it, but they are out there, and they&#8217;re actually there for a reason! \u00a0And if I can learn about lightning and thunder from a few hours of trial and error research, you DEFINITELY can from proper references and oodles of wikipedia. \u00a0Science for all!</i></p>\n<p>Refs:</p>\n<p><a
