There exists</span><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">\u00a0ethical, technical, and musical\u00a0</span><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">standards,</span><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">\u00a0however capoeira is the behavioral manifestation of each being; the greatest expression of human individuality.\u00a0</span></p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<p><span class=\"text_exposed_show\" style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">A true capoeirista is one who has liberated themselves from all the cul<span class=\"text_exposed_show\">tural mooring lines and psychodynamic obstacles, including from the masters, and leaves only the capoeira flowing free and smoothly from one&#8217;s own body, appearing in his movements and state of spirit.\u00a0</span></span></p>\n<p><span class=\"text_exposed_show\" style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">The strategic foundations of capoeira are simply music, cleverness</span><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">, partnership, and love. Without a doubt, the primacy belongs to the love&#8230; for life, for capoeira, for the art, for the pleasure of just &#8220;playing&#8221; with the purity and innocence of the eternal child that is hidden in the heart of each one of us. The behavioral posture of avoidance to the impact of movements, simulated or not, of attack or that involve danger of any nature, back in the safety net of their practice, next to the unconscious reflexes of preservation of physical integrity and life, generating a system of personal defense &#8220;sui generais&#8221;, &#8220;instinctive&#8221; in the words of mestre Bimba.\u00a0</span></p>\n<p><span class=\"text_exposed_show\" style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">The partnership is vital. Without the partner you can&#8217;t play, or learn, capoeira. Only the presence of the partner allows for the development of self-confidence in the ability to improvise the movements of escape before the movements are given to another whose desire and intention one does not control. To know the thoughts and subsequent movements of someone, we need this someone as partner-opponent.\u00a0</span></p>\n<p><span class=\"text_exposed_show\" style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">Music is the very essence, the mystic root of capoeira. It is responsible for and guides the modified state of consciousness of the capoeira players, and controls the nature and dynamic of their movements. It controls the aggressiveness, dissolves psychodynamic blocks, and generates the playful pleasure of their practice.\u00a0</span></p>\n<p><span class=\"text_exposed_show\" style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">The association of these primary forces controls the ritual, and ensures the mutual respect and sportiveness of the game of capoeira! \u00a0The mestre is only the maestro, controlling the ballet of life that we call capoeira!</span></p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-W2Pa1wZClEE/UU3cvKZKcTI/AAAAAAAAAWQ/8aPSQyU7bR8/s1600/423029_10151382215853898_482923685_n.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-W2Pa1wZClEE/UU3cvKZKcTI/AAAAAAAAAWQ/8aPSQyU7bR8/s1600/423029_10151382215853898_482923685_n.jpg\" alt=\"\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p><span class=\"text_exposed_show\" style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\"><br />\n</span><span class=\"text_exposed_show\" style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\"><b><i>Original Portuguese:</i></b></span></p>\n<p><span class=\"text_exposed_show\" style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">A verdadeira capoeira de cada um de n\u00f3s \u00e9 aquela que mora no corpo de cada qual. Existem padr\u00f5es \u00e9ticos, t\u00e9cnicos e musicais, por\u00e9m a capoeira \u00e9 a manifesta\u00e7\u00e3o comportamental de cada ser, express\u00e3o maior da individualidade humana.</span></p>\n<p><span class=\"text_exposed_show\" style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">S\u00f3 \u00e9 capoeirista quem se liberou de todas as amarras culturais e bloqueios psicodin\u00e2micos, inclusive dos mestres e deixa apenas a &#8220;capoeira&#8221; fluir livre e suavemente pelo pr\u00f3prio corpo, aparecendo nos seus movimentos e estado de esp\u00edrito.<br />\nOs fundamentos estrat\u00e9gicos da capoeira s\u00e3o simples m\u00fasica, esquiva, parceria e amor.<br />\nSem d\u00favida alguma, o primado pertence ao amor&#8230; Pela vida, pela capoeira, pela arte, pelo prazer de apenas &#8220;jogar&#8221; com a pureza e a inoc\u00eancia da eterna crian\u00e7a que existe escondida no cora\u00e7\u00e3o de cada um de n\u00f3s.</span></p>\n<p><span class=\"text_exposed_show\" style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">A postura comportamental de esquiva ao impacto de movimentos, simulados ou n\u00e3o, de ataque ou que envolvam perigo de qualquer natureza, tr\u00e1s no bojo a seguran\u00e7a da sua pr\u00e1tica, ao lado de reflexos inconscientes de preserva\u00e7\u00e3o da integridade f\u00edsica e da vida, gerando um sistema de defesa pessoal &#8220;sui generais&#8221;, &#8220;instintivo&#8221; nas palavras de Mestre Bimba.<br />\nA parceria \u00e9 fundamental.</span></p>\n<p><span class=\"text_exposed_show\" style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">Sem o parceiro n\u00e3o se pode jogar, nem aprender, a capoeira.<br />\nSomente a presen\u00e7a do parceiro permite o desenvolvimento da autoconfian\u00e7a na capacidade de improvisar os movimentos de esquiva ante \u00e0 movimentos partidos doutro algu\u00e9m cuja vontade e inten\u00e7\u00e3o n\u00e3o controlamos. Para conhecermos os pensamentos e movimentos subsequentes de algu\u00e9m precisamos deste algu\u00e9m como parceiro-advers\u00e1rio.</span></p>\n<p><span class=\"text_exposed_show\" style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">A m\u00fasica \u00e9 a pr\u00f3pria ess\u00eancia, a raiz m\u00edstica da capoeira. Respons\u00e1vel e guia do estado modificado de consci\u00eancia do capoeirista, comanda a natureza e a din\u00e2mica dos seus movimentos. Controla a agressividade, desfaz os bloqueios psicodin\u00e2micos e gera o prazer l\u00fadico da sua pr\u00e1tica.<br />\n</span><span class=\"text_exposed_show\" style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\"><br />\nA associa\u00e7\u00e3o destas for\u00e7as prim\u00e1rias comanda o ritual, garante o cavalheirismo e esportividade do jogo da capoeira! O mestre \u00e9 apenas o maestro, comanda o bal\u00e9 da vida que chamamos de capoeira!</span></p>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-19T01:47:18", "date_gmt": "2013-03-13T01:44:55", "_links": {"wp:term": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/categories?post=182", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "category"}, {"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/tags?post=182", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "post_tag"}], "curies": [{"href": "https://api.w.org/{rel}", "name": "wp", "templated": true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/182"}], "version-history": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/182/revisions"}], "collection": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts"}], "wp:featuredmedia": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media/183", "embeddable": true}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=182", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/users/1", "embeddable": true}], "wp:attachment": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media?parent=182"}], "about": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/types/post"}]}, "excerpt": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>By Angelo Augusto Dec\u00e2nio Filho &#8211; Mestre Dr. Dec\u00e2nio. {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=176"}, "id": 176, "title": {"rendered": "Repost: Astronomer to Data Scientist"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-19T01:32:34", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "repost-astronomer-to-data-scientist", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 172, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/viz-rain-in-seattle-really/", "date": "2012-11-28T01:26:39", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<figure style=\"width: 237px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-9w4jvCM83YE/ULWxg0fE1DI/AAAAAAAAATE/10qiHmxjz4w/s1600/sadrain.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"237\" height=\"300\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">This is my face most days..</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Before I moved out here to Seattle for graduate school I was repeatedly warned about how rainy it tends to be out here. \u00a0One person even described it as &#8220;London-esque&#8221;. \u00a0However, when I first visited back in March 2010 (this becomes relevant later), not only was it barely raining, but it was absolutely gorgeous for each of the 4 days I was here. \u00a0I left here thinking, &#8220;where&#8217;s all this rain people were talking about? \u00a0It&#8217;s beautiful here!&#8221;<!--more--></p>\n<p>Two years and three months later, I can confirm the well-known Seattle drear. \u00a0It feels like it&#8217;s cloudy more often than not, and it&#8217;s nearly always wet. \u00a0ALWAYS! \u00a0Am I just suffering from confirmation bias, or is Seattle&#8217;s weather always just generally crappy? \u00a0Well, being the scientist that I am, I sought to answer these interesting and personally-relevant questions.</p>\n<p>The initial idea that I had was to gather a mass amount of data regarding Seattle&#8217;s rainfall over the past 10 years, do some basic statistical analysis on that data, and create some plots of my results. \u00a0This also happened to coincide with my initial serious forays into learning <a href=\"http://www.python.org/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Python</a>, so it would be a good way to learn how to use Python to condense large data sets into easy-to-digest conclusions. \u00a0I went to the obvious sites first: <a href=\"http://weather.com/\">weather.com</a> and <a href=\"http://weather.gov/\">weather.gov</a>. \u00a0I ended up dumping a few hours into looking through each, finding them annoyingly frustrating to navigate, more frustrating to pull data from, and even more frustrating to try to manipulate said data with my fledgling knowledge of Python. \u00a0So, I abandoned those and did what any good scientist would do: complain about his data troubles to his friends on Facebook. \u00a0My colleague Jim commented on that post with a link to <a href=\"http://hint.fm/wind/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">an awesome wind map</a>, noting that someone found a way to use weather data, so I checked that out to distract myself for a little bit. \u00a0While on the page, I noticed that they had a link to some weather data for basic maps. \u00a0Intrigued, I hit the link and found <a href=\"http://www.wunderground.com/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Weather Underground</a>. \u00a0They had data just how I wanted it! \u00a0So, I stole all of Seattle&#8217;s monthly data over the past 10 years and got to work.</p>\n<p><b>Note:\u00a0</b>This is my first data visualization post of what I hope to be many more in the future (inspired by my good colleague and Red Army co-member <a href=\"http://www.ifweassume.com/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Jim Davenport</a>). \u00a0I apologize in advance if the image format sucks with respect to my blog layout. \u00a0Now, let&#8217;s have a look at some data! (click to enlarge)</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-4u8-hBIMBnY/ULWwo9xpYiI/AAAAAAAAAS8/U-Xy7bZ3I-s/s1600/seattleweather_10yrs_monthly.png\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-4u8-hBIMBnY/ULWwo9xpYiI/AAAAAAAAAS8/U-Xy7bZ3I-s/s640/seattleweather_10yrs_monthly.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"640\" height=\"240\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p class=\"separator\">Here we have precipitation, cloud cover, and humidity data for Seattle over the past 10 years up to and including November 27th 2012. \u00a0Each individual brick in the graphs represents a month of data. \u00a0The bricks in the Precipitation plot represent cumulative rainfall over the month. The bricks in the other two plots take the average values of the median (<a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Median\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">wiki: median</a>) cloud cover and humidity over that month. \u00a0I drew some lines in the leftmost plot to bracket the &#8220;nice season&#8221; in Seattle: May-Sept. \u00a0Also, the cloud cover percentages are <i>roughly</i> \u00b16%. \u00a0For whatever reason, the source site lists cloud cover in eighths of the sky (e.g. 4/8, 7/8) so I converted them to percentages. \u00a0Hence, error!</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">The lovely thing about this data is that it essentially speaks for itself. \u00a0The really truly dreary months are clearly October through April, where we get the worst of it all. \u00a0Anyone living here for at least a year could tell you that. \u00a0Worse yet, the averaged median cloud cover per month doesn&#8217;t dip below about 25%&#8230;at all, clearing up only between July and September. \u00a0This explains my Vitamin D deficiency last year! \u00a0<b>What&#8217;s the silver lining here? \u00a0If you ever want to visit Seattle to experience some of its real beauty, come in August!</b></p>\n<div class=\"\">\n<p>Here&#8217;s what&#8217;s really interesting to me in this particular set of plots. Check out March 2010 in the left two. \u00a0It was uncharacteristically nice for March in Seattle! \u00a0Look at <u>all</u>\u00a0of the other March data on both graphs. \u00a0It&#8217;s a local minimum in both rainfall and cloud cover! \u00a0I got duped by Seattle!</p>\n</div>\n<p class=\"separator\">After producing these pretty plots I began to wonder how the weather in Seattle compared to my home in NY. \u00a0So, I altered my Python script a little bit (i.e. changed &#8220;Seattle&#8221; to &#8220;New York&#8221;) and made the same three graphs for NYC (at JFK airport).</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-gCWlcyKfPsU/ULWwoH4C9ZI/AAAAAAAAAS0/DOILd9NcP_w/s1600/newyorkweather_10yrs_monthly.png\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-gCWlcyKfPsU/ULWwoH4C9ZI/AAAAAAAAAS0/DOILd9NcP_w/s640/newyorkweather_10yrs_monthly.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"640\" height=\"240\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p class=\"separator\">Well, would you look at that: the amount of rainfall in NYC appears to be roughly on par with that of Seattle. But wait! What do the numbers say? <i><b>Between 2002 and 2012, </b></i><i>there are only 3 years where Seattle&#8217;s total rainfall exceeds New York&#8217;s!</i>\u00a0WHAT!? It can&#8217;t be! In 2006, 2010, and 2012, Seattle&#8217;s rainfall exceeds NYC&#8217;s by no more than 3.35 inches (2006). \u00a0NYC dwarfs Seattle in all other years, hitting a maximum difference of 23.89 inches last year. \u00a0Crazy. \u00a0The cloud cover is better in NYC though, being more or less even on average throughout the year at ~60%. \u00a0Lastly, as anyone who&#8217;s lived in or near NYC can tell you, humidity in NYC is horrid over the summer. Had I gotten info from somewhere on Manhattan island, I&#8217;m absolutely certain that the humidity result would&#8217;ve been just disgusting.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">For no other reason than the fact that I could, I decided to query one more city. \u00a0Here&#8217;s some results for Los Angeles via LAX.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-tVzFCqocDNw/ULWwmyQWVtI/AAAAAAAAASs/i6cZVzzzWwE/s1600/losangelsweather_10yrs_monthly.png\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-tVzFCqocDNw/ULWwmyQWVtI/AAAAAAAAASs/i6cZVzzzWwE/s640/losangelsweather_10yrs_monthly.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"640\" height=\"240\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>Uh, yeah. \u00a0There&#8217;s no contest here. \u00a0You want to know what LA&#8217;s min and max cumulative annual rainfall are over since 2002? 4.84 and 21.01 inches. \u00a0Seattle&#8217;s and New York&#8217;s? \u00a0(26.80, 48.64) and (34.84, 55.76) respectively. \u00a0That is nonsense. \u00a0Utter nonsense. \u00a0Ugh, I&#8217;m depressed already. \u00a0Bleh, 7 months to go until June&#8230;</p>\n<p>Well, that&#8217;s all I&#8217;ve got for data today. \u00a0If you want to play with the data yourself, or use my code to reproduce some of this stuff, shoot me an email. \u00a0I&#8217;ll send you my code and the .tar files for each city. \u00a0My email&#8217;s on here somewhere right? \u00a0No? \u00a0nhuntwalker -at- gmail -dot- com.</p>\n<p><i><u>Credit where credit is due:</u></i></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: small;\">&#8211; Jim Davenport for inspiring me to try some data viz stuff and providing me with a gateway to my source data. \u00a0Check his blog out. \u00a0<a href=\"http://www.ifweassume.com/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">It&#8217;s awesome</a>!</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: small;\">&#8211; Yusra AlSayyad for her Python wizardry.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: small;\">&#8211; Weather Underground for their mass amounts of data.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: small;\">&#8211; Python, for existing and being free.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: small;\">&#8211; AstroML: Machine Learning and Data Mining for Astronomy. \u00a0It&#8217;s an awesome package for Python consisting of various tools that we use to analyze and visualize data in astronomy. \u00a0It was produced by Zeljko Ivezic (my advisor), Andrew Connolly, Jacob VanderPlas (former grad student, now post doc), and Alex Gray. \u00a0<a href=\"http://astroml.github.com/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Link here</a>.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: small;\">&#8211; The reality of our human condition\u2014wherever we come from\u2014is largely the result of the choices we make every day, and in every moment.&#8221;</p>\n</div>\n"}, "modified": was reading through my coworker&#8217;s blog this morning and came across this article in one of his text links. \u00a0I thought it was an interesting essay on cynicism, so I figured what the hell why not post it here. \u00a0This article struck me particularly because I tend to be a cynic when it comes [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [58, 31, 26, 28, 32, 59, 22], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=165"}, "id": 165, "title": {"rendered": "Conan O&#8217;Brien and Cynicism"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-19T01:24:39", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "conan-obrien-and-cynicism", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 50, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/capoeira-na-roda-capoera-na-vida-part-ii-inferno-suado-e-condicionando-de-angola/", "date": "2012-11-01T01:16:52", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-_r6Vmib47B8/UAwMQL-E5wI/AAAAAAAAAHU/E9Joudas4GQ/s1600/capoeiralogos.png\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-_r6Vmib47B8/UAwMQL-E5wI/AAAAAAAAAHU/E9Joudas4GQ/s320/capoeiralogos.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"128\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<div>\u00a0Capoeira dominated much of my summer after the Batizado and the bulk of my research stuff was finished. \u00a0Because the weather had turned upward (as it does in New York, and NOT here in Seattle) and because Columbia&#8217;s Dodge Fitness Center was no longer available to us, every Tuesday and Thursday we&#8217;d find ourselves outside on the grass to hold class. \u00a0The main instructor for these sessions was Papito, who in my opinion was nothing short of a capoeira beast.</div>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<figure style=\"width: 275px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://images-blogger-opensocial.googleusercontent.com/gadgets/proxy?url=http%3A%2F%2Funcannyxmen.net%2Fimages%2Fspotlight%2Fbeast00.jpg&amp;container=blogger&amp;gadget=a&amp;rewriteMime=image%2F*\" alt=\"\" width=\"275\" height=\"317\" border=\"0\" data-orig-src=\"http://uncannyxmen.net/images/spotlight/beast00.jpg\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">A fairly accurate representation of Papito. Don&#8217;t think he&#8217;s this hairy though&#8230;</figcaption></figure>\n<p>He would consistently test the limits of my endurance, and even took it one step forward from there (providing the inspiration for today&#8217;s title). \u00a0Let&#8217;s set the stage. \u00a0At times, the weather outside wouldn&#8217;t be conducive to practicing, or our spot on the lawn would be taken (couldn&#8217;t access the gym over the summer). \u00a0Perhaps it was raining that day or had rained heavily the night before. \u00a0Regardless, for whatever reason we&#8217;d have to find somewhere else to practice. \u00a0If we still decided to have practice, we&#8217;d typically end up in a building east of the Teacher&#8217;s College on Columbia&#8217;s campus. \u00a0In the lounge room of this building we&#8217;d gather up and start practice, right in the dead of summer. \u00a0Thus began the (in my opinion) Sweaty Hell that was our practice in that room.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">I have in my capoeira career had the fortune to practice with a few different instructors and see how they handle their classes differently with regards to students getting water. \u00a0Some will recognize that different people need water at different times and let them have it as needed, while others will have set intervals for breaks where people can get water. \u00a0In Sweaty Hell, there were maybe 2 water breaks available. \u00a0Maybe. \u00a0On top of that, there was an air conditioner in the room that could&#8217;ve alleviated some of the heated punishment, but Papito did not allow such things. \u00a0As such, every time we would have class there, I would damn near melt. \u00a0It was, to put it shortly, a somewhat harrowing experience for me, especially knowing how terrible my endurance is in capoeira.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">That Spring and Summer were also the first times that I visited the main Guerreiros academy out in Newark. \u00a0It&#8217;s amazing how I had been through Newark so many times in my life, going to and from my uncle&#8217;s house(s), and yet never once did I notice that there&#8217;s an entire Brazilian community sitting right next to the train station. \u00a0The school was located in what appeared to be a small old warehouse, embedded firmly within that neighborhood. \u00a0The first time that I had seen the students that practiced here was at my own batizado at Columbia. \u00a0Curious as to what their place was like, I ventured out there with a couple of other classmates. \u00a0It was&#8230;awkward for me. \u00a0Like that first day of class awkward. \u00a0You don&#8217;t really know anyone, and you don&#8217;t quite know how to fit in awkward. \u00a0My protocol was just to change into my whites and follow instructions.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">Looking back on it now, I don&#8217;t really remember what it was like. \u00a0Granted, it was&#8230;.2.5 years ago, and I had only been out there a handful of times. \u00a0There were a few distinct things, however, that stand out in my mind. \u00a0For one, there was a padded floor. \u00a0This meant that we were freer to practice acrobatics if we wanted to, seeing as how if we fell, that hit to the ground would be far softer than straight wood or linoleum. \u00a0Next was the feeling of community that was there, at least amongst those that were regulars to the school. \u00a0There seemed to just be a lot more comraderie than I had experienced at Columbia. \u00a0Not that there wasn&#8217;t a fair bit of it there; that&#8217;s not what I&#8217;m saying at all. \u00a0It&#8217;s just that the atmosphere of friendliness and community at the Newark Guerreiros academy was tangible. \u00a0I almost wished that I could afford to make more trips out there to visit.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">On one occasion, a couple of us Columbia folk stayed after class at the Newark academy and went to the bar across the street with George Palmares. \u00a0I guess that he was a regular there? \u00a0Either way, we got a grand welcome when we went in with a few of the other students, and we took over the dance floor after a bit of time. \u00a0It was definitely fun, and the brazilians there were very welcoming. \u00a0It was still awkward as all hell though.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">Toward the middle of August 2010, I moved to Seattle in order to settle in before the start of my first year of graduate school. \u00a0Back in March 2010 when I had visited campus as a prospective student, I was taken on a tour of the campus by this dude representing the GO-MAP program. \u00a0During our walk, we struck up some conversation and I had told him that I had just started capoeira at Columbia. \u00a0In response, he had mentioned to me that he knew a dude on campus who practiced capoeira. \u00a0When I moved to Seattle in August, I kept that fact in mind and contacted him. \u00a0He forwarded me the info of his acquaintance Santiago, and I contacted Santiago to find out when he taught. \u00a0It was Mondays, Wednesdays, and Fridays on campus at 5:30 (I think?). \u00a0So, on some weekday in August, I went to their spot on the grass on the UW campus and waited for his class to start up. \u00a0His was my first introduction to the world of the angoleiro.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">Capoeira Angola is distinctly different from the Regional-ish, Senzala-ish capoeira that I had been trained in since that February. \u00a0For one, it was slower. \u00a0<i>Significantly</i>\u00a0slower, with much more of an emphasis on deliberate, well-formed movements, as well as bursts of trickiness (malandragem). \u00a0On top of that, the songs were a little bit different (and also much slower) than the ones that I had learned via Guerreiros. \u00a0The words were the same, but the rhythm of the berimbau, the melodies of the songs, and the pacing of the words were way different than what I had learned. \u00a0I distinctly remember being lightly scolded by Santiago for breaking out with &#8220;Da Da Da no Negro&#8221; (Get Get Get the Negro), since Santiago&#8217;s black and it can be construed as an offensive song. \u00a0 The third main bit that pops out in my mind was the way in which Santiago structured his class. \u00a0The lion&#8217;s share of it was based in body conditioning. \u00a0This makes sense, as all of those slow, drawn out, deliberate movements that are inherent to Angola require a lot of endurance-trained muscle.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><img src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2-yFK9ogFY8/UJNcG4pEeEI/AAAAAAAAAQ4/gKBn9C-64i8/s320/santipractice.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"240\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Me helping Toby with handstand pushups at Santi&#8217;s practice</figcaption></figure>\n<p>So the warmup would consist of jogging, duck-walking, frog leaps, squats, crab-walking, walking on all fours, and other such exercises. \u00a0There was also &#8220;trinta&#8221; which translates to &#8220;thirty&#8221;, but translates in MY mind to &#8220;thirty headstand attempts, and perhaps another 30 handstand attempts.&#8221; \u00a0Talk about tests of endurance! \u00a0My arms would be SCREAMING at me after that, not to mention the profound fatigue in my legs after the warmup. \u00a0The warmup! \u00a0My start and consistent training in capoeira at Columbia had reforged my body to show, quite frankly, a fair bit of muscle that I&#8217;m still not quite used to seeing, and yet I would be winded halfway through practice! \u00a0This was the basis for my first capoeira apelido: Modelo (model). \u00a0The reasoning behind it, according to Santi, was that my body made me look like I could do a lot with it and last through training. \u00a0But, it&#8217;s only for show, like a model&#8217;s. \u00a0Yeah. \u00a0I&#8217;m not gonna lie, that one hurt for a long while. \u00a0It was a solid 7-8 months before I would be comfortable enough with myself to embrace the name, and introspective enough to use its meaning as constructive criticism and motivation.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-sDqd8pXCPIc/UJNfpY02aSI/AAAAAAAAARI/pziDyUP2FEw/s320/santipractice2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"240\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">More practice on the &#8220;magic grass&#8221;</figcaption></figure>\n<p>I practiced with Santi&#8217;s group for about a month, and through it met a handful of pretty cool people. \u00a0During that summer, I <b>rarely</b>\u00a0saw Santi play himself, as he was at the time recovering from an accident. \u00a0I also met Barok (pronounced bah-rOOk), this Ethiopian dude with some crazy hair that had a pretty fun playing style. \u00a0I thought he was pretty cool because he was black, had a pretty nice capoeira game, AND was a physics major at the university, much like myself! \u00a0Then there was Henry, a history major I think. \u00a0While his technique wasn&#8217;t as good as mine, he had (and still has) WAY more endurance than I&#8217;ve ever had. \u00a0When we&#8217;ve been at the same rodas since then, we tend to play each other because our levels kind of equal out. \u00a0And I always try to trip him. \u00a0Angie had a great love for capoeira, and seemed to be the organizational head for the group. \u00a0She had a very strong personality, but not so much that she couldn&#8217;t appreciate the game. \u00a0I&#8217;m still pretty cool with Toby, though I haven&#8217;t had the fortune to see much of him over the last couple years. \u00a0Then there was Joji, who was at that point one of the best non-ranked capoeiristas that I had seen to date. \u00a0He seemed to have everything: personal confidence (and thus a confident capoeira game), a unique and flowing, yet effective style, awesome technique and endurance, and a distinct talent for being able to read his opponents and play at their level. \u00a0I still admire his style today (and hope that one day I&#8217;ll be able to whup his ass).</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">Santiago had an angoleiro friend over in Port Orchard, Washington that was having a party (for Joji, I think) and wanted to know who would come with him. \u00a0I, not having anything else to do during that time, and curious about the greater capoeira community in the area, went along for the ride. \u00a0This was when I first met Gabriel Emeka (and family), and saw for my first time an entire half-day filled with food, friendship, and capoeira. \u00a0I&#8217;ve met a fair number of people in my life, yet few have been have welcoming as the Emekas. \u00a0From what I understand, Gabe is an architect and built his own house. \u00a0Because he&#8217;s also an avid angoleiro, he built a floor roda space into his house. \u00a0So cool. \u00a0Here&#8217;s a shot of his floor from above (not from the same event, but here for illustration purposes):</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 400px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-ojHjPGom8Uk/UJNdzrVYMrI/AAAAAAAAARA/aoTxtrmCTcc/s400/gabesfloor.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"400\" height=\"225\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Cork floor, and you can&#8217;t see it, but he has dozens of instruments on the side</figcaption></figure>\n<p>I&#8217;ll say more about his spot itself at a later date (I&#8217;ve been back several times, and it&#8217;s truly magnificent), but for now I want to focus on the capoeira. \u00a0It was here that I got my first chance to actually pick up and hold a berimbau. \u00a0With Guerreiros, I had never gotten a chance to handle the instruments, so I had no real impression of what it entailed. \u00a0Despite my many years as a cellist in high school and college, I was embarrassingly bad at playing music. \u00a0Holding the berimbau itself was a herculean feat. \u00a0Then there was being able to play a rhythm without dropping the damn thing. \u00a0It was interesting, though I wouldn&#8217;t play again for about 7-8 more months.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-TSkKkBiWd6c/UJNgBSnrryI/AAAAAAAAARQ/wTbOemCU7sI/s320/berimbauatgabes.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"240\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Probably laughing because there&#8217;s photographic evidence of me sucking. Man, I miss that necklace&#8230;</figcaption></figure>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 400px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-6znvaL_3-74/UJNh0ao5zoI/AAAAAAAAARY/wht8sUn8BP8/s400/jojivsgabe.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"400\" height=\"300\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">A nice shot of Joji vs. Gabe</figcaption></figure>\n<p class=\"separator\">This was also the first time that I had seen long angola games. \u00a0I mean <i>long</i>\u00a0games too, with some lasting longer than 10 minutes! \u00a0 Jesus! \u00a0It was Joji&#8217;s going-away roda, so they had him play a lot. \u00a0By the end of it, that green shirt he had was drenched in sweat. \u00a0It was also the first time I saw Gabe&#8217;s remarkable style. \u00a0I had never seen such control while upside down. \u00a0Little did I know that in the future I&#8217;d be at the receiving end of his foot control, but I digress. \u00a0They played a nice game, with Gabe being his fun-loving tricky self, and Joji showing off some decent skill. \u00a0I sat on the sidelines (I may have been playing an instrument at the time) and just drank it all in. \u00a0These were two people who knew each other&#8217;s games well, and were just having fun.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">I also got my chance to play my first few angola games. \u00a0I had never known fatigue like this. \u00a0It was something between 5 and 10 minutes of constant movement. \u00a0Constant kicking, dodging, and acute alertness, all while lactic acid built up in my muscles making me slower and less efficient. \u00a0It was also somewhat odd trying to mesh my high-game training with the distinctly low game of angola. \u00a0I got hit a few times, and I also managed to get in a few good hits myself. \u00a0I don&#8217;t remember well who I played against, but it was fun regardless.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">Once the school year started up in late September 2010, Santiago&#8217;s group moved off campus, and didn&#8217;t come back until the next summer. \u00a0I didn&#8217;t join them, mostly due to admitted laziness. \u00a0So it was that I started my 5-month break from capoeira. \u00a0I did other things in the meantime of course, but nothing could quite fill the hole that was left behind by the lack of capoeira in my life. \u00a0I developed a real, solid hunger for it; a real need in my life to be upside down! \u00a0When I finally did come back to it, it was as if I was being reacquainted with an old friend, and I was so ready to make that connection again.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-19T01:22:51", "date_gmt": "2012-11-01T01:16:52", "_links": {"wp:term": [{"href": [&#8230;] Men can be huge jerks in those situations.\u201d \u2014 female associate professor, biology</span></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><span style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', very many of them.\u201d \u2014 female assistant professor, biology</span></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><span style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">\u201cIt\u2019s not going to be solved "2015-09-19T01:15:52", "date_gmt": "2012-10-31T01:12:05", "_links": {"wp:term": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/categories?post=160", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "category"}, {"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/tags?post=160", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "post_tag"}], "curies": [{"href": "https://api.w.org/{rel}", "name": "wp", "templated": true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/160"}], "version-history": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/160/revisions"}], "collection": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts"}], "wp:featuredmedia": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media/162", "embeddable": true}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=160", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/users/1", "embeddable": true}], "wp:attachment": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media?parent=160"}], "about": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/types/post"}]}, "excerpt": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>Another interesting article that I found on someone else&#8217;s blog:\u00a0http://www.buzzfeed.com/annanorth/what-male-and-female-scientists-say-about-women-in Here, scientists of various statuses are interviewed and asked why they think there&#8217;s such a gender disparity between biology and the physical sciences. \u00a0Needless to say, the responses vary based on the gender of the respondent. \u00a0Here&#8217;s a sampling from the article:</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [41, 46, 26, 22], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=160"}, "id": 160, "title": {"rendered": "Cross-Post: Gender Disparity in the Sciences"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-19T01:15:52", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "cross-post-gender-disparity-in-the-sciences", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 154, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/orishas-yemanja/", "date": "2012-10-24T01:02:09", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-uQbVTscxuzw/UHsXpLKt4RI/AAAAAAAAAOg/iUTi-30fjpo/s1600/yemaja.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-uQbVTscxuzw/UHsXpLKt4RI/AAAAAAAAAOg/iUTi-30fjpo/s640/yemaja.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"425\" height=\"640\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>Because of my involvement in Capoeira, and a long-standing interest in the histories and cultures of the descendants of black slaves in the Western Hemisphere, I&#8217;ve become pretty heavily interested in the religion (some would say cult, and I would say that&#8217;s disrespectful due to the connotation of the word &#8220;cult&#8221;) of Candombl\u00e9. \u00a0I&#8217;ll write something about Candombl\u00e9 as a whole at some later time, but with this series I&#8217;d like to focus in on the gods of Candombl\u00e9. \u00a0These gods are known as Orishas (or Orixas), and they rule over different parts of existence. \u00a0This particular post is going to be about Yemanj\u00e1, the Orisha of the waters and the feminine principle of Candombl\u00e9.</p>\n<p><!--more-->Yemanj\u00e1 appears throughout Candombl\u00e9, as well as Cuban Santer\u00eda, Haitian Vodou, and (originally) Nigerian Yor\u00f9b\u00e1 as the queen of the seas and oceans. \u00a0Before continuing, I&#8217;d like to point out that the name of this Orisha takes on different spellings between different cultures, and that I&#8217;ve chosen this particular spelling of her name because that&#8217;s how I was introduced to it via Capoeira. \u00a0Other spellings (and names) that I&#8217;ve come across in my brief research are:</p>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><a href=\"http://www.qualiafolk.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/12/yemanja.jpg\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://images-blogger-opensocial.googleusercontent.com/gadgets/proxy?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.qualiafolk.com%2Fwp-content%2Fuploads%2F2011%2F12%2Fyemanja.jpg&amp;container=blogger&amp;gadget=a&amp;rewriteMime=image%2F*\" alt=\"\" width=\"247\" height=\"320\" border=\"0\" data-orig-src=\"http://www.qualiafolk.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/12/yemanja.jpg\" /></a><span class=\"s1\">Yemanj\u00e1, Iemanj\u00e1, Yemaja, Imanja, Yemay\u00e1, Jemanja, Yemalla, Yemana, Yemayah, Yemoja, Ymoja, Nana Bukulu, Yemonja, Yemowo, Jana\u00edna, La Diosa Del Mar, Mami Wata, Iemanya, La Sir\u00e8ne, and LaSiren (in Vodou).</span></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><span class=\"s1\">There is no doubt in my mind that there are more names to be found. \u00a0However, in relating the entity across different cultures, it&#8217;s important to keep the pronunciation in mind. \u00a0That way, even though you may not recognize the word on the page, you&#8217;re able to still talk about the same entity with speech. \u00a0It&#8217;s my suspicion that the differences in spelling reflect the differences in phonetics across different cultures. \u00a0I feel as if it is the result of people trying to write down a name without knowing how to spell it first, and so they adapt the same sound to the phonetics of their particular language. \u00a0The pronunciation that I&#8217;m familiar with is yay-mahn-YAH, though there&#8217;s a certain rhythm to the phonetics that I can&#8217;t quite capture via text. \u00a0Such is life.</span></p>\n</div>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Nphuz53iOP8/UHs6I_f9nQI/AAAAAAAAAO0/LaUSgSUsEI0/s1600/yemanja_2.jpg\"><img class=\"alignright\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Nphuz53iOP8/UHs6I_f9nQI/AAAAAAAAAO0/LaUSgSUsEI0/s320/yemanja_2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"254\" height=\"320\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><span class=\"s1\">So Yemanj\u00e1, queen of the waters. \u00a0Her name is a contraction of the Yoruba words Yey Omo Eja, which collectively mean &#8220;Mother Whose Children are the Fish.&#8221; Depending upon the source, her origin and relation to other Orishas change. \u00a0The commonality between them all is relatively brief. \u00a0She rules the waters and oceans. \u00a0She takes the form of a woman with long, black hair, and appears either wearing a flowing blue dress, a flowing white dress, or a flowing blue and white dress. \u00a0She wears a type of veil with beaded fringes that hide her face, and holds a mirror (often cited as a metal fan) in one hand representing her beauty. \u00a0Her colors are, as you might imagine, blue and white (and variations in the shades of each). \u00a0She&#8217;s always represented as one of the superior divinities, and associated with femininity and fertility, but her exact station changes with the person talking about her.</span></p>\n</div>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-yNDbANwRxbk/UHs6ZsxnWCI/AAAAAAAAAO8/4w8ua7JwNCo/s1600/yemanja_3.jpg\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-yNDbANwRxbk/UHs6ZsxnWCI/AAAAAAAAAO8/4w8ua7JwNCo/s320/yemanja_3.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"213\" height=\"320\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p>Her place amongst the Orishas is where the interesting differences begin. \u00a0From some sources, she is considered the Mother of All, where all life came from the sea. \u00a0In others (including the image at the top of this post), she&#8217;s still one of the superior Orishas, but is the daughter of Ob\u00e0t\u00e1l\u00e1 (Oxal\u00e1, Orixal\u00e1, Olufon; the creator of human bodies), who in turn is the second son of Ol\u00f2r\u00fan (Olodumare, Olofi; the supreme orisha) who provides the vital energy, a.k.a. ax\u00e9 (ah-SHAY), for all of living existence. \u00a0In one more, she&#8217;s the daughter of Olokun, who is different from Ol\u00f2r\u00fan, and is genderless (or beyond gender) and also associated with the sea, unfathomable wisdom, and the unconscious.</p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\u00a0From her, many (or all) of the Orishas are said to be created. \u00a0I&#8217;m going to take a lot from Yoruba for this. \u00a0Different sources have her as the mother of Oy\u00e1 (Yans\u00e1, Ians\u00e4, Yansan; female orisha of winds and storms), Oba (marriage and domesticity; fem), Olokun (HOW?!), Olosa (orisha of the Lagos Lagoon; fem), Dada (newborns and vegetables; male), Shankpanna (Babalu Aye, Omolu; smallpox; male), Aje Shaluga (wealth; male), Orisra Oko (agriculture; male), Oke (mountains; male), Oxossi (hunters and forests; male), Oxumare (rainbows, movement, and activity; genderless), and Shango (thunder and war; male). \u00a0Exactly which of this bunch (and others not mentioned here) actually did come from her varies on location and who&#8217;s telling the story. \u00a0While she is formally the wife (and sister?!) of Aganju, Orisha of the soil, I remember her being the consort of someone else whose name escapes me. \u00a0Maybe it&#8217;ll come to me later.</div>\n<div class=\"p1\"></div>\n<div class=\"p1\">Due to the heavy indoctrination of slaves into the Christianity of their slave masters, the Orishas of Candombl\u00e9 also find themselves associated with some of the saints and holy figures of Christianity. \u00a0Yemanj\u00e1 in particular is connected with Nossa Senhora, or the Virgin Mary (considering her motherly status, this really confuses me. \u00a0However, I&#8217;ve never been one to make much sense of religion anyway).</div>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-4RPxdVQrWow/UHs7Npcj-DI/AAAAAAAAAPM/v4WwK4w79t4/s1600/yemanja_5.jpg\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-4RPxdVQrWow/UHs7Npcj-DI/AAAAAAAAAPM/v4WwK4w79t4/s320/yemanja_5.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"215\" height=\"320\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><span class=\"s1\">Aside from all of her familial relations and religious associations, the Yemanj\u00e1 the Orisha has a personality, and women that are said to be daughters of Yemanj\u00e1 tend to embody some of these elements of her personality. \u00a0She can be at times be coquettish and vain, as she is said to be quite beautiful and knows it. \u00a0At the same time though, she is seen as the loving and protective mother of mankind. \u00a0She cares deeply for all her children, comforting them and cleansing them of sorrow. \u00a0She does not easily lose her temper, but when angry she can be like the Sea in a storm\u2014wildly and indiscriminately violent and destructive. \u00a0She plays the role of provider (fish to fishermen), teacher, and possessor of the secrets of the depths of the ocean. \u00a0Oftentimes in Western society, her more powerful nature is downplayed, as women tend to have been forced into a backseat role. \u00a0However, this aspect of strength that she possesses is as much a part of her character as her role as a mother. \u00a0In total, she is the main Feminine Principle of Candombl\u00e9, Y\u00f2r\u00fab\u00e1, and Santer\u00eda, and all that that entails.</span></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><span class=\"s1\">Because Yemanj\u00e1 is such a large figure in Candombl\u00e9 (and the others), she has associated with her many ceremonial rituals with pretty specific elements. \u00a0These celebrations typically incorporate someone that embodies the Orisha through dance as well as costume. This portion is all coming from the same source [7] (with grammar and spelling edited because their grasp of English drives me nuts), so take it up with them if you disagree. \u00a0Her dance movements represent the sea&#8217;s tumbling waves, these moves resemble the art of sewing nets, but also commonly represent a story line. \u00a0Her ocean dancing represents the salty water cleansing the distressed soul, or a newborn. \u00a0There is a lot of emphasis on the hands and the legs in Iemanja&#8217;s dance. \u00a0The hands alternate with palms that are neither flat nor round. \u00a0Then there is the shifting of weight from one knee to the other. \u00a0Her dances can also be done with the help of a skirt instead of the hands, or her fan, to represent ease. \u00a0She usually dances with a silver blue dress and something which resembles a fishing net, so as to represent herself as both fetus <i>[is this really supposed to be fetus?] </i>and fish. \u00a0Her metals are lead and silver, and her colors are blue hues and whites<i>. \u00a0</i>The ensemble varies only slightly for different candombles, and fundamentally consists of a silver-colored metal crown (often fringed with beads), bead necklaces, a blouse, fan, crown, sword, heavily-starched underskirts, silver-colored metal bracelets, armlets, and skirt bangles.\u00a0</span></p>\n<p><span class=\"s1\">The fan (abebe), which is silver-colored metal, represents her beauty and her status as Oxala&#8217;s younger wife. \u00a0With the swaying of the fan back and forth, Iemanja has the power to bring peace and coolness to the universe. \u00a0This motion of the fan can also represent the fanning away of negative forces. \u00a0Usually, twelve to sixteen stranded necklaces are worn in festivals, which contain silver symbolizing the clarity of the surface of the water. \u00a0These also represent Iemanja&#8217;s composed and principled moods. \u00a0The skirt (saia) establishes its fullness from a couple or more petticoats (anaguas). \u00a0A unique starching technique was used to make these anaguas, and was handed down from mother to daughter by slaves, though today it is only with the boundaries of candomble.</span></p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><span class=\"s1\">I personally like the idea of Yemanj\u00e1. \u00a0I like the concept of having a female entity act as the divine royalty of the seas and the origin of all creation. \u00a0It makes mythological sense to me, considering many aspects of the sea and who I know my own mother and other strong women in my family to be. \u00a0For one, the ocean is vast, with water covering roughly 70% of the Earth&#8217;s surface. \u00a0Its extent is vast, and as such its temperament has far-reaching consequences. \u00a0Currents under the water&#8217;s surface cause warm water to circulate to northern latitudes, and the capacity of water to regulate heat keeps coastal cities secure against wild fluctuations in temperature. \u00a0The gentle rolling of waves onto and away from the coast are calming like a mother&#8217;s comfort. \u00a0Life began in the waters, as our lives begin inside our mothers. \u00a0T</span>he oceans provide food and oftentimes a gateway to the rest of the world, as mothers do. \u00a0On the flip side, the ocean&#8217;s wrath can strike the fear of god into you, like mom can when you&#8217;ve stirred up her anger. \u00a0Hurricanes that develop over the water can level cities, while tsunamis can wipe miles of civilization from the face of the Earth. \u00a0As a mother might be inclined to remind you when you&#8217;ve sufficiently pissed her off, she brought you into this world and she can just as easily remove you from it. \u00a0So it is with the oceans.</p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><span class=\"s1\">I happen to think that artwork of Yemanj\u00e1 is particularly gorgeous. So, before the references get up there, I&#8217;m going to just let loose with a handful of images of Yemanj\u00e1 as supplied by Google. \u00a0There are of course many representations of her, but I&#8217;m going to stick to the brown-skinned ones because Candombl\u00e9 is a religion founded by brown people. \u00a0And because I&#8217;m biased, as I am also brown people. \u00a0Enjoy!</span></p>\n</div>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-BVn1bFm2JA4/UHs8-znRnPI/AAAAAAAAAPY/GH2XMGZWxjI/s1600/yemanja_6.jpg\"><img class=\"alignleft\" "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-19T01:02:04", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "zen-and-the-art-of-astronomy-research", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 147, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/science-awesome-retinal-prosthesis/", "date": "2012-10-14T00:57:43", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>I don&#8217;t have the words to explain how spectacular this is. \u00a0Instead, I&#8217;ll let the article do that. \u00a0Here&#8217;s the link: <a href=\"http://news.discovery.com/tech/retinal-prosthesis-120613.html\">http://news.discovery.com/tech/retinal-prosthesis-120613.html</a> .\u00a0\u00a0I&#8217;ll repost the discovery here.</p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<h1><span style=\"font-size: xx-large;\">RETINAL PROSTHESIS COULD HELP THE BLIND SEE</span></h1>\n<div>\n<p><span style=\"font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: small;\">A retinal implant has given a brief glimpse of light to a small number of blind people, and could one day be a common treatment for vision loss due to injury or disease.</span></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><span style=\"font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: small;\">Shawn Kelly, a senior systems scientist at Carnegie Mellon University, has developed a computer chip that translates camera images into electrical pulses that the nerves inside the brain can understand. The result is vision.</span></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><span style=\"font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: small;\">The cameras are incredibly small and mounted to a pair of glasses. The digital information picked up from the camera is sent along a wire to a thin film surgically implanted in the back of the patient&#8217;s eye, between the sclera and the retina. The electrical signals stimulate the nerves in the retina, and that allows the patient to see. The system is powered via induction &#8212; not much current is necessary since the electric field doesn&#8217;t have to penetrate far into the head.</span></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><span style=\"font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: small;\">It&#8217;s a far cry from the bionic eyes of science fiction, though. The resolution is only 256 pixels total, because that&#8217;s how many electrodes can be made to fit on the back of the film. A typical digital camera has resolutions measured in millions of pixels and ordinary human vision involves approximately 1 million nerves, and more than 100 millon rod and cone cells. But it is something.</span></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><span style=\"font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: small;\">&#8220;At 256 we start to get some function back to people,&#8221; Kelly told Discovery News.\u00a0 He said people who tested the system reported the ability to see some shapes and light and dark regions. The tests were not &#8220;field tests&#8221; in real-world conditions, but situations where the implant was used for a few hours and then removed.</span></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><span style=\"font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: small;\">There have been other proposals for retinal implants. Recent work in Britain used a\u00a0<a href=\"http://news.discovery.com/tech/self-powered-bionic-eye-restore-eyesight-120518.html\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_self\">self-powered retinal implant\u00a0</a>that is powered by light that enters the eye rather than the external glasses. At the University of Tubingen in Germany, another project involves an implant that has a\u00a0<a href=\"http://news.discovery.com/tech/retinal-implant-birghtens-future-for-blind.html\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_self\">1,500 pixel resolution</a>\u00a0that is inserted below the retina.</span></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><span style=\"font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: small;\">Kelly said the difference with his design is that the processor is sealed well enough that no water vapor gets inside. Ordinarily the liquids in the eye (and the body generally) are in chemical equilibrium, but any implanted device with wires has spaces in it that can allow small amounts of vapor to form, which can reduce the implant&#8217;s effectiveness.&#8221; We have more intelligence in the eye,&#8221; Kelly said. &#8220;Ours is designed to be stable long term.&#8221;</span></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><span style=\"font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: small;\">One kind of blindness that will be targeted with this device is retinitis pigmentosa, a hereditary disease that destroys the cells in the eye that recieve light. Military veterans could also be helped. (Kelly recently recieved a\u00a0<a href=\"http://www.cmu.edu/news/stories/archives/2012/june/june8_retinalprosthesis.html\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_self\">$1.1 million grant</a>\u00a0from the Department of Veterans&#8217; affairs). Some veterans of World War II and Korea suffer from age-related macular degeneration. Others had their eyes damaged by laser rangefinders, Kelly said. The lasers (which are far more powerful than barcode scanners or CD players) can injure the eyes in a way that causes damage later in life.</span></p>\n</div>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n"}, "modified": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=146"}, "id": 146, "title": {"rendered": "Science Being Awesome: Retinal Prosthesis"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-19T01:00:18", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "science-awesome-retinal-prosthesis", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 144, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/science-sunday-the-basics-of-clouds/", "date": "2012-10-14T00:48:33", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<figure id=\"attachment_144\" style=\"width: 400px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"http://i1.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/clouds-1259.jpg\"><img class=\"size-full wp-image-144\" src=\"http://i1.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/clouds-1259.jpg?resize=400%2C269\" alt=\"After taking all this time to write this post about clouds, you'd think that I could identify the types of clouds in this image.  Nope.\" srcset=\"http://i1.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/clouds-1259.jpg?w=400 400w, http://i1.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/clouds-1259.jpg?resize=300%2C202 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 400px) 100vw, 400px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">After taking all this time to write this post about clouds, you&#8217;d think that I could identify the types of clouds in this image. Nope.</figcaption></figure>\n<p><em>&#8220;I&#8217;m a dreamer. I live to dream and reach for the stars, and if I miss a star then I grab a handful of clouds.&#8221; ~Mike Tyson</em></p>\n<p>Like Mike Tyson, today we&#8217;ll be missing the stars and instead grabbing at clouds. \u00a0Sure this seems somewhat random, considering what my subject matter (not to mention my profession) has typically been, \u00a0but this post is borne out of two completely unrelated things. \u00a0First and foremost is my desire to learn about things outside of my field. \u00a0I spend hours each day, every day of the week accumulating knowledge about astronomy in general and stars in particular. \u00a0This has resulted in a sort of scientific tunnel vision, where I neither know of or pay attention to anything that doesn&#8217;t concern stars. \u00a0I feel like I&#8217;ve lost touch with a lot of the science that goes on in the rest of the world, and so I&#8217;d like to reach out every now and again and learn about what other things the Universe has to offer beyond the various happenings of huge balls of burning hydrogen/helium plasma.</p>\n<p>The second motivation for this post comes from my girlfriend&#8217;s affinity for clouds. \u00a0Some days she just hangs out outside and looks up, staring at the shapes and different species of cloud, getting lost in their dance across the sky. \u00a0Then she calls me or sends me a text message to tell me about them, to which I invariably respond with my own personal disdain for clouds (I live in Seattle. \u00a0I have more cloud than I know what to do with). \u00a0Even though there&#8217;s no love lost between clouds and myself, I&#8217;d still like to know what makes them tick. \u00a0Hence, we have this post.</p>\n<p>Since I actually have no real training in this subject, I&#8217;m actually going to try to rely a little less on Wikipedia and a little more on websites with &#8220;atmospheric&#8221;, &#8220;physics&#8221;, &#8220;chemistry&#8221;, or &#8220;meteorology&#8221; in the name. \u00a0Also, if you want to skip much of the scientific inquiry here (in which case I&#8217;d ask you why you&#8217;re even looking at a post entitled &#8220;Science Sunday&#8221;), you can jump to the very brief summary at the end.</p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><img src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-elDZ8Sdh0Yw/UHqjUyuG7iI/AAAAAAAAANI/DIRh5DD-ybM/s320/evaporation.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"167\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Warm air gives these water molecules a chance at freedom. FREEDOM!!!</figcaption></figure>\n<p>As with any subject that I might write about, but actually know very little about going in, let&#8217;s start with the basics. \u00a0According to the <a href=\"http://amsglossary.allenpress.com/glossary/search?id=cloud1\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">American Meteorological Society</a>, clouds are a visible aggregate of minute water droplets and/or ice particles in the atmosphere above the Earth&#8217;s surface. \u00a0That&#8217;s pretty straight forward, and falls right in line with the idea of clouds as these large wispy things. \u00a0But how does water come to be suspended up in the atmosphere?</p>\n<p>Well mon fr\u00e8re, when water gets evaporated from the surface of the Earth (whether from land or from oceans), it rises into the air. \u00a0Why does water vapor rise? \u00a0While writing this, I realized that I actually couldn&#8217;t answer this question off the top of my head because I simply did not know. \u00a0Hadn&#8217;t really thought about it before. \u00a0It was just one of those things that I knew happened because I have always <i>known</i> it to happen. \u00a0So, I asked Google &#8220;what makes water vapor rise?&#8221; and was rewarded with <a href=\"http://wiki.answers.com/Q/What_makes_water_vapor_rise\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">a nice and concise answer</a>. \u00a0Water vapor is a gas made of water molecules, each one of which contains one oxygen atom bound to two hydrogen atoms. \u00a0While the surrounding air is a mixture of different gases, the bulk of it is <a href=\"http://chemistry.about.com/od/chemistryfaqs/f/aircomposition.htm\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">composed of</a>\u00a0diatomic nitrogen (~78%) and diatomic oxygen (~21%). \u00a0The molecular mass of water is 18 atomic mass units (16 + 1 + 1), while the molecular mass of the overwhelming majority of air molecules is heavier by far (14+14 = 28 and 16+16 = 32 respectively). \u00a0Thus, as water molecules are lighter than the surrounding air, they will rise when vaporized until they have time to mix with the air. \u00a0The resulting moist air is lighter than any nearby dryer air at the same temperature, and will then also rise above said dryer air.</p>\n<p>As the moist air rises, it expands due to encountering lower air pressure (gases increase in volume when the pressure on them decreases) and cools down (through a negligibly small exchange of heat with the surrounding air) to the dew point of that air, which is the temperature at which the air becomes saturated (cannot hold anymore vapor). \u00a0How does this air decrease in temperature and yet exchange no actual heat with the surrounding gas? \u00a0This has to do with two of those little wonders of thermodynamics (thermo), <a href=\"http://hyperphysics.phy-astr.gsu.edu/hbase/thermo/heat.html#c1\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Heat</a>\u00a0and a little something called <a href=\"http://hyperphysics.phy-astr.gsu.edu/hbase/thermo/firlaw.html\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Work</a>.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 224px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><img src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ptrnth-yXMc/UHqkZzAFKVI/AAAAAAAAANY/8YPHDrqT194/s320/temperatureheat.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"224\" height=\"320\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">This is external heat input changing\u00a0the temperature of the gas. This is\u00a0NOT what&#8217;s happening with our\u00a0moist air.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In thermo, a gas is said to be heated (or cooled) when the temperature of that gas increases (or decreases). \u00a0Fairly simple there. \u00a0The important thing though is to distinguish between a gas having its temperature altered because of a change in the gas itself, and a difference in because of some energy exchange with its surroundings. \u00a0<a href=\"http://physics.about.com/od/glossary/g/temperature.htm\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Temperature</a>\u00a0is a measurement of the <i>average kinetic energy </i>of the ensemble of particles that comprise some substance. \u00a0Essentially this means that temperature measures the average of the speeds of individual atoms in a gas. \u00a0High-temperature gases have particles that are very energetic, and vice versa. \u00a0A change in temperature of a gas is therefore a change in the energy of the particles of that gas. \u00a0This is an important point, so read it again if you didn&#8217;t get it the first time.</p>\n<p>Now we move to the second thermo concept, Work. \u00a0Work is done when energy is exchanged by either changing the volume of a system (in this case some bubble of air), the pressure within the system, or both. \u00a0If a bubble of moist air expands into the dryer air around it, it&#8217;s physically pushing that dryer air outward and away as its volume increases. \u00a0This type of action, simple as it is, takes energy. \u00a0Thus, it&#8217;s doing Work in pushing the surrounding air, and therefore the gas itself loses energy as it expands.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-VnmLhtzOOEY/UHqlLWH1qOI/AAAAAAAAANg/t8hhbKav4ZQ/s320/adiab_cool.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"263\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Cooling from changes in pressure and volume</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Now let&#8217;s go back to the difference between an internal energy change in a gas and some external energy changing that gas. An internal change in the gas would be some bubble of air exchanging the kinetic energy (temperature) of the gas particles for an increase or decrease in its size (volume). \u00a0An external agent changing the gas would be that same bubble of air having its temperature changed because of some injection of energy into the bubble (radiation input or something).</p>\n<p>For rising moist air, there&#8217;s no heat exchange with the surrounding air to decrease its temperature. \u00a0Instead what&#8217;s happening is that the gas is expanding, and in doing so is drawing energy for that expansion out of the kinetic energy of the individual gas particles. \u00a0This decreases the <i>average</i>\u00a0kinetic energy of the ensemble of gas particles, thus decreasing the temperature of the moist bubble.</p>\n<p>As the temperature of the air decreases, its capacity to hold more water vapor also decreases. \u00a0What I&#8217;m really saying here is that the capacity for the moist air to maintain water in its evaporated state decreases. \u00a0Why is that? \u00a0This was yet another question that I couldn&#8217;t answer off the top of my head, but now that I&#8217;ve looked it up it makes plenty of sense. \u00a0If you want to keep water vapor from becoming water liquid, you have to prevent water molecules from bonding to one another. \u00a0And let me tell you, water molecules love to bond. \u00a0In order to do this, you have to have enough energy to break any potential bonds between water molecules. \u00a0You can think of it like being a hero in an action movie, holding up a collapsing ceiling so that your friends can escape, where the strength that you use to keep the ceiling up is analogous to the energy needed to keep bonds apart. \u00a0As long as you have enough strength to hold the ceiling up, you can keep your friends from being killed. \u00a0The second your strength falters though, your friends become a nice, red paste on the dungeon floor. \u00a0Similarly, when a gas no longer has the energy to keep bonds between molecules from forming, liquid water forms and condenses out of the air.</p>\n<p><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-LSMd58eN1PM/UHql_IN6mAI/AAAAAAAAANo/J5lU1J1SLH8/s1600/05-17-water-droplets-raindrops.jpg\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-LSMd58eN1PM/UHql_IN6mAI/AAAAAAAAANo/J5lU1J1SLH8/s320/05-17-water-droplets-raindrops.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"215\" border=\"0\" /></a>So yeah, the temperature of the moist air bubble decreases down to the point (dew point temperature) at which it cannot hold any more water vapor. \u00a0If the air is cooled further, it sheds the vapor that it can no longer hold, and liquid water condenses out into a cloud. \u00a0This liquid condenses onto what are known as cloud condensation nuclei, which are particles (dust, salt, burnt stuff) light enough to be held aloft by air currents. \u00a0These particles are exceedingly small in size. \u00a0I&#8217;m talking like microscopic (0.000001 cm) at the largest. \u00a0My question to the internet was &#8220;why does water need to condense onto stuff? \u00a0Why can&#8217;t it just glob up into liquid water on its own?&#8221; \u00a0I wasn&#8217;t met with a swift and simple answer, so this time <a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Condensation_nuclei\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">I defer to Wikipedia</a> with a promise to look up an actual source and scientific explanation for this.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-PeTfu8AsExQ/UHqmxoMe_AI/AAAAAAAAANw/KLlj2QQQ71A/s320/img_full_46359.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"187\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Not the CLEAREST diagram in the world, sure. In position 2, the drag force is less than the force of gravity, so the particle accelerates downward. \u00a0In position 3, they&#8217;re equal, so there&#8217;s no acceleration.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>So now we&#8217;ve got our clouds. \u00a0Large, hulking conglomerations of water molecules condensed onto various dust particles in the atmosphere. \u00a0If you just wanted to know how clouds form, you could stop here, or skip to the end where I talk about the different cloud types. \u00a0If, however, you&#8217;re innately curious like myself, you might want an answer to just one more question: how in the hell do these things stay afloat?! \u00a0Or as one website puts it, <a href=\"http://lamp.tu-graz.ac.at/~hadley/whydontcloudsfall.html\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Why don&#8217;t clouds fall?<br />\n</a><br />\nThe answer here is that clouds actually DO fall (just learned this while writing). \u00a0They just fall extremely slowly. \u00a0I defer to the above link for the more quantitative explanation, but I&#8217;ll point out the quasi-quantitative highlights here. \u00a0If you were in Physics 101 (or 151 at my undergrad college because&#8230;I don&#8217;t know why), you&#8217;d assume that any falling object accelerates at a rate of 9.8 meters per second every second. \u00a0This is the acceleration due to the Earth&#8217;s gravitational pull on that object, and is much of the reason why people used to think that t<a href=\"http://www.gantless.com/paper.html\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">hrowing a penny off of the empire state building would kill someone.</a>\u00a0 However, if you paid attention in that class, you&#8217;d notice that one thing was always assumed with any Falling Object Problem: air friction was neglected. \u00a0This is because air friction (aka drag) slows things down as they fall. \u00a0Air friction increases as the physical size of your falling object increases, the speed of its descent increases, and the viscosity of the air increases. \u00a0A falling object will reach terminal velocity (i.e. will not fall faster) when its gravitational force (based solely on its mass) becomes equal to the drag force. \u00a0Water droplets are pretty damn light, so they reach their terminal velocity fairly quickly. \u00a0The result is that they &#8220;fall&#8221; with a gentleness that would make feathers jealous.</p>\n<p>So let&#8217;s summarize the science here.\u00a0 Water evaporates from the Earth&#8217;s surface and rises. \u00a0Then, it mixes with dry air, expands and cools. \u00a0Because of the cooling, water condenses onto dust particles, and aggregates into clouds. \u00a0The clouds are then held aloft by the drag in the air and air currents pushing against their descent. \u00a0The following graphic is just perfect for this.</p>\n<p><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-crM3WnsJCqc/UHqnx8G8btI/AAAAAAAAAN4/lyXpbLL6XM0/s1600/cloud_formation.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-crM3WnsJCqc/UHqnx8G8btI/AAAAAAAAAN4/lyXpbLL6XM0/s400/cloud_formation.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"251\" height=\"400\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>Now we get to the different general cloud types (and some notable subtypes). \u00a0I had no idea that they were organized into families, genuses, and species like animals are. \u00a0Sweet Jesus! \u00a0As I&#8217;m tired of writing, I&#8217;m going to just list their basic qualities (hot and fresh from the Wiki) and show pretty pictures. \u00a0After all, I am an astronomer at heart, and astronomers are suckers for pretty pictures.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-wgugTrKIP6M/UHqiOrzUMlI/AAAAAAAAAM4/_p_CRmgKgMA/s1600/cloud-types.gif\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-wgugTrKIP6M/UHqiOrzUMlI/AAAAAAAAAM4/_p_CRmgKgMA/s640/cloud-types.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"640\" height=\"432\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<ul>\n<li><b>Cirrus</b> &#8211; fibrous wisps of delicate white ice crystal cloud that show up clearly against the blue sky.</li>\n<li><b>Cirrocumulus</b> &#8211; pure white cloud layer. \u00a0Composed of ice crystals or supercooled water droplets appearing as small, unshaded round masses, or flakes in groups, or lines with ripples like sand on a beach [<i>ed &#8211;\u00a0that&#8217;s a lovely description</i>]. \u00a0They occasionally form alongside cirrus or cirrostratus clouds at the very leading edge of an active weather system.</li>\n<li><b>Cirrostratus</b> &#8211; a thin ice crystal veil that typically gives rise to halos caused by refraction of the Sun&#8217;s rays.</li>\n<li><b>Altocumulus</b>\u00a0&#8211; A cloud layer usually in the form of irregular patches or round masses in groups, lines, or waves. \u00a0High altocumulus may resemble cirrocumulus, but is usually thicker and composed of water droplets so that the bases show at least some light-grey shading.</li>\n<li><b>Altostratus </b>&#8211;\u00a0An opaque or translucent veil of grey/blue-grey cloud that often forms along warm fronts and around low-pressure areas where it may thicken into nimbostratus. \u00a0Altostratus is usually composed of water droplets but may be mixed with ice crystals at higher altitudes. [<i>ed &#8211; I think these are what plague Seattle</i>].</li>\n<li><b>Stratocumulus</b>\u00a0&#8211; A cloud layer usually in the form of irregular patches or round masses similar to altocumulus, but having larger elements with deeper-gray shading. \u00a0This cloud often forms under a precipitating deck of altostratus or high-based nimbostratus.</li>\n<li><b>Stratus </b>&#8211; A uniform layer of cloud resembling fog but not resting on the ground. [<i>ed &#8211; Nevermind, it might just be stratus in general</i>].</li>\n<li><b>Cumulus </b>&#8211; Clouds with clear-cut flat bases and domed tops. \u00a0The smaller cumulus types are generally associated with fair weather.</li>\n<li><b>Nimbostratus</b>\u00a0&#8211; A very thick diffuse dark-grey layer that looks feebly illuminated from the inside. \u00a0It normally forms from altostratus and achieves vertical extent when the base subsides into the low-altitude range during precipitation that can reach moderate to heavy intensity.</li>\n<li><b>Cumulus Congestus </b>&#8211; aka Towering Cumulus; cumulus clouds of great vertical size, usually with dark-gray bases, and capable of producing severe turbulence and showers of moderate to heavy intensity.</li>\n<li><b>Cumulonimbus</b>\u00a0&#8211; Heavy towering masses of cloud with dark-grey to nearly black bases that are associated with thunderstorms and showers. \u00a0Thunderstorms can produce a range of severe weather that includes hail, tornadoes, a variety of other localized strong wind events, several types of lightning, and local very heavy downpours of rain that can cause flash floods. \u00a0Require moisture, an unstable air mass, and heat in order to form.</li>\n<li><b>Nimbus</b>\u00a0&#8211; Dense with water and appear darker than other clouds. \u00a0They can be characterized by their great height. \u00a0They are formed at low altitudes and are typically spread uniformly across the sky. \u00a0A nimbus cloud produces precipitation that reaches the ground as rain, hail, snow, or sleet.</li>\n</ul>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-70FBr1ulcoQ/UHqi2ByVa7I/AAAAAAAAANA/nRiyGOMk0Is/s1600/cloud_types2.gif\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-70FBr1ulcoQ/UHqi2ByVa7I/AAAAAAAAANA/nRiyGOMk0Is/s400/cloud_types2.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"400\" height=\"270\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>And that&#8217;s all! \u00a0This post has me thinking about a lot of other non-astro topics that I want to dig my fingers into. \u00a0Gotta love it. \u00a0References are at the bottom, after the disclaimer. \u00a0As always, mind the disclaimer. \u00a0Until next time!</p>\n<p><i>Disclaimer: while this is far better-referenced than my typical intellectual swill, it&#8217;s still MY intellectual swill. \u00a0Additionally, I know very little about atmospheric science, and only retain a smattering of thermodynamics that applies to it. \u00a0As such, some of my conclusions and musings may be questionable. \u00a0This is not to be taken as a definitive source of information. \u00a0If anything, maybe just a primer. \u00a0But seriously though, learn this for yourself. \u00a0Don&#8217;t rely on me. Feel free to ask questions, and make use of the references! \u00a0They&#8217;re actually there for a reason! \u00a0And if I can learn about cloud formation from a few hours of trial and error research, you DEFINITELY can from an organized reference list and oodles of wikipedia. \u00a0Science for all!</i></p>\n<p><u>Refs:</u></p>\n<p><a href=\"http://amsglossary.allenpress.com/glossary/search?id=cloud1\">http://amsglossary.allenpress.com/glossary/search?id=cloud1<br />\n</a><a href=\"http://hyperphysics.phy-astr.gsu.edu/hbase/thermo/heat.html#c1\">http://hyperphysics.phy-astr.gsu.edu/hbase/thermo/heat.html#c1<br />\n</a><a
