"<p>&#8220;I&#8217;m a dreamer. I live to dream and reach for the stars, and if I miss a star then I grab a handful of clouds.&#8221; ~Mike Tyson Like Mike Tyson, today we&#8217;ll be missing the stars and instead grabbing at clouds. \u00a0Sure this seems somewhat random, considering what my subject matter (not to mention my [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [52, 2, 16, 23, 53, 54], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=143"}, "id": 143, "title": {"rendered": "Science Sunday: The Basics of Clouds"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-19T00:56:57", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "science-sunday-the-basics-of-clouds", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 0, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/a-grandfathers-last-letter-to-his-grandkids/", "date": "2012-10-14T00:46:44", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>I came across this on Facebook some time ago, and have been debating on whether or not to repost it here, as I&#8217;m a little wary of getting too into the habit of presenting non-original content. \u00a0Then I remembered that I don&#8217;t actually care about that, so here it is. \u00a0The link to the original article is here (<a href=\"http://www.huffingtonpost.com/ann-brenoff/grandfathers-last-letter-advice-jim-flanagan_b_1909622.html\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">link</a>). \u00a0Everything that follows is a verbatim repost. \u00a0Cheers.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<p><b><span style=\"font-size: x-large;\">James K. Flanagan: A Grandfather&#8217;s Last Letter To His Grandkids</span></b></p>\n<div>\n<p><em>On Sept. 3, 2012, James K. Flanagan of West Long Branch, N.J., died unexpectedly of a heart attack. He wrote this letter to his five grandchildren just months earlier and it is reprinted here with the permission of his daughter Rachel Creighton.</em></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>Dear Ryan, Conor, Brendan, Charlie, and Mary Catherine,</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>My wise and thoughtful daughter Rachel urged me to write down some advice for you, the important things that I have learned about life. I am beginning this on 8 April 2012, the eve of my 72nd birthday.</p>\n<p>1. Each one of you is a wonderful gift of God both to your family and to all the world. Remember it always, especially when the cold winds of doubt and discouragement fall upon your life.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>2. Be not afraid . . . of anyone or of anything when it comes to living your life most fully. Pursue your hopes and your dreams no matter how difficult or &#8220;different&#8221; they may seem to others. Far too many people don&#8217;t do what they want or should do because of what they imagine others may think or say. Remember, if they don&#8217;t bring you chicken soup when you&#8217;re sick or stand by you when you&#8217;re in trouble, they don&#8217;t matter. Avoid those sour-souled pessimists who listen to your dreams then say, &#8220;Yeah, but what if . . .&#8221; The heck with &#8220;what if. . .&#8221; Do it! The worst thing in life is to look back and say: &#8220;I would have; I could have; I should have.&#8221; Take risks, make mistakes.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>3. Everyone in the world is just an ordinary person. Some people may wear fancy hats or have big titles or (temporarily) have power and want you to think they are above the rest. Don&#8217;t believe them. They have the same doubts, fears, and hopes; they eat, drink, sleep, and fart like everyone else. Question authority always but be wise and careful about the way you do it.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>4. Make a Life List of all those things you want to do: travel to places; learn a skill; master a language; meet someone special. Make it long and do some things from it every year. Don&#8217;t say &#8220;I&#8217;ll do it tomorrow&#8221; (or next month or next year). That is the surest way to fail to do something. There is no tomorrow, and there is no &#8220;right&#8221; time to begin something except now.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>5. Practice the Irish proverb:\u00a0<em>Moi an olge agus tiocfaidh s\u00ed</em>\u00a0&#8220;Praise the child and she will flourish.&#8221;</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>6. Be kind and go out of your way to help people &#8212; especially the weak, the fearful, and children. Everyone is carrying a special sorrow, and they need our compassion.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>7. Don&#8217;t join the military or any organization that trains you to kill. War is evil. All wars are started by old men who force or fool young men to hate and to kill each other. The old men survive, and, just as they started the war with pen and paper, they end it the same way. So many good and innocent people die. If wars are so good and noble, why aren&#8217;t those leaders who start wars right up there fighting?</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>8. Read books, as many as you can. They are a wonderful source of delight, wisdom, and inspiration. They need no batteries or connections, and they can go anywhere.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>9. Be truthful.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>10. Travel: always but especially when you are young. Don&#8217;t wait until you have &#8220;enough&#8221; money or until everything is &#8220;just right.&#8221; That never happens. Get your passport today.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>11. Pick your job or profession because you love to do it. Sure, there will be some things hard about it, but a job must be a joy. Beware of taking a job for money alone &#8212; it will cripple your soul.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>12. Don&#8217;t yell. It never works, and it hurts both yourself and others. Every time I have yelled, I have failed.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>13. Always keep promises to children. Don&#8217;t say &#8220;we&#8217;ll see&#8221; when you mean &#8220;no.&#8221; Children expect the truth; give it to them with love and kindness.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>14. Never tell anyone you love them when you don&#8217;t.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>15. Live in harmony with Nature: go into the outdoors, woods, mountains, sea, desert. It&#8217;s important for your soul.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>16. Visit Ireland. It&#8217;s where the soul of our family was born &#8212; especially the West: Roscommon, Clare, and Kerry.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>17. Hug people you love. Tell them how much they mean to you now; don&#8217;t wait until it&#8217;s too late.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>18. Be grateful. There is an Irish saying: &#8220;This is a day in our lives, and it will not come again.&#8221; Live every day with this in mind.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><em>As was written in his obituary, James K. Flanagan &#8220;was proudly liberal and fought unyieldingly for the underdog. He was an accomplished author, poet, and seanchai &#8212; Irish storyteller; he reveled in recounting the joy of growing up Catholic in Jersey City and his adventures in the Adirondack Mountains and on the Western coast of Ireland. His greatest love was spending time with his family, most of all his five grandchildren&#8221; Ryan (11); Conor (10); Brendan (9); Charles (8); and Mary Catherine (5).&#8221;</em></p>\n</div>\n"}, "category"}, {"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/tags?post=141", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "post_tag"}], "curies": [{"href": "https://api.w.org/{rel}", "name": "wp", "templated": true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/141"}], "version-history": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/141/revisions"}], "collection": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts"}], "wp:attachment": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media?parent=141"}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=141", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/users/1", "embeddable": true}], "about": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/types/post"}]}, "excerpt": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>I came across this on Facebook some time ago, and have been debating on whether or not to repost it here, as I&#8217;m a little wary of getting too into the habit of presenting non-original content. \u00a0Then I remembered that I don&#8217;t actually care about that, so here it is. \u00a0The link to the original [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [31, 26, 28, 32, 22], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=141"}, "id": 141, "title": {"rendered": "A Grandfather&#8217;s Last Letter to his Grandkids"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-19T00:48:31", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "a-grandfathers-last-letter-to-his-grandkids", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 0, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/an-introduction-to-capoeira/", "date": "2012-10-06T05:02:13", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p><a href=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/capoeirasenzala.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-139\" src=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/capoeirasenzala.jpg?resize=400%2C268\" alt=\"capoeirasenzala\" srcset=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/capoeirasenzala.jpg?w=400 400w, http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/capoeirasenzala.jpg?resize=300%2C201 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 400px) 100vw, 400px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p>This was originally written as part of a bio post about me, but the bio ended up going a little bit more personal than I had originally intended. \u00a0There was still the bit about capoeira though, and I didn&#8217;t want it to stay in the vault just because I can&#8217;t write short, non-personal blurbs about myself. \u00a0I talk about my introduction to and involvement in capoeira in my series\u00a0<a href=\"http://rationalwhimsy.com/capoeira-na-roda-capoera-na-vida-part-i-no-inicio-com-os-guerreiros/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">capoeira na roda, capoeira na vida</a>, so with this post I&#8217;ll just say a little about capoeira itself. \u00a0Bear in mind, this is as brief as I can manage to get while still giving a solid overview of what goes on in capoeira.</p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<p><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-sylWtoQOoLo/UHBhAB0tRJI/AAAAAAAAAL8/8zf3prze0kA/s1600/slaveroda.jpeg\"><img class=\"alignright\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-sylWtoQOoLo/UHBhAB0tRJI/AAAAAAAAAL8/8zf3prze0kA/s320/slaveroda.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"221\" border=\"0\" /></a>Capoeira is a Brazilian martial art that at its base combines dancing, fighting, and music. \u00a0The exact time and circumstances of its creation remain unknown, so I&#8217;m going to skip over the detailed history of the martial art for now. \u00a0However, it is known to have been created by Afro-Brazilian slaves some time during the 16th century. \u00a0One of the best ways I&#8217;ve heard its origin described is as an amalgam of different aspects of the African cultures that were brought together due to the slave trade into Brazil. \u00a0This makes a lot of sense considering the similarities between the instruments of capoeira and African instruments, as well as the similarities between the religion of many of the blacks that practice capoeira and some of the religions in Africa. \u00a0And also the black people. \u00a0Because they&#8217;re black people. \u00a0Anyway, yes. \u00a0Dancing, fighting and music.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 255px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-tnQ-F2N8Fjs/UHBhVurARcI/AAAAAAAAAME/j_cnWyEInCE/s1600/mestre-bimba.jpg\"><img src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-tnQ-F2N8Fjs/UHBhVurARcI/AAAAAAAAAME/j_cnWyEInCE/s320/mestre-bimba.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"255\" height=\"320\" border=\"0\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Mestre Bimba, aka Manoel dos Reis Machado</figcaption></figure>\n<p>At a given a formal capoeira event, you&#8217;ll see some standard things. \u00a0The first thing that you&#8217;ll probably notice is that everyone&#8217;s wearing white pants and white shirts, with colored ropes around their waists (if it&#8217;s a school that practices the Angola style, it may be yellow shirts and black pants). \u00a0The insistence upon white as the school uniform comes from a man known as Mestre Bimba (mestre = master, much like a sensei in karate, or a sifu in kung fu). \u00a0Mestre Bimba is the man that legitimized capoeira in Brazil, as before him it was solely associated with black gangs. \u00a0As part of this legitimization, he insisted that his students wear a clean white uniform, as white is thought to represent purity. \u00a0The colored ropes are known as cordas (COR-dahs), and represent a student&#8217;s proficiency in their practice of capoeira. \u00a0The meaning of each color varies wildly from school to school, where a beginner&#8217;s white in one school might be a mestre&#8217;s white in another. \u00a0The difference is usually pretty obvious though, even without seeing them perform.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-26fjUlpSd5s/UHBhqrBsJlI/AAAAAAAAAMM/0RIC5lOuNF0/s1600/roda.jpg\"><img src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-26fjUlpSd5s/UHBhqrBsJlI/AAAAAAAAAMM/0RIC5lOuNF0/s320/roda.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"240\" border=\"0\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">A damn large roda</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The next thing that you may notice is that when two people enter combat, they do it while being surrounded by everyone else who&#8217;s there in a circle, much like the fights people might have in high school. \u00a0This circle is known officially as the roda, pronounced HOH-dah (it&#8217;s really important to get the silent &#8220;h&#8221;). \u00a0The roda is important to capoeira as it provides structure for the games. \u00a0Otherwise, the embattled capoeiristas would fight all over the place (trust me, this happens anyway). \u00a0Some believe that it even provides energy to the fighters, as the energy of the people on the outside of the roda circulates amongst the onlookers and is given to the fighters.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-7oOu34mZzlQ/UHBiYVezU8I/AAAAAAAAAMU/S9iDLActGbE/s1600/capoeiraattack.jpg\"><img src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-7oOu34mZzlQ/UHBiYVezU8I/AAAAAAAAAMU/S9iDLActGbE/s320/capoeiraattack.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"267\" border=\"0\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Attack and defense, with the defense even serving as another attack</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Another notable is that when people fight, they rarely if ever actually make physical contact. \u00a0In fact, many of the fights look like they&#8217;re entirely choreographed. \u00a0This is not something that you&#8217;d expect from a martial art. \u00a0Why is that? \u00a0The way that it was explained to me (I forget by who) is that capoeira is a game (jogo) first and a fight second. \u00a0The emphasis therefore is on playing a game that makes people want to watch (in portuguese: joga bonito que eu quero ver) and learn from you (joga bonito que eu quero aprender), and not beating your opponent to a pulp. \u00a0The latter would be easy, as you could simply rush into the roda, tackle your opponent to the ground, and start pummeling their face. \u00a0But that removes much of the &#8220;art&#8221; from the martial art. \u00a0The emphasis is on technique and fully expressing the movements, as well as having a physical conversation with your opponent by flowing with them. \u00a0This is where the notion of choreography comes in. \u00a0No actual jogo is choreographed. \u00a0There may be some sequences that appear in a capoeirista&#8217;s jogo, but it&#8217;s all mixed together on the spot. \u00a0The conversation that two capoeiristas have is one of attack and defense. \u00a0If I kick at you, you know instinctively to defend yourself by getting out of the way. \u00a0Then, now that I&#8217;m open, you know to attack back, where I&#8217;ll get out of the way. \u00a0I may let loose with a string of attacks, each one you&#8217;ll know to dodge. \u00a0Then you&#8217;ll fight back and I&#8217;ll try not to get hit. \u00a0And so it goes on and on.</p>\n<p><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-RjsgKm3WIy4/UHBlHCtJ99I/AAAAAAAAAMk/71rQjojjFf0/s1600/ginga.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-RjsgKm3WIy4/UHBlHCtJ99I/AAAAAAAAAMk/71rQjojjFf0/s320/ginga.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"240\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>I would be remiss if I didn&#8217;t say anything about the ginga, the basic swinging movement of capoeira. \u00a0In fact, I&#8217;d probably be yelled at for it by a variety of people. \u00a0The ginga is what you do when you&#8217;re not doing anything at all. \u00a0Se n\u00e3o ataca ou defensa, voc\u00ea deve gingar (If you don&#8217;t attack or defend, you must ginga). \u00a0The ginga gives your movement rhythm, and serves as a launching point for any capoeira movement. \u00a0It gives you your basic stance, guarding your face with one hand and your side with the other, while giving you a solid footing so that no one trips you up too easily. \u00a0It gives you a little bit of unpredictability too, as you can perform most movements from literally any point in the ginga (if you&#8217;re skilled enough). \u00a0It also gives your particular capoeira game a smattering of your own individuality. \u00a0Every ginga is different, and while there are many wrong ways to ginga, there&#8217;s no one right way. \u00a0It should never be mechanical, and always have elements of your own personal swing. \u00a0And of course, always keep your face guarded. \u00a0Because if you don&#8217;t, someone will try to check you on it, and while it is a very quick and direct way to learn to correct your form, a broken nose is never fun.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><img src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-XxFZB_spWK8/UHBiypf6jvI/AAAAAAAAAMc/c_cpFna7HQE/s320/capoeira-kids-bateria.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"268\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Kids bateria</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The last major notable is the presence of music. \u00a0There are almost always instruments at every capoeira roda. \u00a0The staples are the berimbau, the atabaque, and the pandeiro, though there may be a host of others such as the agogo, and the reco-reco. \u00a0The berimbau is most easily described as looking like a bow (like one that fires arrows) with a large gourd (caba\u00e7a) tied to the bottom around the main string (aram\u00e9). \u00a0It has three basic sounds, and is played with a combination of a large coin (or a flat rock, either of which is known as the dobrao) and a long stick (baqueta). \u00a0The person playing the berimbau will hold the entire instrument in his left hand by clutching the string holding the gourd to the instrument with his pinky, and clutching the main shaft of the instrument (the verga) with his ring and index fingers. \u00a0He&#8217;ll hold the dobrao in between his index finger and thumb, and use it to apply varying degrees of pressure to the aram\u00e9 in order to make different sounds when it&#8217;s hit with the baqueta. \u00a0The hand holding the baqueta often will also hold a small, wooden, woven container of beans called the caixixi, which will make sounds like a shaker with each hit of the baqueta. \u00a0The atabaque is analogous to the conga drum, and is a long wooden drum with a head of calfskin. \u00a0The pandeiro is simply a large tambourine. \u00a0These instruments form what is known as the bateria, or the band of instruments.</p>\n<p>The person holding the berimbau controls the flow of each jogo with his rhythm, and also typically leads everyone in song. \u00a0The atabaque then picks up after the rhythm of the berimbau, and the other instruments after that. \u00a0Everyone else claps in rhythm to the berimbau and sings the chorus of whatever song the bateria has started. \u00a0There are meaningful songs and nonsense songs. \u00a0There are songs for fast games and songs for slow ones. \u00a0Songs for men, songs for women, songs for birthdays, songs for deaths, songs for newcomers, and songs for farewells. \u00a0A clever berimbau player will link songs to different rhythms and events in the game. \u00a0If he&#8217;s particularly savvy, he might even start off the roda with a ladainha, which is a long solo at the very beginning of a roda which. \u00a0At its end, the capoeirista gives recognition to God (or a god), his mestre, whoever else he wants to give recognition to, and to capoeira itself. \u00a0If people get too far apart, he might start singing &#8220;jogo de dentro&#8221; to get them to play closer together. \u00a0If the roda is about to end, he might sing &#8220;para roda capoeira&#8221; as a send off.</p>\n<p>And there you have the bulk of it. \u00a0There will no doubt be more about capoeira on my page as time goes on, but I think that&#8217;s a pretty good primer to start with. \u00a0Here&#8217;s a video that I just love to watch which shows you a bit of it in motion (and actually is choreographed). \u00a0And before you ask, no, I am not nearly this polished.<br />\n<iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/Z8xxgFpK-NM\" width=\"420\" height=\"315\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe></p>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-19T00:46:04", "date_gmt": scientist.</p>\n<p>Anyway, enough of my babbling about the topic. \u00a0The link to the article is here: <a did get a camera for capoeira, however I borrowed it from the university because I was broke. \u00a0So really, this is a </span><span style=\"color: #ff0000;\">FAILURE.</span></i></b></span></li>\n</ol>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<div>\n<p><span style=\"font-family: Arial, Tahoma, Helvetica, FreeSans, sans-serif;\">Well, there we have it. \u00a0The total score for the moment is 6 things accomplished and 9 things definitely failed out of the 41 resolutions. \u00a0Hey, 6 is not bad. \u00a0Thats 14.6% completion, with a ~22% failure thus far. \u00a0Should ideally \u00a0be about 75% completion considering 75% of the year is gone now. \u00a0I hope to have at least 51% completion by the end of the year, though. \u00a0Nobody&#8217;s perfect, eh? \u00a0Some additional statistics/notes here that I find interesting:</span></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p><span style=\"font-family: Arial, Tahoma, Helvetica, FreeSans, "taxonomy": "post_tag"}], "curies": [{"href": "https://api.w.org/{rel}", "name": "wp", "templated": true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/126"}], "version-history": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media/127", "embeddable": true}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=126", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/users/1", "embeddable": true}], "wp:attachment": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media?parent=126"}], "about": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/types/post"}]}, "excerpt": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>So it&#8217;s been quite a year for me, with many changes that I did not see coming, both positive and negative. \u00a0As such, I&#8217;d like to take quick account of the goals that I had earlier in the year and see how I did toward achieving them thus far over the past 10 months. \u00a0Or [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [6, 26, 2, 28, 7], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=126"}, "id": 126, "title": {"rendered": "The 2012 Resolutions Review"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-18T04:55:08", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "the-2012-resolutions-review", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 124, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/science-sunday-the-stars-part-iii-low-mass-shinys/", "date": "2012-09-30T04:43:01", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<figure id=\"attachment_124\" style=\"width: 400px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"http://i1.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/Morgan-Keenan_spectral_classification.png\"><img class=\"size-full wp-image-124\" src=\"http://i1.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/Morgan-Keenan_spectral_classification.png?resize=400%2C145\" alt=\"This one's about the red-boxed stars\" srcset=\"http://i1.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/Morgan-Keenan_spectral_classification.png?w=400 400w, http://i1.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/Morgan-Keenan_spectral_classification.png?resize=300%2C109 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 400px) 100vw, 400px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">This one&#8217;s about the red-boxed stars</figcaption></figure>\n<p>On <a href=\"http://rationalwhimsy.com/science-sunday-the-stars-part-ii-all-types-of-shiny-things/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">the last Science Sunday</a>, I discussed all the basic stellar populations, putting up little descriptions of each part of the HR diagram. \u00a0For the next few posts, I want to go in more depth regarding each portion of the diagram, starting with the Main Sequence. \u00a0As always, Wikipedia will be a major source of information. \u00a0Aside from that, I&#8217;ll also *gasp* be using actual notes from my actual Stellar Interiors class that I actually took\u00a0(and somehow passed)\u00a0this past spring. \u00a0Actually! \u00a0So there might be some actual truth to this post! \u00a0Don&#8217;t count on it though.</p>\n<p>Without further ado, let&#8217;s get into it.</p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<p>The Main Sequence (hereon referred to as MS) spans a mass range from about 0.08 solar masses up to (and beyond?) let&#8217;s say 100 solar masses. \u00a0For reference, 1 solar mass is basically the mass of our Sun. \u00a0Because MS stars span such a large dynamic range, I&#8217;m going to chop even this post into two &#8220;smaller&#8221; ones. \u00a0As you might infer from the title, this post will cover low-mass MS stars. \u00a0This means that we&#8217;ll be discussing stars whose initial masses don&#8217;t exceed 6 solar masses. \u00a0Why this particular cutoff in the mass range? \u00a0Well, something super duper <b><i>extra</i></b> special happens to stars above this range when they die. \u00a0But those are details for another Sunday.</p>\n<div>\u00a0So, low mass MS stars. \u00a0The basics were <a href=\"http://rationalwhimsy.com/science-sunday-the-stars-part-ii-all-types-of-shiny-things/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">covered last time</a>, but I&#8217;ll copy those here and move from there.</div>\n<div></div>\n<blockquote>\n<div><strong>The Main Sequence:</strong>\u00a0Where stars of all types reside after their initial birth. \u00a0Stars on the Main Sequence will be fusing hydrogen into helium (by way of either\u00a0<a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proton_proton_chain\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">the p-p chain</a>\u00a0or\u00a0<a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CNO_cycle\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">the CNO cycle</a>) in their cores, much like\u00a0<a href=\"http://nhuntwalker.blogspot.com/2012/01/science-sunday-stars-part-i.html\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">our own Sun</a>. \u00a0Roughly about 10% of a star&#8217;s initial mass will be involved in fusion over its lifetime as a Main Sequence star, with 0.7% of that mass being converted into energy. \u00a0[&#8230;skipping over a lot of it&#8230;]\u00a0 If we divide the total energy production of the Sun in its lifetime (1.26 x 10^44 J) by this rate (1.26 x 10^34 J/year), we get out that the Sun should last about 10^10 years, or 10 billion years.</div>\n</blockquote>\n<div>As was stated, MS stars are defined by hydrogen fusion in their cores producing the light that allows them to be seen. \u00a0For many of these low-mass MS stars (mass &lt; 2 solar masses), the overwhelming majority of hydrogen fusion takes place via <a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proton_proton_chain\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">the proton-proton chain</a> (hereafter the pp chain). \u00a0The pp chain works something like this&#8230;</div>\n<div></div>\n<div>\n<figure style=\"width: 175px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-UAd1ZxsP5bI/UGYlzyVwxjI/AAAAAAAAAIs/139nmye_ElE/s200/pp_fusion.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"175\" height=\"200\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">The proton sitting next to a neutron is the deuterium nucleus.</figcaption></figure>\n<div></div>\n<p>Two lone protons are chilling around in the core of a star. \u00a0Their companion electrons, that would make them neutral atoms, have long since been stripped off. \u00a0It&#8217;s really hot (~10 million Kelvin) and really dense (screw you and your numbers). As such, even though they&#8217;re naturally opposed to being around one another, they&#8217;re able to overcome their mutual repulsion and <i>FUSE</i>\u00a0into a single, bare, deuterium nucleus. \u00a0In doing so, they spit out some antimatter (the antielectron), and a neutrino (which ends up escaping from the star very quickly). \u00a0This first step takes a dumb long time (~1 billion years), and produces about 0.42 MeV of energy. \u00a0The escaped antielectron will undoubtedly meet up with a normal electron and form a joint suicide pact, going on to release 1.02 MeV of energy. \u00a0The total produced in this step is ~1.44 MeV of energy, which corresponds to just about 2.3 x 10^(-13) Joules, or the amount of energy coming off of a 40-watt lightbulb in 5.75 femtoseconds.</div>\n<div></div>\n<div style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://www.windows2universe.org/sun/Solar_interior/Nuclear_Reactions/Fusion/Fusion_in_stars/Animation/pp2.mpg\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Link for Helium-3 formation</a></div>\n<div></div>\n<div>Almost immediately (1 second) after that deuterium nucleus is formed, another proton that isn&#8217;t looking where it&#8217;s going just slams face (face?) first into it, creating a helium-3 nucleus, as well as producing about 5.5 MeV of energy. \u00a0You can see a schematic of this in the link above. \u00a0The yellow ball popping out is light in the form of gamma radiation.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<figure style=\"width: 200px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><img src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-0MnpKNjH_9I/UGYr8cTnd9I/AAAAAAAAAI8/wmWH50ycWY8/s200/H3_fusion.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"200\" height=\"110\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">The final product: raw uncut He-4. The good shit.</figcaption></figure>\n</div>\n<div>This final stage differs a wee bit depending on just how hot it is in the star&#8217;s core, but I don&#8217;t really care. I&#8217;m going to give the simplified version here. \u00a0Over the next million years, two helium-3 nuclei have a hell of a time smacking together to make helium-4, producing another 12.9 MeV of energy and two chaos-wreaking protons. \u00a0Altogether, this whole process produces about 27 MeV of energy. \u00a0That&#8217;s just about 4.3 x 10^(-12) Joules of energy.</div>\n<div></div>\n<div><i>&#8220;Um&#8230;what gives? \u00a0I thought this process produced a star&#8217;s light. \u00a0It takes over a billion years and doesn&#8217;t make enough energy to power my TV!&#8221;</i> \u00a0Well maybe you should hush\u00a0and think for a second. \u00a0There&#8217;s more than just 6 damn protons in a star&#8217;s core right? \u00a0Right! \u00a0And all the light that&#8217;s produced at the surface has to come from these reactions in the core right? \u00a0Right! \u00a0So let&#8217;s be smart about this. \u00a0If we measure the brightness of a given star, let&#8217;s say our Sun for instance (~4 x 10^33 watts or Joules per second), we can extrapolate back to find out just how many times this is happening in the Sun&#8217;s core every second. \u00a04 x 10^33 Joules produced every second, and each process produces ~4 x 10^(-12) Joules. \u00a0That means that every second, this process is happening roughly 1 x 10^45 times in the Sun! \u00a0Yeah. \u00a0There&#8217;s a lot of protons in stellar cores.</div>\n<div></div>\n<div>More massive stars still use the pp chain, but also get a significant contribution from the Carbon-Nitrogen-Oxygen cycle. \u00a0Look on wikipedia for that. \u00a0I&#8217;m lazy, and there&#8217;s more to talk about than different methods of fusion.</div>\n<div></div>\n<div>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-fKWMaW9MQ0c/UGZBFWBOP2I/AAAAAAAAAJU/WqoBH2LH5Wg/s320/suninterior2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"316\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Radiative zone between the core and the convection zone</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Let&#8217;s keep looking into the interiors of these stars, and consider how all of this energy gets out. \u00a0Now, stars are all about energy transport. \u00a0You&#8217;ve got to get all of that energy that&#8217;s generated in the core out to the surface of the star somehow. \u00a0Typically, energy gets out from the core by scattering the light produced by fusion outward from particle to particle over ~10 million years (the figure changes depending on what type of star we&#8217;re talking about). \u00a0That scattering is demonstrated by the white path of photons in the picture above.</p>\n<p>However, with most stars, energy transport by outward scattering of radiation isn&#8217;t the most efficient method of transport throughout the entirety of the star. \u00a0And nature is nothing but efficient. \u00a0Always (he says as he remembers his appendix&#8230;). \u00a0Soooo&#8230;the star will instead turn to convection in order to transport energy outward. \u00a0HOW DOES THIS WOOOOOOORK!? \u00a0Consider a pot of boiling water.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-eCJQR0-ZO6k/UGZHOeU8s9I/AAAAAAAAAJk/H0L3w72GLPM/s320/waterconvection.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"216\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Convection of the agua</figcaption></figure>\n<p>You put a pot of water on the stove and it&#8217;s cold. \u00a0You turn the stove on and the pot gets heated from below. \u00a0Now as we all know, hot water rises and cool water sinks. \u00a0So, hot bubbles created by the heating from below rise to the top of the water, reach the surface, release their heat (energy) to the air above, cool off, and sink back to the bottom where they&#8217;re heated again. \u00a0And thus the cycle continues. \u00a0This is what happens in stars, except instead of water it&#8217;s hot plasma rising and falling back into the star.</p>\n<p>Now, convection in low mass stars is interesting, as the location of the convective layer changes based on the mass of the star. \u00a0For stars with masses less than that of the Sun, the convective layer starts at the surface, and extends downward from there into the star as the mass of your star decreases. \u00a0Going upward from 1 solar mass, the convective layer starts at the core and grows outward with increasing mass. \u00a0This is illustrated in the graphic that I copied out of my notebook below.</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 400px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-vrncTvoMVdE/UGZPYBx8NoI/AAAAAAAAAJ0/RSljQyWqXiI/s400/convectionschema.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"400\" height=\"237\" border=\"0\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Ok so this is like the first science-ish plot to appear on this blog, so pay attention to it. m/M is the mass fraction of the star, and M/Mo is the actual mass of the star in solar masses. The shaded area is where convection occurs in the star, as a function of mass fraction and the overall mass of the star.</figcaption></figure>\n<div>\n<p>Why the division at 1 solar mass (oh geez oh geez the Sun is super duper extra special!)? \u00a0Well, for stars of less than one solar mass, their exteriors are really cool (temperature-wise). \u00a0In addition, the temperature of the star doesn&#8217;t drops off very steeply as you move from the core of the star to the surface of it. \u00a0As such, radiative energy transfer becomes very inefficient. \u00a0Convection on the other hand is more efficient (due to EQUATIONS that I&#8217;m too lazy show here), and thus the energy from the interior of the star gets transported outward via convection.</p>\n<p>With stars that are greater than 1 solar mass, the conditions are a bit different. \u00a0In these circumstances, the star&#8217;s interior is really really hot. \u00a0It&#8217;s so hot that the temperature toward the core of the star doesn&#8217;t decrease very sharply as you move outward in the star. \u00a0As such, the core transports energy outward via convective bubbles, until the temperature of the star starts to decrease sharply again with distance from the star&#8217;s center. \u00a0The hotter a star is in its interior, the farther out this convective layer extends.</p>\n<p>Alright. \u00a0That&#8217;s enough for now. \u00a0This was a huge information dump. \u00a0Until next time!</p>\n<p><i>Here are some non-wikipedia, non-class notes references that I may have stolen from for this post:</i></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><a href=\"http://csep10.phys.utk.edu/astr162/lect/energy/ppchain.html\"><i>http://csep10.phys.utk.edu/astr162/lect/energy/ppchain.html</i></a></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><a href=\"http://hyperphysics.phy-astr.gsu.edu/hbase/thermo/heatra.html\"><i>http://hyperphysics.phy-astr.gsu.edu/hbase/thermo/heatra.html</i></a></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p><i>Disclaimer disclaimer, this is scientific musing at best. \u00a0This is not to be taken as a definitive source of information. \u00a0If anything, maybe just a primer. \u00a0But seriously though, learn this for yourself. \u00a0Don&#8217;t rely on me. At least, not until I get a doctorate and am qualified to teach this type of stuff. \u00a0Blah blah stolen from wikipedia, blah blah order of magnitude calculations. \u00a0Feel free to ask questions!</i></p>\n</div>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<div></div>\n</div>\n<div></div>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-18T04:52:27", "date_gmt": "2012-09-30T04:43:01", "_links": {"wp:term": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/categories?post=123", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "category"}, {"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/tags?post=123", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "post_tag"}], "curies": [{"href": "https://api.w.org/{rel}", "name": "wp", "templated": true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/123"}], "version-history": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/123/revisions"}], "collection": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts"}], "wp:featuredmedia": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media/124", "embeddable": true}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=123", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/users/1", "embeddable": true}], "wp:attachment": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media?parent=123"}], "about": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/types/post"}]}, "excerpt": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>On the last Science Sunday, I discussed all the basic stellar populations, putting up little descriptions of each part of the HR diagram. \u00a0For the next few posts, I want to go in more depth regarding each portion of the diagram, starting with the Main Sequence. \u00a0As always, Wikipedia will be a major source of [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [13, 31, 2, 16, 23, 24], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=123"}, "id": 123, "title": {"rendered": "Science Sunday: The Stars &#8211; so that&#8217;s what I did. "cross-post-us-population-by-longitude-latitude", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 116, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/the-storybook-of-the-kingkiller-chronicles-pt-1-intro-tinkers-and-taborlin-the-great/", "date": "2012-09-25T04:32:03", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<figure id=\"attachment_116\" style=\"width: 300px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"http://i1.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/kvothe.jpg\"><img class=\"wp-image-116 My hero</figcaption></figure>\n<p>There exists a series of books in this world that currently has my undying love: The Kingkiller Chronicles. \u00a0This series is as of now unfinished and still being written, with 2 books out of 3 already published by the author <a href=\"http://blog.patrickrothfuss.com/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Patrick Rothfuss</a>. \u00a0The first two books are <a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/Name-Wind-Kingkiller-Chronicles-Day/dp/0756404746\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">The Name of the Wind</a>, and <a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/The-Wise-Mans-Fear-Kingkiller/dp/0756407125/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">The Wise Man&#8217;s Fear</a>. <i>\u00a0<b>Buy them</b></i>. \u00a0The only thing that you&#8217;ll regret about this purchase is that the third book has not been published yet, leaving thoughts of how this story will conclude to keep you up at night like a crack addict jonesin&#8217; for his (or her! Equal opportunity, folks) next hit.</p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<p>The story is a story within a story, following the life and adventures of one Kvothe, Arliden&#8217;s Son. \u00a0Without going into too much detail, I&#8217;ll just put up here the way in which he introduces himself in the first book (it&#8217;s also written on the inner leaf of the book):</p>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0My name is Kvothe, pronounced nearly the same as &#8220;quothe.&#8221; \u00a0Names are important as they tell you a great deal about a person. \u00a0I&#8217;ve had more names than anyone has a right to.</p>\n<p>The Adem call me Maedre. \u00a0Which, depending on how it&#8217;s spoken, can mean The Flame, The Thunder, or the Broken Tree.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The Flame&#8221; is obvious if you&#8217;ve ever seen me. \u00a0I have red hair, bright. \u00a0If I had been born a couple of hundred years ago I would probably have been burned as a demon. \u00a0I keep it short but it&#8217;s unruly. \u00a0When left to its own devices, it sticks up and makes me look as if I have been set afire.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The Thunder&#8221; I attribute to a strong baritone and a great deal of stage training at an early age.</p>\n<p>I&#8217;ve never thought of &#8220;The Broken Tree&#8221; as very significant. \u00a0Although in retrospect, I suppose it could be considered at least partially prophetic.</p>\n<p>My first mentor called me E&#8217;lir because I was clever and I knew it. \u00a0My first real lover called me Dulator because she liked the sound of it. \u00a0I have been called Shadicar, Lightfinger, and Six-String. \u00a0I have been called Kvothe the Bloodless, Kvothe the Arcane, and Kvothe Kingkiller. \u00a0I have earned those names. \u00a0Bought and paid for them.</p>\n<p>But I was brought up as Kvothe. \u00a0My father once told me it meant &#8220;to know.&#8221;</p>\n<p>I have, of course, been called many other things. \u00a0Most of them uncouth, although very few were unearned.</p>\n<p>I have stolen princesses back from sleeping barrow kings. \u00a0I burned down the town of Trebon. \u00a0I have spent the night with Felurian and left with both my sanity and my life. \u00a0I was expelled from the University at a younger age than most people are allowed in. \u00a0I tread paths by moonlight that others fear to speak of during day. \u00a0I have talked to Gods, loved women, and written songs that make the minstrels weep.</p>\n<p>You may have heard of me.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Badass. \u00a0Anyway, one of the telltale bits of this series seems to be that there are many little bits of lore scattered about the book from legends of the world being built by Rothfuss. \u00a0Some are meant for foreshadowing. \u00a0Some are simply meant for entertainment. \u00a0All are interesting to me. \u00a0So, I&#8217;ve decided to copy some of those stories on to here in what is yet another series of posts on my blog.</p>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p>The first story is set in the Waystone Inn, the main setting of the whole shabang, and is being told by what appears to be the village storyteller, Old Cob.\u00a0 From the first couple pages of the book:</p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<blockquote><p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0&#8220;When he awoke, Taborlin the Great found himself locked in a high tower. \u00a0They had taken his sword and stripped him of his tools: key, coin, and candle were all gone. \u00a0But that weren&#8217;t even the worst of it you see&#8230;&#8221; Cob paused for effect, &#8220;&#8230;cause the lamps on the wall were burning blue!&#8221;</i></p></blockquote>\n</div>\n<blockquote>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>Graham, Jake, and Shep nodded to themselves. \u00a0The three friends had grown up together, listening to Cob&#8217;s stories and ignoring his advice.</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>Cob peered closely at the newer, more attentive members of his small audience, the smith&#8217;s prentice. \u00a0&#8220;Do you know what that meant, boy?&#8221; \u00a0Everyone called the smith&#8217;s prentice &#8220;boy&#8221; despite the fact that he was a hand (~4 inches) taller than anyone there. \u00a0Small towns being what they are, he would most likely remain &#8220;boy&#8221; until his beard filled out or he bloodied someone&#8217;s nose over the matter.</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>The boy gave a slow nod. \u00a0&#8220;The Chandrian.&#8221;</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;That&#8217;s right,&#8221; Cob said approvingly.\u00a0 &#8220;The Chandrian.\u00a0 Everyone knows that blue fire is one of their signs.\u00a0 Now he was\u2013&#8221;</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;But how&#8217;d they find him?&#8221; the boy interrupted.\u00a0 &#8220;And why din&#8217;t they kill him when they had the chance?&#8221;</i></p>\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<blockquote><p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;Hush now, you&#8217;ll get all the answers before the end,&#8221; Jake said.\u00a0 &#8220;Just let him tell it.&#8221;</i></p></blockquote>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><strong><i>\u2026.</i>skipping past some outer story exposition\u2026.</strong></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<blockquote><p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;Now Taborlin needed to escape, but when he looked around, he saw his cell had no door.\u00a0 No windows.\u00a0 All around him was nothing but smooth, hard stone.\u00a0 It was a cell no man had ever escaped.</i></p></blockquote>\n</div>\n<blockquote>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;But Taborlin knew the names of all things, and so all things were his to command.\u00a0 He said to the stone: &#8216;Break!&#8217; and the stone broke.\u00a0 The wall tore like a piece of paper, and through that hole Taborlin could see the sky and breathe the sweet spring air.\u00a0 He stepped to the edge, looked down, and without a second thought he stepped out into the open air\u2026.&#8221;</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>The boy&#8217;s eyes went wide. &#8220;He didn&#8217;t!&#8221;</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>Cob nodded seriously.\u00a0 &#8220;So Taborlin fell, but he did not despair.\u00a0 For he knew the name of the wind, and so the wind obeyed him.\u00a0 He spoke to the wind and it cradled and caressed him.\u00a0 It bore him to the ground as gently as a puff of thistledown and set him on his feet softly as a mother&#8217;s kiss.</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;And when he got to the ground and felt his side where they&#8217;d stabbed him, he saw that it weren&#8217;t hardly a scratch.\u00a0 Now maybe it was just a piece of luck,&#8221; Cob tapped the side of his nose knowingly. &#8220;Or maybe it had something to do with the amulet he was wearing under his shirt.&#8221;</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;What amulet?&#8221; the boy asked eagerly through a mouthful of stew.</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>Old Cob leaned back on his stool, glad for the chance to elaborate.\u00a0 &#8220;A few days earlier, Taborlin had met a tinker on the road.\u00a0 And even though Taborlin didn&#8217;t have much to eat, he shared his dinner with the old man.&#8221;</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;Right sensible thing to do,&#8221; Graham said to the boy. &#8220;Everyone knows: &#8216;A tinker pays for kindness twice.'&#8221;</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;No no,&#8221; Jake grumbled.\u00a0 &#8220;Get it right: &#8216;A tinker&#8217;s advice pays kindness twice.'&#8221;</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>The innkeeper spoke up for the first time that night.\u00a0 &#8220;Actually, you&#8217;re missing more than half,&#8221; he said, standing in the doorway behind the bar.</i></p>\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p><i>&#8220;A tinker&#8217;s debt is always paid:</i><i>Once for any simple trade.</i><i>Twice for freely-given aid.</i><i>Thrice for any insult made.&#8221;</i></p></blockquote>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><strong><i>\u2026.</i>skipping outer story exposition\u2026</strong></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<blockquote><p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>Old Cob nodded before he cleared his throat and launched back into the story.\u00a0 &#8220;Now this amulet was worth a whole bucket of gold nobles, but on account of Taborlin&#8217;s kindness, the tinker sold it to him for nothing but an iron penny, a copper penny, and a silver penny.\u00a0 It was black as a winter&#8217;s night and cold as ice to touch, but so long as it was around his neck, Taborlin would be safe from the harm of evil things.\u00a0 Demons and such.&#8221;</i></p></blockquote>\n</div>\n<blockquote>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;I&#8217;d give a good piece for such a thing these days,&#8221; Shep said darkly.\u00a0 He had drunk most and talked least over the course of the evening.\u00a0 Everyone knew that something bad had happened out on his farm last Cendling night, but since they were good friends they knew better than to press him for the details.\u00a0 At least not this early in the evening, not as sober as they were.</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;Aye, who wouldn&#8217;t?&#8221; Old Cob said judiciously, taking a long drink.</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;I din&#8217;t know the Chandrian were demons,&#8221; the boy said.\u00a0 &#8220;I&#8217;d heard\u2013&#8221;</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;They ain&#8217;t demons,&#8221; Jake said firmly.\u00a0 &#8220;They were the first six people to refuse Tehlu&#8217;s choice of the path, and he cursed them to wander the corners\u2013&#8221;</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>&#8220;Are you telling this story, Jacob Walker?&#8221; Cob said sharply.\u00a0 &#8220;Cause if you are, I&#8217;ll just let you get on with it.&#8221;</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>The two men glared at each other for a long moment.\u00a0 Eventually Jake looked away, muttering something that could, conceivably, have been an apology.</i></p>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>Cob turned back to the boy.\u00a0 &#8220;That&#8217;s the mystery of the Chandrian,&#8221; he explained.\u00a0 &#8220;Where do they come from?\u00a0 Where do they go after they&#8217;ve done their bloody deeds?\u00a0 Are they men who sold their souls? Demons? Spirits?\u00a0 No one knows.&#8221; Cob shot Jake a profoundly disdainful look.\u00a0 &#8220;Though every half-wit </i>claims<i> he knows\u2026&#8221;</i></p>\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<blockquote><p><i>\u00a0 \u00a0 \u00a0</i><i>The story fell further into bickering at this point, about the nature of the Chandrian, the signs that showed their presence to the wary, and whether the amulet would protect Taborlin from bandits, or mad dogs, or falling off a horse.\u00a0 Things were getting heated when the front door banged open.</i></p></blockquote>\n</div>\n<div class=\"p2\"></div>\n<div class=\"p1\">\n<p>I think that&#8217;s a good start. \u00a0Next time, whenever that is, the beginnings of this world&#8217;s belief in the god Tehlu.</p>\n</div>\n<div ado&#8230;</p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<h3 class=\"post-title entry-title\">Leaving Academia</h3>\n<div class=\"post-header\">\u00a0After reading\u00a0<a href=\"http://drdadphd.blogspot.com/2012/03/why-am-i-afraid-of-industry-job.html\">Dr. Dad&#8217;s post</a>\u00a0about industry, I was reminded of the whole agonizing will-I-be-an-academic struggle.\u00a0 Just like so many other bitter and disillusioned grad students who have been hit in the face with the Big Wet Dead Reality Fish.\u00a0 I&#8217;m sure I wrote about it at great length.\u00a0 However, at a distance of several years&#8217; worth of graduatin&#8217;, industry-workin&#8217;, and baby-wranglin&#8217;, here&#8217;s my summary:</div>\n<div id=\"post-body-4801261554612166548\" class=\"post-body entry-content\">\n<p><b>The Five Stages Of Academic Disillusionment</b></p>\n<ol>\n<li><b>Relentless Optimism<i>.\u00a0\u00a0</i></b>I will get an academic, tenure-track job when I graduate!\u00a0 I am smart enough, I am good enough, and everyone will love me!\u00a0 I&#8217;ll be such a good teacher!</li>\n<li><b>Great Expectations</b>. Everyone else who\u00a0<i>didn&#8217;t\u00a0</i>get an academic job just wasn&#8217;t working hard enough!\u00a0\u00a0<i>I\u00a0\u00a0</i>will graduate in\u00a0<i>four</i>\u00a0years because I&#8217;m better than all of them. (Note: People who are not jerks tend to skip this stage in favor of clinical depression.)</li>\n<li><b>Reality Fish.\u00a0</b>Damn, I finally read the NSF statistics.\u00a0 I&#8217;m never going to get an academic job.\u00a0 I&#8217;m never going to graduate.\u00a0 I&#8217;m not sure I&#8217;m ever leaving this damn lab.\u00a0 Shoot me now.\u00a0 Also, what the fuck does doing research have to do with a SLAC teaching job?\u00a0 Bastards.</li>\n<li><b>Solipsistic Agony.\u00a0\u00a0</b>Is there any good outside of academia?\u00a0 Will I be a miserable, useless failure if I cannot live up to my own ideals?</li>\n<li><b>Money Money Money.</b>\u00a0Hey!\u00a0 Real jobs pay&#8230;. real money.\u00a0 Suddenly this looks much more attractive\u00a0 See you later, academia.\u00a0 Don&#8217;t let the door hit you&#8230;</li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-18T03:10:29", "date_gmt": "2012-09-25T03:07:41", "_links": {"wp:term": [{"href": "taxonomy": "post_tag"}], "curies": [{"href": "https://api.w.org/{rel}", "name": "wp", "templated": true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/111"}], "version-history": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/111/revisions"}], "collection": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts"}], "wp:featuredmedia": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media/113", "embeddable": true}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=111", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": here:\u00a0http://naturalscientist.blogspot.com/2012/05/leaving-academia.html Now, without further ado&#8230;</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [41, 31, 26, 42, 22], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=111"}, "id": 111, "title": {"rendered": "On Leaving Academia"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-18T03:10:29", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "on-leaving-academia", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 107, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/exploring-buddhism-pt-1/", "date": "2012-09-23T02:57:54", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p><a href=\"http://yoga-boston.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/08/buddha_yoga.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://images-blogger-opensocial.googleusercontent.com/gadgets/proxy?url=http%3A%2F%2Fyoga-boston.com%2Fwp-content%2Fuploads%2F2012%2F08%2Fbuddha_yoga.jpg&amp;container=blogger&amp;gadget=a&amp;rewriteMime=image%2F*\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"240\" border=\"0\" data-orig-src=\"http://yoga-boston.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/08/buddha_yoga.jpg\" /></a></p>\n<p>I was sitting around in my apartment today thinking about how I haven&#8217;t updated my blog in about 2 months and felt guilty about it, especially since one of my coworkers called me out on it on Friday. He was right too, I&#8217;ve been super lazy regarding this blog. \u00a0So, inspired the 6 (7?) fat and happy little buddhas that I&#8217;ve used to decorate my bathroom, I&#8217;ve decided today to look up some information regarding something that&#8217;s always interested me a little bit: Buddhism.</p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<p>Buddhism is interesting in many ways, one of which regards its nature as a philosophy as opposed to the religion that people tend to think that it is. \u00a0This philosophy stems from the alleged teachings and life of Siddhartha Gautama. \u00a0This installment will delve into a bit of the history of Gautama, courtesy of our good friends\u00a0<a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddha#Conception_and_birth\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Wikipedia</a>\u00a0and Google. \u00a0Mind you, I&#8217;m trying to keep this history portion relatively short:</p>\n<p>Siddhartha Gautama was born into ancient Indian royalty and lived the life of a prince in his early years. \u00a0When he was born, it was predicted that he would become a great king or a great sage. \u00a0His father, King Shuddodana, hoping for his son to become a great king, shielded Siddhartha from anything that might result in him taking up the religious life. \u00a0Thus, Siddhartha was isolated in various palaces during his early life <i>[I take it they were quite wealthy]</i>, sheltered from experiencing those of old age, disease, death, or the religious (then Hindu) path. \u00a0As he grew older, he became increasingly curious of life outside of the palace walls. Eventually, he demanded that he be permitted to venture beyond them.</p>\n<p>Still hoping to keep his son from realizing the truth of suffering and decay, the king arranged it so that Siddhartha would be introduced to the world via a parade, demanding that only the young and healthy appear. \u00a0However, two old men happened to wander into view on his parade route. \u00a0Amazed and confused at their appearance, he followed them to find out what their deal was. \u00a0In doing so, he came across people riddled with illness. \u00a0Finally he came across a funeral and for the first time in his life saw death. \u00a0Asking one of his staff for assistance in understanding these things, he learned that many people get sick, and all grow old and die. \u00a0Apparently he was REALLY sheltered.</p>\n<p><a href=\"http://webspace.ship.edu/cgboer/buddha8.gif\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://images-blogger-opensocial.googleusercontent.com/gadgets/proxy?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwebspace.ship.edu%2Fcgboer%2Fbuddha8.gif&amp;container=blogger&amp;gadget=a&amp;rewriteMime=image%2F*\" alt=\"\" border=\"0\" data-orig-src=\"http://webspace.ship.edu/cgboer/buddha8.gif\" /></a>At\u00a0the age of 29 he denounced wealth and luxury as the path to happiness, and sought to explore other methods for attaining it. \u00a0He left his palace, gave away his personal possessions, cut his hair, abandoned his wife and child, and set on his way. \u00a0He began to practice the austerities and self-mortifications practiced by a group of Hindu ascetics. \u00a0They tried to find Enlightenment through the self-deprivation of worldly goods, including food beyond what was absolutely necessary (<a href=\"http://www.letusreason.org/buddh2.htm\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">some say</a> a single grain of rice per day). \u00a0He eventually took it so far that he brought himself near a state of death, without feeling any closer to Enlightenment.</p>\n<p>Realizing that these extreme practices would not get him toward Enlightenment and the understanding, and ending, of suffering, he accepted food from a peasant girl that happened to be passing by. \u00a0He then decided to devote himself to the Middle Way: a path of moderation between the extremes of self-indulgence and self-mortification.</p>\n<p>Following this redirection, Gautama sat under a Bodhi tree, where he vowed to never arise until he had achieved enlightenment <i>[ed\u2013 How is this a middle ground between indulgence and self-mortification exactly?]</i>. \u00a0He sat there for many days, first in deep concentration to free himself of distraction, then in mindful meditation, opening himself up to the truth of [<i>apparently</i>] the Universe. \u00a0It was during this period that he attained Enlightenment.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"http://i0.wp.com/media.trb.com/media/photo/2010-04/53135921.jpg?resize=600%2C337\" alt=\"\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p>The accounts of this flash of personal insight are a bit&#8230;scattered and conflicting. \u00a0<a href=\"http://online.sfsu.edu/rone/Buddhism/footsteps.htm\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Some</a> accounts claim that he sat there for a mere night and in the morning attained enlightenment. \u00a0<a href=\"http://www.ascensiongateway.com/quotes/buddha/biography.htm\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Others</a> claim that the timescale for meditation was 49 days and 49 nights. \u00a0Others still claim that it was some <a href=\"http://webspace.ship.edu/cgboer/siddhartha.html\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">non-specific amount of time</a>\u00a0[<i>if I ever used &#8220;many days&#8221; in a paper it&#8217;d never be published</i>]. \u00a0Then of course there&#8217;s the <a href=\"http://www.letusreason.org/buddh2.htm\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">claims</a> of <a href=\"http://online.sfsu.edu/rone/Buddhism/footsteps.htm\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">encounters</a> with <a href=\"http://webspace.ship.edu/cgboer/siddhartha.html\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">some &#8220;evil one&#8221; named Mara</a>, who tried to tempt Siddhartha to quit with the pleasures of the world, and then the fears of the world, and finally fears of the supernatural.</p>\n<p>Regardless, he arose from the tree as the historical Buddha, with knowledge of the truth of the suffering of the world, as well as the way in which one can escape the endless cycle of birth, life (suffering), death, and rebirth known as <a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samsara\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">samsara</a>. \u00a0He realized the Four Noble Truths, the Noble Eightfold Path, The Four Immeasurables, and the Middle Way, amongst others. \u00a0He spent the rest of his life spreading his teachings to wherever he journeyed. \u00a0Here&#8217;s an introduction to those bits that I just mentioned (to be explored later if I don&#8217;t drop off the face of the Earth again). \u00a0Forgive me for omitting accent marks. \u00a0I don&#8217;t feel like putting them in:</p>\n<p><strong>The Four Noble Truths</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li>The truth of dukkha (birth, suffering, illness, aging, death)</li>\n<li>The truth of the origin of dukkha: craving of worldly desires</li>\n<li>The truth of the cessation of dukkha: giving up craving these desires (simple right?)</li>\n<li>The truth of the Eightfold Path as the way to the cessation of dukkha</li>\n</ul>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p><a href=\"http://buddhistblog.files.wordpress.com/2010/02/eightfoldpath11.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://images-blogger-opensocial.googleusercontent.com/gadgets/proxy?url=http%3A%2F%2Fbuddhistblog.files.wordpress.com%2F2010%2F02%2Feightfoldpath11.jpg&amp;container=blogger&amp;gadget=a&amp;rewriteMime=image%2F*\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"207\" border=\"0\" data-orig-src=\"http://buddhistblog.files.wordpress.com/2010/02/eightfoldpath11.jpg\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong>The Noble Eightfold Path</strong></p>\n<p><i>Prajna &#8211; The wisdom that purifies the mind, allowing it to attain spiritual insight into the nature of all things</i></p>\n<ul>\n<li>The right view (ditthi): viewing reality as it is, not just as it appears to be.</li>\n<li>The right intention (sankappa): intention of renunciation, freedom, and harmlessness.</li>\n</ul>\n<p><i>Sila &#8211; The ethics or morality, or abstention from unwholesome deeds</i></p>\n<ul>\n<li>The right speech (vaca): speaking in a truthful and non-hurtful way</li>\n<li>The right action (kammanta): acting in a non-harmful way</li>\n<li>The right livelihood (ajiva): a non-harmful livelihood</li>\n</ul>\n<p><i>Samadhi &#8211; The mental discipline required to develop mastery over one&#8217;s own mind. \u00a0This is done through the practice of various contemplative and meditative practices</i></p>\n<ul>\n<li>The right effort (vayama): making an effort to improve</li>\n<li>The right mindfulness (sati): awareness to see things for what they are with clear consciousness (<i>how is this different from #1?</i>)</li>\n<li>The right concentration (samadhi): correct meditation or concentration</li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong>The Four Immeasurables</strong></p>\n<p>In short: love, compassion, joy, and equanimity. In longer, prayer form:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>May all sentient beings have happiness and its causes [<i>love</i>]</li>\n<li>May all sentient beings be free of suffering and its causes [<i>compassion?</i>]</li>\n<li>May all sentient beings never be separated from bliss without suffering [<i>joy</i>]</li>\n<li>May all sentient beings be in equanimity, free of bias, attachment, and anger [<i>it&#8217;s right there</i>]</li>\n</ul>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p><strong>The Middle Way</strong></p>\n<p>As previously mentioned, the path between the extremes of self-indulgence and austerity. If you ask me, it seems to be skewed more toward the austere, but I&#8217;m no buddhist scholar.</p>\n<p>More on this topic later (hence the Pt 1 up top).</p>\n<p>Some refs outside Wikipedia:</p>\n<p><a href=\"http://webspace.ship.edu/cgboer/siddhartha.html\">http://webspace.ship.edu/cgboer/siddhartha.html<br />\n</a><a href=\"http://www.buddhanet.net/e-learning/5minbud.htm\">http://www.buddhanet.net/e-learning/5minbud.htm<br />\n</a><a href=\"http://online.sfsu.edu/rone/Buddhism/footsteps.htm\">http://online.sfsu.edu/rone/Buddhism/footsteps.htm<br />\n</a><a href=\"http://www.ascensiongateway.com/quotes/buddha/biography.htm\">http://www.ascensiongateway.com/quotes/buddha/biography.htm<br />\n</a><a href=\"http://www.letusreason.org/buddh2.htm\">http://www.letusreason.org/buddh2.htm</a></p>\n<p><i>I should of course mention as always that this is not a definitive source of information. \u00a0Whatever you see above here does not reflect on Buddhism. \u00a0This is the hurried compilation of bits of information found scattered about the first few pages of Google searches such as &#8220;Buddhism&#8221;, &#8220;Siddhartha Gautama Biography&#8221;, and such. \u00a0Seriously, I am no philosophical scholar. \u00a0Don&#8217;t take anything that I say as any sort of golden truth. \u00a0My view of right and wrong flickers like a flame in the wind.</i></p>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-18T03:06:32", "date_gmt": "2012-09-23T02:57:54", "_links": {"wp:term": [{"href": "taxonomy": "post_tag"}], "curies": [{"href": "https://api.w.org/{rel}", "name": "wp", "templated": true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/106"}], "version-history": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/106/revisions"}], "collection": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts"}], "wp:featuredmedia": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media/107", "embeddable": true}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=106", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/users/1", "embeddable": true}], "wp:attachment": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media?parent=106"}], "about": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/types/post"}]}, "excerpt": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>I was sitting around in my apartment today thinking about how I haven&#8217;t updated my blog in about 2 months and felt guilty about it, especially since one of my coworkers called me out on it on Friday. He was right too, I&#8217;ve been super lazy regarding this blog. \u00a0So, inspired the 6 (7?) fat [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [40, 31, 26, 2, 32], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=106"}, "id": 106, "title": {"rendered": "Exploring Buddhism &#8211; Pt 1"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-18T03:06:32", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "exploring-buddhism-pt-1", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 101, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/thoughts-on-mediocrity/", "date": "2012-07-24T02:47:50", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p><a href=\"http://i1.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/gully_foyle.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-101\" src=\"http://i1.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/gully_foyle.jpg?resize=300%2C340\" alt=\"You pigs, you. You rut like pigs, is all. You got the most in you, and you use the least. You hear me, you? Got a million in you and spend pennies. Got a genius in you and think crazies. Got a heart in you and feel empties. All a you. Every you\u2026 \u2026Take a war to make you spend. Take a jam to make you think. Take a challenge to make you great.
