"<p>Within the last seven days, my life has encountered two major milestones: &#8211; I took the longest, most intense, high-stress exam in my life thus far\u2014the Qualifying Exam. &#8211; Two days later, I found out the results of that exam. I passed, apparently without a bit of of debate. \u00a0I officially became Nicholas Hunt-Walker, Master [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [13, 35, 36, 31, 26, 29, 2], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=67"}, "id": 67, "title": {"rendered": "Experiences With Impostor Syndrome"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-18T02:04:18", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "experiences-with-impostor-syndrome", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 65, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/you-must-balance-your-yin-and-your-yang/", "date": "2012-06-14T01:21:39", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Z730IPIwFyQ/TrApK5OtP-I/AAAAAAAAAKo/PGos4GtYMx0/s1600/Taijitu_Sun_and_Moon.png\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Z730IPIwFyQ/TrApK5OtP-I/AAAAAAAAAKo/PGos4GtYMx0/s1600/Taijitu_Sun_and_Moon.png\" alt=\"\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>Ever since I can first remember recognizing the yin-yang symbol, I&#8217;ve been interested in it. \u00a0When it was first introduced to me so very many years ago, its symbolism simply meant a balance between darkness and light, where within each there is exists a small part of the other. \u00a0No darkness without light, and vice versa. \u00a0I always had the impression that somehow, through bringing balance to one&#8217;s yin and yang, one achieves internal peace, though I never quite understood why.</p>\n<p>Well, even without any actual deeper understanding of the symbol, I&#8217;ve managed to doodle some version of this little guy on pretty much every notebook that I&#8217;ve had, as well as on homework assignments, chalkboards, whiteboards&#8211;pretty much on every surface that I can find to write on. \u00a0Deciding to have more than just a superficial association with it, I&#8217;ve taken some time to do bits of research here and there about it (read: looked at the same few Wikipedia articles again and again), read a bit of the <a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/Tao-Te-Ching-Lao-Tzu/dp/1613822421/ref=sr_1_2?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1339690998&amp;sr=8-2\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Dao de Jing</a> (didn&#8217;t really understand it; need to read it again), and have looked into more of the philosophy behind the yin-yang. \u00a0Much of what follows\u00a0will be personal conjecture/opinion, so if you have your own opinion, feel free to leave a comment and we can have a discussion! \u00a0Here&#8217;s some of what I&#8217;ve gotten so far (again, Wikipedia heavy!)</p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<div class=\"\">\n<p>The Yin and the Yang refer to more than just specifically darkness and light\u2014they represent complimentary yet polar opposites in nature: female/male, darkness/light, low/high, cold/hot, water/fire, earth/air, birth/death, etc. \u00a0Through their interaction, the world (meaning not just the Earth, but the Universe in its entirety) exists as we see it (<a href=\"http://taoism.about.com/od/thefiveelements/p/Five_Element.htm\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">the five elements</a> and <a href=\"http://taoism.about.com/od/daojiadaojiao/a/daojia.htm\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">ten thousand things</a>) and made whole. \u00a0Male and female produce new life, darkness and light produce our cycle of days, cold and heat produce the range of temperatures that make life sustainable, etc etc.</p>\n</div>\n<figure style=\"width: 260px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img class=\"\" src=\"http://i2.wp.com/usercontent1.hubimg.com/7897866_f260.jpg?resize=260%2C261\" alt=\"\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">The 5 elements (fire, earth, metal, water, wood) and their associations</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Out of these comes the concept of bringing balance to the world, both internal and external to oneself. \u00a0The way that it works\u00a0(I think)\u00a0is that the yin and yang represent the balance that the world <i>should</i> possess. \u00a0Note that that&#8217;s not really making a moral statement in the sense that action X is intrinsically bad or intrinsically good. \u00a0Instead, if you were to attach any sort of moral code to this, it&#8217;d be that actions should strive to move toward and maintain balance throughout the world and balance within oneself. \u00a0It is through that balance, then, that one achieves what is Good. The two eternal partners lie within a circle, which itself <a href=\"http://taoism.about.com/b/2008/04/02/the-yin-yang-symbol.htm\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">apparently represents the Tao (or Dao)</a>. \u00a0I just learned of this today while reading about it! \u00a0It&#8217;s interesting, because I&#8217;ve never once actually noticed the circle being as a distinct component of the whole symbol. I just always took it for granted as being a part of the symbol itself and that the yin and yang together make a circular figure. \u00a0This is even more interesting to me, as the tao itself (as I have interpreted it) is at its base naturally that way: it&#8217;s not a distinct part of the world, it simply represents everything that is. \u00a0Here we have the same trend\u2014the circle isn&#8217;t really a distinct part of the symbol. \u00a0It simply just IS the symbol, within which yin and yang dance their way through creation and destruction.</p>\n<table class=\"tr-caption-container\" cellspacing=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" align=\"center\">\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td><a href=\"http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Bagua-name-later.svg/275px-Bagua-name-later.svg.png\"><img src=\"https://images-blogger-opensocial.googleusercontent.com/gadgets/proxy?url=http%3A%2F%2Fupload.wikimedia.org%2Fwikipedia%2Fcommons%2Fthumb%2F2%2F2e%2FBagua-name-later.svg%2F275px-Bagua-name-later.svg.png&amp;container=blogger&amp;gadget=a&amp;rewriteMime=image%2F*\" alt=\"\" border=\"0\" data-orig-src=\"http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Bagua-name-later.svg/275px-Bagua-name-later.svg.png\" /></a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td class=\"tr-caption\"><i>The taijitu/yin-yang and ba gua</i></td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<p>Accompanying the yin and yang are 8 trigrams composed of solid and broken lines called the Ba Gua. \u00a0\u00a0 In all the years that I spent drawing yin-yangs on various media, I never once suspected that it had partners. \u00a0However it does, and I first noticed the existence of these trigrams while watching the popular anime series <a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naruto\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Naruto</a>. \u00a0To be briefish about it, Naruto is a story about <a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ninja\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">ninjas</a>, friendship, and the turbulent, militaristic world within which they all live. \u00a0Within this world, there are adults and kids practicing various types of jutsu (ninja-related martial arts and what is essentially magic) of which there are three types: <b>ninjutsu</b> (the tangible &#8220;magic&#8221; component to the series utilizing one&#8217;s internal energy, or their chakra, to manifest changes in the physical world), <b>genjutsu</b> (types of mind control that, while not tangible, are still quite devastating), and <b>taijutsu</b> (various styles of hand-to-hand combat). \u00a0Amongst the taijutsu users there are two general schools: Strong Fist users (most people) and Gentle Fist users (a very select group). \u00a0Strong Fist users employ hard punches, kicks, and other physical techniques with the purpose of causing great external, visible damage (e.g. broken bones, dislocated joints, knock outs). \u00a0Conversely, Gentle Fist users practice what looks like combative Tai Chi, and use a combination of precise, flowing, open-hand strikes and focused amounts of chakra to cause great internal damage (e.g. damaging internal organs, blood flow, chakra flow).</p>\n<figure style=\"width: 320px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><img src=\"https://images-blogger-opensocial.googleusercontent.com/gadgets/proxy?url=http%3A%2F%2Fimages1.wikia.nocookie.net%2F__cb20090428130858%2Fnaruto%2Fimages%2Fthumb%2F1%2F16%2FNeji.PNG%2F586px-Neji.PNG&amp;container=blogger&amp;gadget=a&amp;rewriteMime=image%2F*\" alt=\"\" width=\"320\" height=\"239\" border=\"0\" data-orig-src=\"http://images1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20090428130858/naruto/images/thumb/1/16/Neji.PNG/586px-Neji.PNG\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Hyuuga Neji about to start Eight Trigrams Sixty-Four Palms aka Hakke Rokujuuyonshou</figcaption></figure>\n<p>One of the Gentle Fist users, Hyuuga Neji, is an adept at Tai Chi and developed a technique called the Eight Trigrams Sixty-Four Palms technique (<i>Hakke Rokujuuyonshou</i>). \u00a0When he performs this technique, a projection of the taijitu and ba gua appears beneath him, and if his target is within the range encompassed by that circle he proceeds to thoroughly rock their shit (<a href=\"http://youtu.be/57XY93oOLac?t=6s\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">it really is quite lovely to watch</a>). \u00a0Forgive the digression.</p>\n<p>Anyway, I saw that a few times and I thought to myself, &#8220;huh, that&#8217;s interesting. \u00a0What are those symbols around that yin-yang? \u00a0Is that some taoist thing?&#8221; \u00a0From there I abused Google, as is my nature, and through various jumps of topics found out quite a bit which I had not known before.</p>\n<p>I first found out that these symbols were called the ba gua. \u00a0I further found that the\u00a0symbols each had names and that these names had different associations depending on the system with which you&#8217;re defining your taijitu+ba gua combination. \u00a0The one seen above is the King Wen (Later Heaven) system, while the other one that I know of (all praise and honor is to Wikipedia) is the Fuxi (Earlier Heaven) system. \u00a0<a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ba_gua\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">According to <b>TRI</b>gram), where each part is <a href=\"http://www.nationsonline.org/oneworld/Chinese_Customs/bagua.htm\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">a broken (representing yin) or solid (yang) line</a>. \u00a0Here, we see where the various combinations of yin and yang producing the different components of nature, people, and existence in general. \u00a0Why it&#8217;s only 3 lines per ba gua symbol is beyond me, but that&#8217;s the way it&#8217;s done. \u00a0Maybe as I read more about this and taoism (which is another article in and of itself), I&#8217;ll learn why.</p>\n<p>On top of all of THAT, the eight trigrams can be configured together into 64 more combinations called hexagrams (probably why the technique is called Eight Trigrams 64 Palms Technique, but I digress), each representing a different philosophical concept. \u00a0I won&#8217;t list them all here, but I will provide a link (<a href=\"http://www.iching123.com/64_hexagrams_chart_text.htm\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">link</a>). \u00a0Together with the ba gua and the taijitu, you have all of life, the Universe, and everything.</p>\n<p>I think that I&#8217;ll end this already-lengthy article right here, as I&#8217;ve hit what I consider to be the major points of what I&#8217;ve learned about yin and yang. \u00a0In the future, I hope to explore more about these symbols, the various ba gua configurations, taoism, and zen in general. \u00a0Maybe, with all of these at my back, I can move one step closer towards true understanding of existence and She was a friend to all who crossed her path, and held great expectations in her heart for all her progeny. Grandma, I hope that I&#8217;ve begun to become as great as you thought I could be, and I hope you know that whenever I have grits and cheese, I&#8217;m gonna think of you (and know that I couldn&#8217;t ever make it better than you). I&#8217;ll continue to try to make your name a proud one, through my achievements and even through my failures. Rest in Peace, Tomannie Walker. Your work is done. Ours has only begun.</span></p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<div data-blogger-escaped-style=\"text-align: -webkit-auto;\">\n<p>I had that up as my Facebook status today, but I wanted to use this space to talk a little bit more about it (and take a break from writing this PowerPoint Presentation).</p>\n</div>\n<div data-blogger-escaped-style=\"text-align: -webkit-auto;\">\n<p>I&#8217;ve been talking about this with my lifelong friends today, and I actually made a comment continuing my thought process for the day on that status. \u00a0In reply to\u00a0<span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">&#8220;</span><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">You are a good grandson. But I already know that you are a good man!&#8221;</span><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">:</span></p>\n</div>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p><span style=\"color: #333333; font-family: 'lucida grande', tahoma, verdana, arial, sans-serif;\">Am I either though? I&#8217;m not saying I&#8217;m not, I&#8217;m just generally questioning it. And further I wonder if I&#8217;m the type of person my ancestors (in general) would approve of being in their lineage. If they were to see me on a daily basis interacting with people, working, during my leisure hours, would they think &#8220;seeing this makes all that struggle, all that sweat blood and tears, worth it&#8221;</span></p></blockquote>\n<p>I still wonder that, you know? \u00a0Not that I&#8217;m trying to fulfill the dreams of anyone else\u2014no no, I live my life for me. \u00a0However, I come from a long long line of people (as do we all, no?) and many of those people (I presume?) went through some high atrocities. \u00a0Every generation before mine had to face varying degrees of racism and discrimination, whether it was the racial tension of the 50&#8217;s &#8211; 70&#8217;s, or suffering through Jim Crow, or on a plantation somewhere in the South or in Barbados. \u00a0Would they look at myself and my brother, the current torch bearers for our lineage, and smile? \u00a0I would hope so. \u00a0Granted, I know that I could do better with my life. \u00a0And I know my grandmother enough to know that she&#8217;d push me to do better as well, but she&#8217;d also acknowledge my journey and be happy that I&#8217;ve managed to find happiness.</p>\n<p>My other grandmother would be proud too, but to a point. \u00a0She&#8217;d definitely hate (I&#8217;m sorry, <i>strongly dislike</i>)\u00a0that I&#8217;m atheist, and that I curse as much as I do. \u00a0But, even with that, she&#8217;d like that I&#8217;m pursuing my passions, or at least I&#8217;d like to think so.</p>\n<p>This brings me to my next thought, another point that I was discussing with my boys: when it comes right down to it I really don&#8217;t know all that much about my family, or how they&#8217;d feel about the choices I&#8217;ve made. \u00a0I&#8217;ve only been able to guess at what their opinions would be. \u00a0If they were all to tragically die in a fire right now that also managed to burn all the records we have, I&#8217;d only be able to piece together bits of their lives that I&#8217;ve managed to remember. \u00a0I know a fair bit about my father&#8217;s struggles in his younger days (i.e., my current age), but there was a lot that was glossed over that I know nothing about. \u00a0I know even less about my mother&#8217;s early life. \u00a0I think I might add a couple things to the ol&#8217; resolutions list:</p>\n<p>\u2022 Talk to family members about their lives in detail, so that you can carry the torch properly. \u00a0Get a feel for their likes, their dislikes, their triumphs, and more importantly their failures. \u00a0Learn as much as they have to offer, because they won&#8217;t be around forever.</p>\n<p>And neither will I, so maybe I should get my story straight too. \u00a0Maybe I should first make sure it&#8217;s a story worth telling.</p>\n<p>I think it is.</p>\n<p>More on this at another time.</p>\n<p>Peace</p>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-18T01:20:56", "date_gmt": "2012-02-09T01:13:23", "_links": {"wp:term": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/categories?post=57", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "category"}, {"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/tags?post=57", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "post_tag"}], "curies": [{"href": "https://api.w.org/{rel}", "name": "wp", "templated": true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/57"}], "version-history": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/57/revisions"}], "collection": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts"}], "wp:attachment": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media?parent=57"}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=57", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/users/1", "embeddable": true}], "about": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/types/post"}]}, "excerpt": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>***Disclaimer: This was written in one go, so it&#8217;s probably pretty bad. \u00a0But, I&#8217;m not correcting it. \u00a0So it goes!*** 10 years ago today, one of the greatest women I&#8217;ve had the pleasure to know died. She was a friend to all who crossed her path, and held great expectations in her heart for all [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [26, 2, 28, 30], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=57"}, "id": 57, "title": {"rendered": "10 Years Ago, Today"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-18T01:20:56", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "10-years-ago-today", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 54, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/we-are-the-tas/", "date": "2012-01-30T05:32:18", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-0jioNJ1eWFQ/TybBYUpH4mI/AAAAAAAAAFY/nfMcY-KV3Lw/s1600/unclesam.jpg\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-0jioNJ1eWFQ/TybBYUpH4mI/AAAAAAAAAFY/nfMcY-KV3Lw/s320/unclesam.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"240\" height=\"320\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<div>\n<p>We are the TA&#8217;s.</p>\n<p>We are on the front lines, providing the buffer between the misunderstandings and confusions of the students, and the lack of coherent notes by the professors. We take knowledge from on high, and attempt to partition and filter it down so that it can be palatable for the masses. \u00a0We are Prometheus, stealing the fire of knowledge from the gods of the ivory tower, and giving it to man so that man may enrich its own life.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>We are the damage control. \u00a0We pick up the pieces that have been produced by waves of information crashing against the beachhead of people in the lecture hall. \u00a0We put these pieces back together as best we can, like an incomplete puzzle. \u00a0We tease the signal out of the noise.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>We are the TA&#8217;s!</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>And we rock the god damn HOUSE!</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>HOO RAH!</p>\n</div>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-18T01:20:50", "date_gmt": "2012-01-30T05:32:18", "_links": {"wp:term": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/categories?post=53", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "category"}, {"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/tags?post=53", "embeddable": true, "taxonomy": "post_tag"}], "curies": [{"href": "https://api.w.org/{rel}", "name": "wp", "templated": true}], "self": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/53"}], "version-history": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts/53/revisions"}], "collection": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/posts"}], "wp:featuredmedia": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media/54", "embeddable": true}], "replies": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/comments?post=53", "embeddable": true}], "author": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/users/1", "embeddable": true}], "wp:attachment": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/media?parent=53"}], "about": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/types/post"}]}, "excerpt": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>We are the TA&#8217;s. We are on the front lines, providing the buffer between the misunderstandings and confusions of the students, and the lack of coherent notes by the professors. We take knowledge from on high, and attempt to partition and filter it down so that it can be palatable for the masses. \u00a0We are [&hellip;]</p>\n"}, "categories": [1], "tags": [29, 2, 16, 19], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=53"}, "id": 53, "title": {"rendered": "We Are The TA&#8217;s!"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-18T01:20:50", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "we-are-the-tas", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 50, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/capoeira-na-roda-capoera-na-vida-part-i-no-inicio-com-os-guerreiros/", "date": "2012-01-25T05:27:46", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-7QQqIxIrmV8/Tx2AnzZl9eI/AAAAAAAAAEE/zVc62h7llXE/s1600/capoeiralogos.png\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-7QQqIxIrmV8/Tx2AnzZl9eI/AAAAAAAAAEE/zVc62h7llXE/s400/capoeiralogos.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"400\" height=\"160\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p class=\"separator\">In about a week and a half it will have been 2 years since I first began to practice capoeira. \u00a0It&#8217;s amazing that this activity has become such a large part of my life, especially considering how before that moment I hadn&#8217;t thought about capoeira outside of <a href=\"http://youtu.be/yhp-TyRJGUc\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">video games</a> and <a href=\"http://youtu.be/iQzT7CHHVEk\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">movies</a>. \u00a0Even then, while I thought it looked cool, I only really thought of it as sort of a quaint novelty. \u00a0Knowing absolutely nothing about the style, I had thought it impractical for real-world fighting scenarios, and entirely too filled with unnecessary movements to be useful before the practitioner exhausted himself. \u00a0Then came February of 2010.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><!--more--></p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-doGvoEZCWW8/TyOX779QIfI/AAAAAAAAAFA/lm64Wfj7sm4/s1600/capoeiraguerreiroslogo.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-doGvoEZCWW8/TyOX779QIfI/AAAAAAAAAFA/lm64Wfj7sm4/s200/capoeiraguerreiroslogo.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"200\" height=\"200\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p class=\"separator\" data-blogger-escaped-style=\"clear: both; text-align: -webkit-auto;\">Between the fall of 2009 and summer of 2010 I had been employed at Columbia University as a post-baccalaureate student in the department of Astronomy. \u00a0Late into the fall of 2009, I had broken up with my girlfriend at the time (who I&#8217;m with now) and had since found someone else that had captured my interest. \u00a0I would make any excuse that I could to spend time with her, if only to keep myself on her mind and maybe find a way to capture her interest. \u00a0Heh, I&#8217;ve never really been good at the whole &#8220;courting&#8221; thing, so that was the only strategy that I had. \u00a0Anyway, one of the ways, that I would try to spend time with her was to go to the gym with her twice per week. \u00a0The Columbia gym (the Dodge Fitness Center) is an indoor gym extending underground, with several facilities, individual workout rooms, and an indoor track which tours the upper level of the complex and passes some of the aforementioned workout rooms.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">Once inside the gym, we&#8217;d go our separate ways but we&#8217;d meet up after our respective workouts to jog around for a bit on the track. \u00a0About two years ago on a Tuesday at the beginning of February (2/2/2010 in fact), we had been jogging around the track when my ears picked up on the sound of drums. \u00a0Being the black man that I am, the drums stirred something within me, compelling me to follow their sound back to their source. \u00a0So, I said to my lovely companion, &#8220;hey, drums! \u00a0Wanna see where they&#8217;re coming from?&#8221; \u00a0She complied, and we proceeded toward one of the workout rooms in the back. \u00a0As we approached, I peered through the glass window and saw people dressed in all white with their shoes off, some with colorful ropes around their waists, performing those same movements that I had seen in video games and movies so long ago; the movements of capoeira.</p>\n<p>As we stood outside the door to the room and watched, one of the capoeiristas came over and beckoned us to join them inside. \u00a0Apparently this was their first class of the semester, and was serving as an introductory class for those that were interested. \u00a0As such, the class was split up: on the left side of the room were the newbies (dressed in whatever workout clothes they were wearing) and on the right side were the people who had been there before (most of which were wearing all-white with various colored cords around their waists). \u00a0So, we drifted over to the left side of the class and ran through a few of the basic movements. \u00a0We learned how to perform and pronunce the names of ginga (everyone looks stupid when they begin. \u00a0I still look pretty stupid), martelo, meia lua de frente, esquiva de frente, esquiva lateral, negativa, rol\u00ea, and a\u00fa. \u00a0None of this was easy to do, and I really hated looking like a doofus in front of the girl I was interested in, as well as in general, but it was definitely fun.</p>\n<p>Toward the end of class, everyone in the room joined up into a large circle. \u00a0The instructor, Contramestre George Palmares, briefly spoke to us (I forget about what) and then began to start what I would later come to know as the <i>roda</i>. \u00a0Some instruments were brought out in addition to the drum that was out before, and some of the students left the circle to man those instruments. \u00a0These were the <a href=\"http://www.colorado.edu/StudentGroups/CapoeiraAngola/berimbau.gif\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">berimbau</a>, <a href=\"http://www.sultansound.com/pandeiro.jpg\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">pandeiro</a>, and the <a href=\"http://www.gope.net/Produtos/AtabaqueCordas.jpg\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">atabaque</a>, comprising the basic components of the\u00a0<i><a href=\"http://www.ele-mental.org/capoeira/TABCAT/images/TABCATroda0411-bateria.jpg\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">bateria</a>, </i>or the percussion band that commands the roda (other instruments include, but are not limited to: the <a href=\"http://www.expobrazil.com/en/fotos/prd2132.jpg\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">agogo</a>\u00a0and the <a href=\"http://www.start-playing-capoeira.com/images/Reco-Reco-Parts.jpg\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">reco-reco</a>). \u00a0Then the bateria began to play. \u00a0The music began with the odd, rhythmic <i>twang</i> of the single-stringed berimbau. \u00a0This was joined by the pandeiro, whose mini-cymbals filled the room with a light-hearted shake, punctuated every so often with an abrupt SLAP upon its center. \u00a0Bringing up the rear was the atabaque, whose bass and hypnotic sound filled the room and moved my soul.</p>\n<p>Once the instruments had started up, capoeiristas around the roda began to clap 1-2-3, 1-2-3, led by the rhythm strung out on the berimbau. \u00a0As quickly as the music had begun, a microcosm was created in which all the capoeiristas were focused on the roda and the music, seeming to share a common essence (ax\u00e9?) with the external world fading away. \u00a0Two capoeiristas entered the roda at the foot of the bateria, crouched, and waited for the berimbau player to let them know when it was time to play a game. \u00a0Then, a call-and-response song started up, led by the berimbau player. \u00a0I forget which song it was exactly, but if I were to guess, it probably would have been&#8230;</p>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p>Luanda \u00e9 meu boi / Luanda \u00e9 para / Tereza canta sentado / Oi Marina samba de p\u00e8 / La no cais da Bahia / Na roda de capoeira / N\u00e3o tem l\u00eal\u00ea n\u00e3o tem nada / Oi, n\u00e3o tem l\u00eal\u00ea nem lala /</p></blockquote>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p>Oi la\u00ea la\u00ea la \u00a0/\u00a0<b><i>Oi l\u00eal\u00ea</i></b></p></blockquote>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p>Oi la\u00ea la\u00ea la\u00a0 /\u00a0<b><i>Oi l\u00eal\u00ea</i></b></p></blockquote>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p>Oi la la\u00ea la la\u00ea la la\u00ea o la\u00ea la</p></blockquote>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p><b>Eeeeee!</b></p></blockquote>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p>Oi la la\u00ea la la\u00ea la la\u00ea o la\u00ea la</p></blockquote>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p>Oi la\u00ea</p></blockquote>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p><b><i>la la\u00ea la</i></b></p></blockquote>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p><b><i></i></b>Oi l\u00eal\u00ea</p>\n<p><b><i>la la\u00ea la</i></b></p></blockquote>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p><b><i></i></b>Oi la\u00ea</p>\n<p><b><i>la la\u00ea la</i></b></p></blockquote>\n<blockquote class=\"tr_bq\"><p><b><i></i></b>Oi l\u00eal\u00ea</p>\n<p><b><i>la la\u00ea la</i></b></p></blockquote>\n<div>\n<p>The regular text would be what the main guy said, and the bold italicized text would be how we all responded. \u00a0While clapping. \u00a0It was difficult to sing a new song and clap at the same time without sounding like a complete idiot (and I&#8217;m sure I sounded like that) or screwing up the rhythm (it still is quite difficult) but I gave it a shot anyway. \u00a0It was my first introduction to the base teaching method of capoeira: I do x, you attempt to follow x until you can actually follow x.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>As we sang and clapped, and tried not to embarrass ourselves, the two players at the foot of the bateria cartwheeled in and began to play (in capoeira we don&#8217;t fight, we play). \u00a0Kicks flew left and right, bodies rose, fell, and rotated, the players swayed from here to there, and all of this was done to the rhythm of the berimbau. \u00a0After each game had gone on for a little while, maybe 45 seconds to a minute, one of the capoeiristas standing on the rim of the roda next to the bateria would crouch down at the foot of the bateria and then take their turn playing the person who had been in the roda the shortest. \u00a0I later learned that this was called &#8220;buying&#8221; the game. \u00a0So, games were bought and people played, songs were sung, and fun was had by all. \u00a0I think that I even played, though I can&#8217;t exactly remember if I had. \u00a0If I did play though, I was most definitely an uncoordinated mess.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>After some time, the class approached its end. \u00a0The roda games ended, the instruments were put to rest, and we once again all gathered on the rim of the roda. \u00a0George said a few more words, let us know that this was a trial class for those who might be interested in capoeira, then ended the class by having us come together and give a big &#8220;Capoeira Guerreiros! \u00a0Salv\u00e9!&#8221; before dispersing. \u00a0Thus was my first introduction to capoeira through the Columbia University branch of the Newark, NJ-based Capoeira Guerreiros, led by a very tall Brazilian man that I came to know as contramestre George Palmares.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>After that first class, everything on my body was pain incarnate. \u00a0My legs, my arms, my ass, my back, my chest, my abs, my shoulders, my neck, my palms, my wrists, my feet; they were all either in pain or too fatigued to be of any real use. \u00a0The bottoms of my feet were torn up and stinging from friction against the hard wood floors. \u00a0My legs were jelly from the ginga and the constant movement. \u00a0My body was little more than a stinging meat bag with limbs. \u00a0Even though by the end of that first class I had been thoroughly exhausted from the workout and embarrassed from having looked like a complete and utter fool, with the next few days finding my body to be akin to a rag doll, after that first day I was hooked.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>I spent the next couple of months training every Tuesday and Thursday night with Guerreiros, learning and refining techniques, songs, mind-body coordination, and the etiquette of the martial art through a combination of direct instruction and my own inquiry. \u00a0I kept trying to get the girl I had originally brought with me to join me, and she did indeed come by a few times. \u00a0However, it wasn&#8217;t for her and I could see that after a few times, and so after awhile I simply stopped putting on that pressure. \u00a0It was an activity that was for me; something that was my own to have and to enjoy. \u00a0I quickly developed the feeling that to treat capoeira like some obligation or some chore that you had to get through during the week was to do a disservice to yourself and to the martial art. \u00a0The people that were in the group that practiced consistently felt similarly, and I soon began to become friendly with some. \u00a0There were a few that had started with me that managed to stay on. \u00a0If memory serves me, their apelidos (capoeira nicknames) were Panda, Coqueiro, and A\u00e7ucena. \u00a0There were also a few that had been there a little while longer that I would train with often; two of whose apelidos were Jesus and Doutor. \u00a0I actually never received an apelido from Guerreiros, as they could never figure out what to call me (though I think by default a few of my instructors settled on what sounded like\u00a0<i>negho,</i>\u00a0spelled &#8220;<i>neg\u00e3o&#8221;,\u00a0</i>portuguese-ish for &#8220;big black guy&#8221; &lt;= the nice way of putting it). \u00a0I eventually got one from another group, but I&#8217;ll get to that later.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<figure id=\"attachment_51\" style=\"width: 300px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><a href=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/omi_george.jpg\"><img class=\"wp-image-51 size-medium\" src=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/omi_george.jpg?resize=300%2C225\" alt=\"omi_george\" srcset=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/omi_george.jpg?resize=300%2C225 300w, http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/omi_george.jpg?resize=135%2C100 135w, http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/omi_george.jpg?w=960 960w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Omi is in the center. George to his left.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>During class we&#8217;d all practice together, two-by-two, and play together in the roda. \u00a0I showed some natural ability with a few techniques (really anything that called for agility or power, like a\u00fa or front hand springs), and through boldness (or stupidity; the jury&#8217;s still out on that one) was able to learn a few advanced sequences and movements from watching and copying some of the older students. \u00a0I&#8217;d be my naturally shy self, preferring to listen and watch far more than speaking and acting, though my classmates and the instructors would slowly get me to open up. \u00a0I remember some classes where we&#8217;d practice headstands on gym mats, and while I could do them pretty well (mom had us doing yoga at a young age) I&#8217;d often feel embarrassed at the oil from my dreads being left behind on the mats. \u00a0Some classes we&#8217;d line up at one end of the room and move forward in rows of 2 doing various movements or little sequences, looking like an army in training. \u00a0During other classes, we&#8217;d set up chairs in the middle of the room and practice kicking over them while facing a partner and a\u00fa-ing (cartwheeling) over to the next chair. \u00a0Our instructors would switch from class to class, I suppose depending on who George could get to teach that day. \u00a0Sometimes it was George, sometimes George and the dude he called his &#8220;brother&#8221;, Omi (it was about a year before I realized that Omi was not his biological brother. \u00a0Yes, I am working toward my doctorate in science. \u00a0Why do you ask?). \u00a0Sometimes it&#8217;d be Papito (who was a task master!) either alone or with others. \u00a0From time to time we&#8217;d even have Sonic (from Senzala) come by with his crazy ass. \u00a0We&#8217;d train and practice and train and practice and sing and play and it was all good and fun.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>While I don&#8217;t remember the exact day that I got my abadas (all-white capoeira clothes), I do remember the happiness and pride that I felt when I received them. \u00a0They gave me a sense of identity with the group; a feeling that I was more than just some dude who practiced with them\u2014I was one of them. \u00a0I especially liked the distinctive yellow band around the hips.</p>\n</div>\n<p class=\"separator\">The first outing that I had gone to with members of Capoeira Guerreiros took place at this bar/restaurant near Columbia called Campo. \u00a0I forget exactly where this occurred in my capoeira timeline, but it was definitely within those first few months before May 2010, as it was sort of a fundraiser for an upcoming event (it might even have taken place the night before the batizado&#8230;hmm&#8230;.). \u00a0So, after class, several of us went to Campo where there was an area in the back that was cleared out for the Capoeira Guerreiros cohort. \u00a0The few of us that were coming from Columbia arrived early, so we kinda just lounged around until the main crew arrived from Jersey. \u00a0It was during this waiting time that I had my first <a href=\"http://media.cocktailia.com/2007/10/caipirinha.jpg\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">caipirinha</a>\u00a0(heaven in a glass. That&#8217;s not a translation. \u00a0It&#8217;s actually heaven in a glass.). \u00a0It was a little awkward because I was still in my shy phase and was more or less afraid to talk to people, so I continued to wait with the people that I did recognize until the Newark crew began to trickle in. \u00a0As they did, we set up the instruments, changed into our capoeira clothes, and the party got started.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\">It was so awesome! \u00a0We took over the whole bar, played some games in the bar, and even had some people show off some acrobatics amongst the dimmed light and loud music. \u00a0I played in my work clothes, and even managed to dance a bit. \u00a0I had invited the girl from earlier to come with me, and she had a pretty good time too. \u00a0All the guys wanted to dance with her, and she got to shake her ass every which way. \u00a0I have to admit I was definitely keeping an eye out because I still wanted to lay some claim, but not too much because I had my own dancing to do. \u00a0I was amazed to see people playing capoeira after drinking <i>several</i>\u00a0drinks, but they did (and didn&#8217;t even throw up! That in itself is amazing!). \u00a0It was a great and fun night for all involved.</p>\n<div>\n<p>The above was a very successful fundraiser for what is known as the capoeira batizado (pronounced &#8220;ba-chi-ZAH-dooh&#8221;; Portuguese for &#8220;baptism&#8221;), which for us would occur in late April. \u00a0The batizado (in my very limited experience) is an event where capoeiristas from all around the world come together for various celebrations, with the main celebration being that of the induction of new members into the world of capoeira via the baptism of the foot. \u00a0When I had first heard about this event, I really didn&#8217;t know what to think. \u00a0There was never really a formal session to introduce me to batizados, so it was a complete mystery to me. \u00a0I just knew that it would be big and that it was important for me to attend if I had hoped to continue practicing capoeira. \u00a0So, I invited a few of my friends, my parents, and my new-old girlfriend (the one I had broken up with before), and went to my first batizado.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>The Spring 2010 Columbia University Capoeira Guerrieros Batizado was held (primarily) inside of the Columbia University Dodge Fitness Center, the big underground gym where we had all of our practices. \u00a0However, instead of being confined to a small room in the back of the gym, we occupied the center floor at the very bottom. \u00a0Looking up, one would see rings on top of rings of levels of the gym, with various people doing various workouts. \u00a0Because the students in attendance at the batizado were comprised not only of the Columbia branch of Guerreiros, but also from other capoeira schools in and around the NY area, as well as other Guerreiros branches along the east coast, there were capoeiristas in every direction. \u00a0As we entered, we changed into our white shirts and our white pants with the yellow band, and were told to get on the floor and warm up. \u00a0Thus it had begun.</p>\n</div>\n<div></div>\n<table class=\"tr-caption-container\" cellspacing=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" align=\"center\">\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-f8G9BvA67Dc/TyDMMdH7JXI/AAAAAAAAAEg/k7GMqVKEd-E/s1600/GEDC0511.JPG\"><img src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-f8G9BvA67Dc/TyDMMdH7JXI/AAAAAAAAAEg/k7GMqVKEd-E/s400/GEDC0511.JPG\" alt=\"\" width=\"400\" height=\"300\" border=\"0\" /></a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td class=\"tr-caption\"><i>A shot of some of the Guerreiros students on the gym floor.<br />\nWe all wore white until they actually gave us blue shirts.</i></td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<div>\n<p>OK, that last bit might be a bit of an embellishment on my part, as I actually arrived a little bit late and missed one of the morning workshops (I&#8217;m not and have never been a morning person). \u00a0You see, the batizado was an all-day event, running from about 8am until (and beyond) 5pm. \u00a0Each hour was packed with a different workshop or other activity. \u00a0Some capoeiristas were brought in to teach advanced movements and sequences, while others gave instruction on dancing and music. \u00a0The workshops ran the gamut of what I knew at the time to represent capoeira, and they ran all day until the main event.</p>\n</div>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-o4GFTjQXEM0/TyDWzWhYn5I/AAAAAAAAAEo/2IYOCk0sWE4/s1600/GEDC0512.JPG\"><img class=\"alignright\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-o4GFTjQXEM0/TyDWzWhYn5I/AAAAAAAAAEo/2IYOCk0sWE4/s320/GEDC0512.JPG\" alt=\"\" width=\"240\" height=\"320\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<div>\n<p>The main event had us form a huge roda, filled with far more people than are seen in the above photograph (many trickled in late; what is it about minorities and punctuality? \u00a0Smh&#8230;). \u00a0Represented (as far as I know) were Guerreiros from Columbia U.,; Newark, NJ; Montclair, NJ; and some senzalites (senzaleiros? senzaliens?) from Mestre Zumbi&#8217;s school in NY; amongst many others who I&#8217;ve never known or met again. \u00a0We all changed into our blue shirts (special for the batizado!), and formed up into the roda. \u00a0The bateria players got their chairs, their instruments, and their different berimbaus (gunga, medio, viola), and waited for it all to begin. \u00a0The first bit was an open roda, meaning that whoever wanted to buy in could buy in and play. \u00a0I got to watch some pretty amazing games (I was blown away at the time) between some very experienced people, including but not limited to Mestre Zumbi and George.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>Once those preliminary festivities were over, the actual induction part of the batizado began. \u00a0This is where each student would be &#8220;tested&#8221; against someone that&#8217;s far more experienced, and after being tested they&#8217;d obtain a new colored rope, called a corda, to wear around their waist. \u00a0The type of cord they were being tested for would determine how many people they&#8217;d be tested against, as well as how they&#8217;d be tested. \u00a0Beginners would have to face only one person, while some of the more advanced capoeiristas would have to go against 3 or 4 (or more) people consecutively. \u00a0The cord system for Guerreiros follows the colors of the Brazilian flag, with light green signifying a fresh-off-the-press beginner. \u00a0It then continues to deep green &gt; deep green + yellow &gt; yellow &gt; yellow + blue &gt; blue &gt; green + yellow + blue &gt;\u00a0green + yellow + blue + white &gt; green + white &gt; yellow + white &gt; blue + white &gt; white (for mestre).</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>The interesting thing about my test was that I wasn&#8217;t aware that I was allowed to attack back. \u00a0I thought it was a &#8220;survive if you can, FOOL!&#8221; situation! \u00a0Therefore, when it was my turn to go up I spent the entire time dodging. \u00a0Esquiva &gt; negativa &gt; rol\u00ea, esquiva &gt; negativa &gt; rol\u00ea, a\u00fa, a\u00fa, duck, dodge, move to the side. \u00a0If you were to hear my thoughts, they probably would have sounded something like: &#8220;Shit! Shit! Shit! Shit! \u00a0What do I do?! Don&#8217;t get hit! \u00a0What do I do?! Don&#8217;t get hit! \u00a0Get out the way! Shit! Shit! Shit!&#8221; \u00a0At some point, for whatever reason, I decided to go in for a head-butt (cabe\u00e7ada), only to meet my opponent&#8217;s elbow. \u00a0He then prepared to drop me, but showed mercy and ended the game. \u00a0You can see it all below [<i>video dead for some reason</i>].</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>Once I had finished embarrassing myself, flailing about, and getting my ass kicked all over the roda, I was awarded a light-green cord and officially recognized as a student of Capoeira Guerreiros. \u00a0Following my test, other students from my cohort went for their cords. \u00a0Then some of the advanced students had their multiple-opponent tests. \u00a0All of that had been completed, the roda began to get far more lively.\u00a0 Instead of the traditional system of a single game per roda, the super-roda housed 3 simultaneous games! \u00a0It was quite the spectacle.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>It was interesting trying to play in the roda with two other games going on. \u00a0Not only did I have to focus on my own game, but it was necessary to be mindful of the other two games around me as well. \u00a0 While I&#8217;m trying to go for a compasso, someone else might just be landing from a parafuso, and a third person might be tumbling backwards from eating a ben\u00e7ao. \u00a0It was crazy!</p>\n<p>All of the excitement could only last but for so long, as we did have to eventually disperse. \u00a0Before leaving, all of the students and the instructors, including the guests, gathered together for a group shot. \u00a0There sure was a hell of a lot of us.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-ukca8ukubYc/TyOV9u7DfoI/AAAAAAAAAE4/iT0JfqRTsvs/s1600/IMG00023-20100502-1529.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-ukca8ukubYc/TyOV9u7DfoI/AAAAAAAAAE4/iT0JfqRTsvs/s400/IMG00023-20100502-1529.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"400\" height=\"300\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>This ended the officially official indoor batizado event, not that it put a halt to the festivities in any way, shape, or form. \u00a0This is, after all, a martial art that&#8217;s founded in Brazilian culture, and Brazilians apparently like to party. \u00a0After cleaning up the area and hauling furniture and food back to their rightful places, the capoeiristas migrated outdoors. \u00a0It was still a sunny day, and there was still much capoeira to be had. \u00a0Once outside, they found a decently-sized spot to play, threw off their shirts, picked up their instruments, and started flying high and fast on the Columbia grass, attracting the attention of any and everyone that had happened to be passing by. \u00a0I watched, and even played a game or two. \u00a0I didn&#8217;t try to jump in too much though, because they were into doing acrobatic stunts, and the best that I could do is a one-handed front handspring. \u00a0Still, it was amazing to watch people twist and fly through the air in sync, and throw kicks left and right at lightning speed.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>After some time, I left. \u00a0It had been a long day, and I was physically and emotionally wiped. \u00a0But, in all of my fatigue and my embarrassment, I had succeeded in becoming something that had quickly come to mean a lot to my life. \u00a0With my brand, spankin&#8217; new light green cord around my waist and the day behind me, I had added to my character.</p>\n</div>\n<div>\n<p>I had become a capoeirista.</p>\n</div>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-18T01:20:44", "date_gmt": "2012-01-25T05:27:46", "_links": [25, 26, 22], "guid": {"rendered": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/?p=43"}, "id": 43, "title": {"rendered": "Life is Art"}, "comment_status": "open", "author": 1, "modified_gmt": "2015-09-18T01:20:31", "meta": [], "sticky": false, "slug": "life-is-art", "template": "", "ping_status": "open"}, {"featured_media": 38, "format": "standard", "type": "post", "link": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/science-sunday-the-stars-part-i-introduction-to-shiny-things/", "date": "2012-01-22T05:15:47", "content": {"protected": false, "rendered": "<p>I&#8217;ve thought a lot about this, and I&#8217;ve decided\u2014really for my own benefit\u2014that I should spend some time once per week thinking and writing about a science topic that interests me. \u00a0I figured that it&#8217;d be good to just choose something and go somewhat in-depth about it. \u00a0In the future, should I continue, I won&#8217;t always choose something astronomical, though anything outside of what I&#8217;ve been fortunate enough to learn will take extensive use of Wikipedia (and maybe even *gasp* a book!). \u00a0However, to start, I think that I should talk about something(s) that has interested me since the first time that I actually cared about astronomy: Stars.</p>\n<p><!--more--></p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_38\" style=\"width: 250px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><a href=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/the_sun_1.jpg\"><img class=\"wp-image-38 size-full\" src=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/the_sun_1.jpg?resize=250%2C250\" alt=\"the_sun_1\" srcset=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/the_sun_1.jpg?w=250 250w, http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/the_sun_1.jpg?resize=150%2C150 150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 250px) 100vw, 250px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">The Sun \u2014 our closest star</figcaption></figure>\n<p>There is so very much to say about stars that it&#8217;s really difficult to know quite where to start, and my level of exposure to them it&#8217;s also quite difficult to know how to proceed without getting too technical. \u00a0Let&#8217;s start with this: stars are the massive balls of gas in the Universe that shine brightly and live dynamically by way of a constant balance against the inward force of gravity with the outward force of radiative pressure from nuclear fusion. \u00a0Wow, that is definitely a packed sentence. \u00a0Let&#8217;s take it back to basics and build up some understanding so that we can come back and actually appreciate what all of that meant.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_39\" style=\"width: 185px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><a href=\"http://i1.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/gravity.gif\"><img class=\"size-full wp-image-39\" src=\"http://i1.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/gravity.gif?resize=185%2C200\" alt=\"Nevermind all the lines, the apple is falling on this dude's head due to gravity!\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Nevermind all the lines, the apple is falling on this dude&#8217;s head due to gravity!</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Gravity always acts radially. \u00a0So, if you have a box full of particles that experience no other force aside from gravity, they will eventually collapse into a sphere (or sphere-like object, depending on what that initial distribution is). \u00a0Gravity doesn&#8217;t make boxes or pyramids, nor does it build buildings or cars. \u00a0It just pulls things 1 and 2 together. \u00a0Gravity is love! \u00a0I digress&#8230;Gravity, as we all know so very well, is responsible for making things on the Earth that go up come back down. \u00a0It&#8217;s also what keeps us tethered to the Earth&#8217;s surface, what keeps the Moon orbiting the Earth, and what keeps the Earth orbiting the Sun. \u00a0The law of gravity, in essence, states that any two physically-existing objects with some mass (call them <i>M1 </i>and <i>M2</i>) that are separated in space by some distance, <i>d</i>, will experience a force that will always act to pull them toward one another. \u00a0This force\u2014this affinity for action\u2014will weaken fairly quickly as the distance grows between these two objects (if the distance doubles, the force between the two objects will reduce to 1/4th of its former strength). However, no matter how far apart they may be, the force will always be there.</p>\n<p>The gas that makes up the physical objects that we know of as stars acts much like that hypothetical box of particles that I mentioned before. \u00a0However, where one might imagine that box of particles with the length of a side comparable to our own size, stars themselves (like our own Sun) are balls of gas that span sizes that are almost beyond our comprehension! \u00a0And this is AFTER the gas has already collapsed from a far-larger reservoir, called a Giant Molecular Cloud (which I may get to in the future). \u00a0Though this may prove to not actually help very much for visualizing this scale, for a sense of scale regarding the size of the Sun (our nearest star), the United States is roughly 2,500 miles wide from east to west. \u00a0According to <a href=\"http://maps.google.com/\" data-blogger-escaped-target=\"_blank\">Google Maps</a>, driving from Sacramento, CA to Washington, D.C. covers 2,731 miles and would take&#8230;1.83 days?! \u00a0An average speed of ~62 mph? \u00a0That seems&#8230;a little ambitious&#8230;I&#8217;m digressing again. \u00a0Anyway, in contrast, the average diameter of the Sun is *very roughly* 865,000 (really ~864,950) miles! That amounts to 346 cross-country road trips (or close to 2 years of constant driving) in order to travel from one end of the Sun to the other, going through the center. \u00a0Its circumference on the other hand is *again very roughly* 2.7 million miles. \u00a0It&#8217;s crazy huge.</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_40\" style=\"width: 200px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><a href=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/hydrogen-atom.jpg\"><img class=\"size-full wp-image-40\" src=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/hydrogen-atom.jpg?resize=200%2C200\" alt=\"A very artistic and barely-accurate rendering of a hydrogen atom\" srcset=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/hydrogen-atom.jpg?w=200 200w, http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/hydrogen-atom.jpg?resize=150%2C150 150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 200px) 100vw, 200px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">A very artistic and barely-accurate<br />rendering of a hydrogen atom</figcaption></figure>\n<p>So, what do we have so far? \u00a0Star&#8217;s are physically large, physically massive, and are made of gas that is gravitationally bound to itself. \u00a0Awesome, we have progress. \u00a0However, out of these facts come an interesting question: with all of this mass experiencing all of this gravitational force pulling everything inward, how is it that all of this material doesn&#8217;t just collapse indefinitely until it becomes just an extremely massive point in space? \u00a0An initial guess might be that the atoms that comprise this gas act like solid billiard balls, where the gas ensemble will compact down in volume until each atomic &#8220;sphere&#8221; is physically touching the next one. \u00a0Let&#8217;s do a quick and dirty calculation of what that might be like (Christ, there will be so many approximations&#8230;.).Packed within this gargantuan volume is enough gas to equate to ~333,000 Earth masses. \u00a0The stuff that comprises this gas isn&#8217;t what we usually think of when we think of gas (certainly not what&#8217;s in your car). \u00a0It is almost entirely a gas of hydrogen atoms (~75% hydrogen and ~25% helium\u00a0by mass,\u00a0but they exist in an almost 12:1 ratio by number in our own Sun; the ratio may be even higher when you account for the mass fraction of heavier elements), which themselves are extreeeeemely tiny (using the Bohr radius of the hydrogen atom, you can fit ~700,000 hydrogen atoms along the width of a single hair), and are extreeeeemely light (I could give a sense-of-scale factoid here, but I don&#8217;t feel like it). \u00a0Hydrogen is honestly worthy of its own article, but that&#8217;s for another time. \u00a0What I will say about basic hydrogen (there are isotopes, as well as ionization states), that hasn&#8217;t already been said within parentheses, is that it is the most basic atom in existence, with each atom being composed of a single proton orbited by a single electron (though the force that keeps the electron tethered is <b><i>not</i></b> gravity!). \u00a0This will become useful later.</p>\n<p>Let&#8217;s first approximate the Sun as a hypothetical star being entirely comprised of hydrogen atoms. \u00a0This comes out to roughly ~10^57 atoms (this symbol &#8220;^&#8221; means &#8220;the numbers following this are the exponent of the preceding number&#8221;) if you divide the mass of the Sun by the mass of an individual hydrogen atom. \u00a0Each of these atoms has a radius of roughly 5.3 x 10^(-11) meters, resulting in a volume for every atom of ~6.2 x 10^(-31) cubic meters. \u00a0I&#8217;m going to do something really stupid and highly incorrect and invert this, giving a number density (# of atoms per unit volume) of one atom per 6.2&#215;10^(-31) cubic meters, or 1.6 x 10^30 atoms per cubic meter of space. \u00a0Given that we have ~10^57 atoms in this hypothetical pure hydrogen star, we divide the total number of atoms by the number density of atoms, giving ~6 x 10^26 cubic meters for the volume of our pure-hydrogen star. \u00a0Now, if you look up the radius of the Sun and do the volume calculation, you get something like 1.4 x 10^27 cubic meters for the Sun&#8217;s volume. \u00a0Then, you can look at the two numbers side by side and say, considering all the approximations we made along the way, that this could possibly work.</p>\n<p>HOWEVER, remember that the Sun is not purely hydrogen, and instead has roughly 1 helium atom per 12 hydrogen atoms, with the size of an individual helium atom being roughly 60% of a hydrogen atom. \u00a0Thus if we were to make our hypothetical star a little more realistic and include helium, as well as some of the heavier elements present in the Sun like oxygen, nitrogen, carbon, neon, and even iron, our hypothetical star with atoms bumping up against one another like billiard balls begins to shrink drastically in size, and the volume may decrease by an order of magnitude (meaning a factor of 10, and no I do not have a calculation for that.). \u00a0But, the Sun is puffed up to a much greater volume than that. \u00a0On top of that, the Sun also shines, which an inert ball of hydrogen billiard balls cannot do. \u00a0What gives? \u00a0What is it that&#8217;s holding the Sun up against that ever-present collapse of gravity? \u00a0The answer: <b>radiative pressure</b>.</p>\n<p class=\"separator\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-zp55oIKRml4/UGYiu_OLXrI/AAAAAAAAAIM/WJmOXE5Y-Ac/s1600/incandescent-light-bulbs-lg.jpg\"><img class=\"alignleft\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-zp55oIKRml4/UGYiu_OLXrI/AAAAAAAAAIM/WJmOXE5Y-Ac/s200/incandescent-light-bulbs-lg.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"200\" height=\"156\" border=\"0\" /></a></p>\n<p>Radiative pressure is a fancy way of saying the force produced on a surface by\u00a0<i>light</i>, that same phenomenon that makes it so that we can see the world around us. \u00a0You might be thinking to yourself, aside from my argument above being&#8230;fairly weak, &#8220;self, what the hell is he talking about? \u00a0You need something that has the ability to PUSH in order to hold against gravity! \u00a0Light doesn&#8217;t push anything, it just shines!&#8221; \u00a0Well, mon fr\u00e8re, that is where you&#8217;re wrong. \u00a0Light (another topic to discuss at great and painful length! Woo!) is energy, and has the ability to imbue particles with motion when it interacts with matter (in many different ways that will be detailed later). \u00a0This motion can then translate into a pressure, as these newly-energized particles smack up against other particles and physically push them outward. \u00a0But how, pray tell, does this light get produced? \u00a0What is the source at the center of it all?</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_41\" style=\"width: 236px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><a href=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/fusion-de-hidrogeno.jpg\"><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-41\" src=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/fusion-de-hidrogeno.jpg?resize=236%2C300\" alt=\"The proton-proton chain of nuclear fusion\" srcset=\"http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/fusion-de-hidrogeno.jpg?resize=236%2C300 236w, http://i0.wp.com/rationalwhimsy.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/fusion-de-hidrogeno.jpg?w=289 289w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 236px) 100vw, 236px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">The proton-proton chain of nuclear fusion</figcaption></figure>\n<p>So now what do we have? \u00a0We&#8217;ve discussed that stars are giant balls of gas. \u00a0We&#8217;ve covered that these giant balls of gas are bound together by gravity, but are held up against collapse by radiative pressure. \u00a0We&#8217;ve also covered that this radiative pressure is due to nuclear fusion occurring in their cores. \u00a0And so, stars live dynamically, balancing radiative pressure against gravity! \u00a0It&#8217;s dynamic because there&#8217;s constant action in this stand-off. \u00a0If the radiative pressure relents just a bit, gravity acts right away to contract the star. \u00a0If gravity contracts the star just a bit, the core will heat up from this contraction, and the radiative output will increase, puffing the star back up. \u00a0Now that I&#8217;ve gotten through all that, where do we go from here? \u00a0There&#8217;s just so much to cover. \u00a0I think that next time, I&#8217;ll start talking about all of the different types of stars and their physical and observational properties, moving up through their evolution, and going over how different stars die. \u00a0I&#8217;d like to go into detail about every stellar population, just so that we (read: I) have a good idea of what makes each population special. \u00a0I&#8217;d then like to go into how they&#8217;re distributed throughout the galaxy, whether they&#8217;re in clusters or are cruising along in the galactic field, and how their locations and compositions tell us more about the galaxy that we live in. \u00a0After that, I think it might be a good time to cut the star stuff, because there&#8217;s so much more of the natural world to explore, and I&#8217;m interested to see what I can dig up.<i>FUUUUUUUUUSION!!!</i>\u00a0 Hydrogen in the core of the Sun is packed together really tightly, and is fairly heavily ionized, meaning that the central proton has been stripped of its electron companion. \u00a0It&#8217;s also really hot (~27 million degrees Fahrenheit, vs ~10,300\u00b0 F on the Sun&#8217;s surface, and ~1,800\u00b0 F for magma on Earth), and heat makes things want to move, so these free protons in high densities jet around really really quickly. \u00a0Now, for visualization, try to imagine yourself in any given mall on Black Friday. \u00a0It&#8217;s extremely crowded, and everyone within the mall is trying to move as quickly as they can in order to get to a sale. \u00a0Inevitably these people will collide, sometimes even with you. \u00a0Let&#8217;s take this analogy back to the Sun, where we instead have protons colliding at very high energies. \u00a0When people in the mall collide when they&#8217;re under high pressure, in high density, and are really hot, they tend to explode into a fight. \u00a0When protons collide under these conditions, they fuse into a single nucleus of one proton and one neutron called deuterium, which one can think of as heavy hydrogen. \u00a0The reaction also produces a positron (the antimatter form of an electron), a neutrino (a mysterious little particle that seems to only interact with matter when it feels like it), and a little energy that is given off in the form of light. \u00a0The positron eventually goes on to meet up with a free electron, annihilate, and produce some energy. \u00a0The next leg of fusion, the major energy-releasing part, occurs when another free proton smacks into the deuterium atom, creating helium-3 (called as such because there&#8217;s 3 particles comprising it&#8217;s nucleus: 2 protons and 1 neutron), and releasing energy in the form of light. \u00a0This is all amazing and whatnot, but it is important to note that the time scale for a single proton-proton fusion interaction is on the order of one billion years per reaction. \u00a0This would be an incredibly long wait if not for the fact that there are far more than billions of protons in the Sun&#8217;s core. \u00a0The sheer vastness in the number of protons in this region means that even though the time scale is so long, every second there are roughly 3.6 x 10^38 protons going through the reaction and being converted into helium nuclei. \u00a0This, according to Wikipedia, releases energy at a rate of ~9.1 x 10^10 megatons of TNT per second! \u00a0PER SECOND! \u00a0That&#8217;s about the power in 9 billion nuclear bombs of the highest yield, PER SECOND. \u00a0Crazy. \u00a0Stars are objects that are at constant nuclear war, with themselves, in order to stay alive. \u00a0That&#8217;s some serious personal issues.</p>\n<p>At\u00e9 ent\u00e3o!</p>\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n<p>*<i>Physical quantities like the mass of hydrogen and diameter of the Sun were obtained from the textbook that I used to TA for Astronomy 101 last quarter, whatever that is. \u00a0I don&#8217;t feel like looking for it. \u00a0It&#8217;s got stars on the front. \u00a0Unit conversions from km to miles, as well as all calculations were done by me using anything from IDL to my Macbook&#8217;s Spotlight calculator to my iPhone, and may be a little (or a lot) off due to rounding errors and general laziness. \u00a0This is certainly not an ultimately-reliable source for facts and figures, just an astronomer rambling about stuff that gets him excited. \u00a0Enjoy for your own pleasure, but cite at your own peril!</i></p>\n"}, "modified": "2015-09-18T01:20:18", "date_gmt": "2012-01-22T05:15:47", "_links": {"wp:term": [{"href": "http://rationalwhimsy.com/wp-json/wp/v2/categories?post=37",
